source packets.

Proof.  This is Lemma 10.17d restated as an ARC-C0 clause.  The packet
constants are finite for each packet, and the rational finite packets are
countable.  A standard diagonal subnet preserves cofinality and makes every
finite-packet anisotropy response vanish.

$$
\square
$$

##### Theorem 10.26: ARC-C0 From CL1a

Assume CL1a: the cutoff theory admits a controlled asymptotically free local
operator chart for the bounded positive-flow source packet.  Then ARC-C0
holds.

Proof.  Lemma 10.21 proves ARC1.  Lemma 10.22 proves ARC2.  Lemma 10.24
proves ARC3 from the positive-flow Symanzik anisotropy bound supplied by the
CL1a chart.  Lemma 10.25 proves ARC4.  Hence all clauses of ARC-C0 hold.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.27: CL1a Closes Euclidean Restoration

Assume CL1a.  Then:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1a}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{ARC-C0}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{FWS3}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL1d}.
}
$$

Proof.  CL1a implies ARC-C0 by Theorem 10.26.  ARC-C0 implies FWS3 by Theorem
10.17.  FWS3 implies CL1d by Corollary 10.18.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.10 CL1a: Flowed Source-Response RG Chart

Searchable CL1a tag:

`V4P39-C0-CL1A-FLOWED-SOURCE-RG-CHART`.

CL1a is the coordinate-chart gate.  It does not prove that all irrelevant
directions contract.  It proves that, for every finite positive-flow source
packet and fixed response order, there is a controlled local operator chart:
the relevant and marginal coordinates are finite, the pure Yang-Mills
coupling is the only untuned bulk marginal coordinate, and all other local
directions are typed or irrelevant.

This is the finite-print version of asymptotic freedom.  A continuum route is
not specified by a mystical bare lattice field.  It is specified by finite
flowed source responses at a positive physical flow scale.

##### Definition 10.28: The Flowed RG Coordinate Packet

Fix a finite packet:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal P}_m
\subset
{\mathcal F}_{flow,\tau}.
}
$$

Fix a finite response order:

$$
\boxed{
r_m<\infty.
}
$$

The flowed RG coordinate packet is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_m
=
\{
\hbox{all local gauge-invariant source derivatives of elements of }
{\mathcal P}_m
\hbox{ through response order }
r_m
\}.
}
$$

The chart is required to express every response in:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_m
}
$$

using a finite local operator basis:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_m
=
{\mathcal O}_{rel,m}
\cup
{\mathcal O}_{marg,m}
\cup
{\mathcal O}_{irr,m}.
}
$$

##### Definition 10.28a: Finite-Packet RG Banach Space

For the packet:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal P}_m
}
$$

define the finite response-coordinate Banach space:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak B}_m
=
{\mathfrak B}_{rel,m}
\oplus
{\mathfrak B}_{marg,m}
\oplus
{\mathfrak B}_{irr,m}
\oplus
{\mathfrak B}_{typed,m}.
}
$$

Its elements are:

$$
\boxed{
x_m
=
(u_m,g_m,h_m,s_m).
}
$$

The norm is the weighted response norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|x_m\|_m
=
\|u_m\|_{rel,m}
+
|g_m|
+
\sum_{\alpha\in I_m}
w_{m,\alpha}|h_{m,\alpha}|
+
\|s_m\|_{typed,m}.
}
$$

The irrelevant weights are chosen by scaling degree:

$$
\boxed{
w_{m,\alpha}
=
b^{\Delta_{m,\alpha}},
\qquad
\Delta_{m,\alpha}>0.
}
$$

The physical chart ball is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak U}_m(\rho)
=
\{x_m:\|x_m\|_m<\rho\}.
}
$$

##### Definition 10.28b: Finite-Step RG Map By Response Matching

Fix a block factor:

$$
\boxed{
b>1.
}
$$

The finite-packet RG map:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{m,b}
:
{\mathfrak U}_m(\rho)
\longrightarrow
{\mathfrak B}_m
}
$$

is defined by one shell integration followed by response matching:

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{x_m,a}
\left(F\right)
=
\omega_{{\mathcal R}_{m,b}x_m,ba}
\left(F\right)
+
\mathrm{Err}_{m,b,a}(F),
\qquad
F\in{\mathcal P}_m.
}
$$

The error obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{F\in{\mathcal P}_m}
|\mathrm{Err}_{m,b,a}(F)|
\le
C_m a^{\eta_m}.
}
$$

The same definition applies to source derivatives through response order:

$$
\boxed{
r_m.
}
$$

##### Lemma 10.28c: RG Map Is Analytic On The Finite Packet Ball

For sufficiently small:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_m>0,
}
$$

the map:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{m,b}
}
$$

is analytic on:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak U}_m(\rho_m).
}
$$

Its Taylor expansion has the block form:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
u_m'&={\mathsf A}_{rel,m}u_m+{\mathsf N}_{rel,m}(u_m,g_m,h_m,s_m),\\
g_m'&=g_m-b_0(\log b)g_m^3+{\mathsf N}_{g,m}(g_m,h_m,s_m),\\
h_m'&={\mathsf A}_{irr,m}h_m+{\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g_m,h_m,s_m),\\
s_m'&={\mathsf A}_{typed,m}s_m.
\end{aligned}
}
$$

Proof.  At finite packet and finite response order the shell integration is a
finite-dimensional analytic operation on compact link variables with a
strictly positive heat-kernel density.  Source derivatives through the fixed
order commute with the finite shell integration.  Response matching is a
finite analytic coordinate inversion near the Gaussian ultraviolet point
because the finite response Jacobian on the chosen operator basis is
nondegenerate after Ward descendants and typed redundancies are quotient out.
The remainder from replacing the exact shell by the packet response chart is
the displayed local truncation error.  Hence the finite-packet RG map is
analytic on a sufficiently small chart ball.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.28d: Explicit RG Bounds And Contraction Constants

There are finite constants:

$$
\boxed{
C_m<\infty,
\qquad
q_m<1,
\qquad
\rho_m>0,
}
$$

such that, on:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak U}_m(\rho_m),
}
$$

the irrelevant block obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf A}_{irr,m}\|_m
\le
q_m.
}
$$

The nonlinear terms obey:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,h,s)\|_m
\le
C_m g^2\|h\|_m
+
C_m\|h\|_m^2
+
C_m a^{\eta_m}.
}
$$

The marginal coordinate obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
g'
-
g
+
b_0(\log b)g^3
\right|
\le
C_m g^5
+
C_m\|h\|_m^2
+
C_m a^{\eta_m}.
}
$$

The relevant block is finite dimensional and is fixed by the normalization and
anisotropy conditions:

$$
\boxed{
u_m'=0.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.29 gives a finite local operator basis, so all operator norms
in the packet chart are equivalent.  Operators in the irrelevant block have
strict positive excess degree.  With the weights of Definition 10.28a, the
linear irrelevant block gains at least a factor:

$$
\boxed{
b^{-\Delta_m}.
}
$$

Choose the block factor and radius so that:

$$
\boxed{
b^{-\Delta_m}
+
C_m\rho_m^2
\le
q_m<1.
}
$$

Lemma 10.31 gives triangularity, so irrelevant coordinates do not linearly
regenerate relevant or marginal coordinates after the typed and Ward quotient.
The pure Yang-Mills beta coefficient gives the displayed marginal estimate.
The finite packet and positive flow bound the nonlinear Taylor coefficients,
and the shell truncation gives the cutoff error.  The relevant coordinates are
not free coordinates of the continuum trajectory; they are fixed by the
predeclared finite normalization and anisotropy equations.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.28e: Finite-Packet Stable Trajectory

For every finite packet and every sufficiently small renormalized coupling:

$$
\boxed{
g_R>0,
}
$$

there is a unique local trajectory:

$$
\boxed{
x_{m,n}
=
(u_{m,n},g_{m,n},h_{m,n},s_m)
}
$$

defined for all large ultraviolet depths:

$$
\boxed{
n\ge n_m,
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{m,b}^{\,n-n_m}x_{m,n}
\longrightarrow
(0,g_R,0,s_m)
}
$$

in the packet response norm, and:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{n\ge n_m}
\|h_{m,n}\|_m
\le
C_m g_{m,n}^2.
}
$$

Proof.  Use Lemma 10.28d.  The relevant coordinates are solved by the finite
normalization and anisotropy equations.  The marginal coordinate is the
asymptotically free one-dimensional running coupling.  The irrelevant
coordinates are solved by the contraction mapping:

$$
\boxed{
h
\mapsto
{\mathsf A}_{irr,m}h
+
{\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,h,s).
}
$$

On the ball:

$$
\boxed{
\|h\|_m\le K_m g^2,
}
$$

Lemma 10.28d makes this map a strict contraction for sufficiently small
coupling.  Banach's fixed-point theorem gives the local stable graph:

$$
\boxed{
h=H_m(g,s).
}
$$

Iterating the marginal equation backward toward the ultraviolet gives:

$$
\boxed{
g_{m,n}^{2}
\sim
\frac{1}{2b_0 n\log b}.
}
$$

The stable graph then gives the stated cofinal trajectory.

$$
\square
$$

##### Theorem 10.28f: Constructive Finite-Packet RG Trajectory

For every finite positive-flow source packet and response order, the RG map:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{m,b}
}
$$

has a cofinal asymptotically free trajectory in the Banach response norm.  The
trajectory has:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{one\ untyped\ marginal\ coupling},
\qquad
\mathrm{finite\ tuned\ relevant\ block},
\qquad
\mathrm{contracting\ irrelevant\ block}.
}
$$

Moreover the finite packet responses converge along that trajectory:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{n\to\infty}
\omega_{x_{m,n},a_n}(F)
\quad
\hbox{exists for every }
F\in{\mathcal P}_m.
}
$$

Proof.  Definition 10.28a gives the Banach space and norm.  Definition 10.28b
constructs the finite-step RG map by shell integration and response matching.
Lemma 10.28c proves analyticity of the map.  Lemma 10.28d gives explicit
finite constants, the marginal beta estimate, and the strict irrelevant
contraction.  Lemma 10.28e constructs the stable cofinal trajectory.  The
response-matching error is summable along the cofinal route because it is
bounded by a positive cutoff power.  Therefore every finite packet response
has a continuum limit on the constructed trajectory.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.28g: Initial Open Core Of The Constructive RG Trajectory

Searchable open-core tag:

`V4P39-C0-CL1-OPEN-CORE-HONEST-STATUS`.

This subsection first states plainly what Theorem 10.28f does and does not
establish, so that no later citation overstates it.  The subsequent executions in
10.28g2 through 10.28g6 then attempt to close the ultraviolet positive-flow
versions of the listed clauses by finite heat-kernel receipts.

What is established.  For each fixed finite source packet ${\mathcal P}_m$ and
finite response order $r_m$, on the small chart ball ${\mathfrak U}_m(\rho_m)$
and at fixed positive flow time $\tau>0$, the finite-step response map
${\mathcal R}_{m,b}$ is analytic, carries the displayed one-loop marginal beta
coefficient, and is a strict contraction on the irrelevant block for
sufficiently small coupling.  Banach's theorem then gives a stable small-field
trajectory for that packet.  This is a genuine but local statement.

What is not established by Theorem 10.28f alone.  Five clauses are used
downstream but are not proved at the strength a continuum construction requires
until the execution subsections below:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|l}
\hbox{clause} & \hbox{what is missing}\\
\hline
\mathrm{U} & \hbox{uniform-in-}m\hbox{ bounds: }C_m,q_m,\rho_m,\eta_m\hbox{ are
not controlled as the packet grows}\\
\mathrm{LF} & \hbox{large-field regions outside }{\mathfrak U}_m(\rho_m)\hbox{ are
not bounded nonperturbatively}\\
\mathrm{ER} & \hbox{the response-matching error }C_m a^{\eta_m}\hbox{ is asserted
summable, not derived}\\
\mathrm{ZF} & \hbox{the zero-flow }\tau\downarrow0\hbox{ limit still needs a
small-flow counterterm receipt at this stage}\\
\mathrm{NT} & \hbox{nontriviality: the continuum normalization lower bound
}\liminf_a{\mathsf N}_{a,L}\ge n_->0\hbox{ still needs a positive scale readout}
\end{array}
}
$$

Why these are not removable by the present method.  The chart of Lemma 10.28c
is defined on a small ball at small coupling, so it has no access to the
large-field configurations LF that a continuum gauge construction must control;
the contraction of Lemma 10.28d is therefore a small-field, perturbative
statement near the ultraviolet Gaussian point and says nothing about the
strong-coupling infrared.  The operator basis ${\mathcal O}_m$ of Lemma 10.29
grows with the packet, and no equiboundedness of the Taylor coefficients or of
the inverse response Jacobian is proved across packets, so U is not available.
The diagonal passages of Lemmas 10.17d and 10.25 assign each packet its own
tolerance and therefore produce a limit with no uniform modulus; this is a
packetwise limit, not a continuum field theory with uniform local bounds.  ER
is exactly the central nonperturbative estimate of four-dimensional constructive
gauge theory and is not supplied by the packetwise chart alone.  ZF is deferred
to the small-flow counterterm execution of Theorem 10.28g4.6 rather than treated
as automatic membership in the small-flow quotient.  NT is the continuum
nontriviality lower bound: Lemma 10.7c proves strict positivity of the
normalization at each fixed cutoff but does not by itself prevent continuum
collapse; Theorem 10.28g5.5 supplies the separate flowed energy readout used
below.

Relation to the established literature.  A complete proof of U and LF that
maintains lattice gauge invariance through the continuum limit is the content of
the Bałaban-type ultraviolet renormalization-group program, which has not been
carried through to a full construction satisfying the Osterwalder-Schrader
axioms.  Two-dimensional Yang-Mills is constructed; three-dimensional Yang-Mills
has substantial recent progress on the measure and state space through
stochastic quantization and regularity structures; the four-dimensional
construction is open, and a positive mass gap is open for every nonabelian gauge
theory in four dimensions.  Theorem 10.28f should be read as a small-field,
fixed-flow, packetwise chart consistent with that frontier.  The manuscript's
stronger claim begins only when the finite receipts in Executions I through V
are added.

Relation to the Bałaban/Magnen-Rivasseau-Séneor ultraviolet frontier.  The
positive-flow receipt program below lives in the same weak-coupling ultraviolet
regime as the established constructive work.  Bałaban's four-dimensional lattice
renormalization-group papers control the small-field/large-field decomposition,
effective actions, cluster expansions, and large-field renormalization along an
asymptotically free ultraviolet corridor.  Magnen, Rivasseau, and Séneor remove
the ultraviolet cutoff for four-dimensional pure SU(2) Yang-Mills with a fixed
infrared cutoff.  These results are substantial ultraviolet control, not a
solution of the fixed-scale infrared mass-gap problem.  Therefore g1-g6 below
should be read as a gradient-flow and packet-language reconstruction of
Bałaban-regime ultraviolet receipts unless and until the fixed-scale bridge of
subsection 10.28k is proved.  In particular, a perturbative positive-flow
readout is not by itself a non-Gaussian infrared nontriviality theorem.

##### 10.28g1: Rigorous Open-Core Closure Program

Searchable open-core program tag:

`V4P39-C0-OPEN-CORE-EINSTEIN-FEYNMAN-PROGRAM`.

This subsection turns the C0 core of subsection 10.28g into precise theorem
targets.  It is not counted by itself as a proof of four-dimensional continuum
Yang-Mills.  It is a UV proof program: once the estimates below are supplied
from the regulated heat-kernel or Wilson lattice measures, the ultraviolet
positive-flow versions of U, LF, ER, ZF, and NT close without adding
ontology-dependent assumptions.  The fixed-scale infrared bridge is a separate
target in subsection 10.28k.

Einstein discipline.  The continuum object must be independent of the finite
packet used to interrogate it, must not hide noncovariance in the cutoff, and
must not define away missing observables by choosing a convenient record
completion.  Therefore the proof must be stated as an invariant local-net
construction with packet-independent constants, Euclidean covariance in the
limit, and a zero-flow algebra obtained as a theorem rather than as a
definition.

Feynman discipline.  Every open clause must leave a finite receipt.  The
receipts are packet-comparison constants, large-field polymer activities,
summable scale errors, small-flow counterterm remainders, and a nonzero
renormalized physical readout.  If any receipt cannot be printed, the clause is
not proved.

Definition 10.28g1.1: cofinal flowed packet tower.  A cofinal flowed packet
tower consists of:

$$
\boxed{
({\mathcal P}_m,\tau_n,a_n,L_n,{\mathcal N}_{m,k,n})_{m,n,k}
}
$$

Here ${\mathcal P}_m$ is an increasing family of finite gauge-invariant local
source packets, $a_n$ is a decreasing lattice spacing, $L_n$ is an increasing
volume, and $\tau_n$ is a positive flow time satisfying:

$$
\boxed{
a_n^2\ll \tau_n \downarrow 0.
}
$$

The norm ${\mathcal N}_{m,k,n}$ is the finite-energy OS matrix-element norm on
the algebra generated by the packet ${\mathcal P}_m$ at Sobolev order $k$ and
flow time $\tau_n$:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_{m,k,n}(A)
=
\sup_{\Psi,\Phi\in{\mathcal D}_{m,k,n}}
\frac{|\langle \Psi,A\Phi\rangle_{OS,a_n,L_n,\tau_n}|}
{\|\Psi\|_{OS,a_n,L_n}\|\Phi\|_{OS,a_n,L_n}}.
}
$$

The domains ${\mathcal D}_{m,k,n}$ are generated by finitely many
gauge-invariant flowed Wilson/source insertions with bounded support, bounded
representation Casimir, bounded derivative order, and bounded finite-energy
transfer cost.  Cofinality means that the support radius, Casimir cutoff,
derivative order, and finite-energy cutoff tend to infinity with $m$ and $k$.

Uniformity convention.  A constant is acceptable for C0 only if it may depend
on the gauge group, a physical support radius, a Sobolev order, and a source
radius, but not on the packet index once those physical bounds are fixed, not
on the cutoff, and not on the volume after the support is separated from the
boundary.

###### Master Theorem M1: Uniform Flowed RG Chart

Searchable M1 tag:

`V4P39-C0-M1-UNIFORM-FLOWED-RG-CHART`.

For every fixed physical support radius, Sobolev order, and source radius,
there exist Banach spaces of gauge-invariant flowed local coordinates:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak B}_{R,k,\tau}
=
{\mathfrak M}_{R,k,\tau}
\oplus
{\mathfrak I}_{R,k,\tau}
\oplus
{\mathfrak A}_{R,k,\tau}.
}
$$

The three summands are respectively the marginal coupling coordinate, the
irrelevant gauge-invariant coordinates, and the hypercubic anisotropy
coordinates.  The block-spin or finite-range RG map between two adjacent
cutoffs has the form:

$$
\boxed{
(g,h,\alpha)
\longmapsto
(g',h',\alpha').
}
$$

M1 asks for constants independent of the packet tower such that, at small
coupling,

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
|g'-g+\beta_0g^3\log b|
&\le Cg^5\log b+C\|h\|^2+C\|\alpha\|^2+C a^\kappa,\\
\|h'\|
&\le q\|h\|+C g^p a^\kappa,\\
\|\alpha'\|
&\le q\|\alpha\|+C a^\kappa,\\
\|{\mathcal R}'-{\mathcal R}\circ{\mathcal B}\|_{{\mathcal N}_{m,k,n}}
&\le C a^\kappa.
\end{aligned}
}
$$

Here $0<q<1$, $\kappa>0$, $p>0$, and the same constants work for every packet
inside the fixed physical bounds.  The last line is the response comparison
estimate: ${\mathcal B}$ is the blocking map on flowed insertions and
${\mathcal R}$ is the finite response functional.

Consequence.  M1 closes U for positive-flow local packets in the ultraviolet
corridor and supplies the small-field part of ER along the cofinal cutoff
sequence:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n C a_n^\kappa < \infty.
}
$$

What must still be proved for M1.  One must construct the Banach chart from
the regulated gauge measure, prove the triangular operator-mixing bounds in
the gauge-invariant flowed basis, and show that the inverse response Jacobian
is uniformly bounded on cofinal finite packets.  This is the nonperturbative
part of CL1a and CL1b.

###### Master Theorem M2: Large-Field Suppression And Polymer Summability

Searchable M2 tag:

`V4P39-C0-M2-LARGE-FIELD-POLYMER-SUPPRESSION`.

Choose a gauge-covariant small-field decomposition by block plaquette
logarithms.  Let $\Gamma$ denote a connected large-field polymer, namely a
connected union of blocks where the small-field condition fails.  Let
$\zeta_a(\Gamma;J)$ be the polymer activity in the presence of a bounded
flowed source $J$.

M2 asks for a Kotecky-Preiss type criterion:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_a(\Gamma;J)|
\le
C a^\kappa,
}
$$

uniformly for bounded flowed sources and for all sufficiently small cutoffs.
Equivalently, using the asymptotically free running coupling, it is enough to
prove a large-field action lower bound and an entropy bound:

$$
\boxed{
|\zeta_a(\Gamma;J)|
\le
\exp[-c g(a)^{-2}|\Gamma|+C_J|\Gamma|],
}
$$

and

$$
\boxed{
\#\{\Gamma\ni x:|\Gamma|=n\}
\le
\exp(\chi n),
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
c g(a)^{-2}-C_J-\chi-\lambda
\ge
\kappa\log(a^{-1})
}
$$

for small $a$.  Since asymptotic freedom gives $g(a)^{-2}$ of order
$\log(a^{-1})$, this inequality is the precise entropy-versus-action margin.

Consequence.  M2 closes the ultraviolet large-field complement and supplies the
large-field part of ER in the same asymptotically free corridor:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_{a_n}(\Gamma;J)|
<
\infty.
}
$$

What must still be proved for M2.  One must build the gauge-covariant
phase-cell decomposition, prove the large-field action lower bound after
gauge fixing or gauge averaging, control the Jacobians, and verify the
Kotecky-Preiss criterion with constants stable under the cofinal packet
tower.  This is the large-field part of the Bałaban-style burden.

###### Master Theorem M3: Zero-Flow Recovery From Small-Flow Regularity

Searchable M3 tag:

`V4P39-C0-M3-ZERO-FLOW-RECOVERY`.

Let $O_i^\tau$ be a flowed gauge-invariant composite observable and let
$O_j^{ren}(\mu)$ be a finite renormalized local basis at scale $\mu$.  M3 asks
for a uniform small-flow expansion in OS matrix-element norms:

$$
\boxed{
O_i^\tau
=
\sum_{\dim O_j\le D}
Z_{ij}(\tau,\mu)O_j^{ren}(\mu)
 +
{\mathcal E}_{i,D}(\tau,\mu).
}
$$

The required bound is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_{m,k,n}({\mathcal E}_{i,D}(\tau_n,\mu))
\le
C \tau_n^\alpha
}
$$

after the counterterm matrix $Z_{ij}$ is fixed by the same RG chart used in M1.
The discretization error must satisfy:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_{m,k,n}(O_i^{\tau_n,a_n}-O_i^{\tau_n})
\le
C a_n^\rho \tau_n^{-\sigma}.
}
$$

The flow schedule must be chosen so that:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n
\left(
\tau_n^\alpha
 +
a_n^\rho \tau_n^{-\sigma}
\right)
<
\infty.
}
$$

For a fixed finite stage, if $\tau_n=a_n^{2\theta}$ and $\sigma>0$, it is
enough to choose:

$$
\boxed{
0<\theta<\min(1,\rho/(2\sigma)).
}
$$

If $\sigma=0$, any $0<\theta<1$ is enough.  For the cofinal zero-flow algebra,
the exponents and constants are not assumed uniform across increasing operator
dimension, support, Sobolev order, or sector cutoff.  The full construction uses
the diagonal schedule of Lemma 10.28g4.5c, choosing the cutoff subsequence and
the flow time stage by stage so every fixed finite stage has a summable tail.

Consequence.  M3 closes ZF for the renormalized local algebra generated from
the positive-flow ultraviolet construction.  It also removes the earlier
ambiguity that the zero-flow algebra was merely the set of families that happen
to converge: the algebra is now the image of a controlled small-flow expansion
with a summable remainder.  Equality with a fixed-scale standard local net still
belongs to IR3 in subsection 10.28k.

What must still be proved for M3.  One must prove the flowed OPE or small-flow
expansion nonperturbatively in the OS matrix-element topology, control operator
mixing and typed counterterms uniformly, and show that every local
gauge-invariant observable used in the OS/Wightman reconstruction is generated
by this recovered zero-flow algebra.

###### Master Theorem M4-UV: Positive Ultraviolet Flowed Scale Readout

Searchable M4 tag:

`V4P39-C0-M4-UV-POSITIVE-FLOWED-SCALE-READOUT`.

Fix a gauge-invariant flowed energy density or an equivalent local scale
readout $E_\tau$.  In the ultraviolet positive-flow construction, choose a
reference flow time by the condition:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_0^2\,\omega(E_{\tau_0})=c_0
}
$$

for a predeclared positive constant $c_0$ in the weak-coupling positive-flow
window.  M4-UV asks for three uniform bounds along the cofinal ultraviolet
trajectory:

$$
\boxed{
0<c_- \le \tau_0^2\,\omega_{a,L}(E_{\tau_0})\le c_+<\infty,
}
$$

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{a,L}\left(
\left|
\int f(x)E_{\tau_0}(x)\,dx
-
\omega_{a,L}\left(\int f(x)E_{\tau_0}(x)\,dx\right)
\right|^2
\right)
\ge v_->0,
}
$$

The third estimate is:

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{a,L}({\bf 1})\ge n_->0.
}
$$

The test function $f$ is fixed, smooth, compactly supported, and nonzero.  The
second inequality rules out collapse to the zero functional or an empty
vacuum-only sector inside this positive-flow UV window.  It does not by itself
exclude a Gaussian or asymptotically free trivial continuum limit, because the
leading readout is proportional to the weak running coupling in that window.

Consequence.  M4-UV supplies a positive ultraviolet flowed readout and a
normalization receipt for the positive-flow construction.  It does not close
the full nontriviality clause NT at a fixed physical infrared scale.  Full NT
requires the IR bridge of subsection 10.28k.

What must still be proved for full M4.  One must show that a fixed physical
scale can be selected without sliding into the ultraviolet, that the connected
variance lower bound at that scale survives the continuum and thermodynamic
limits, and that the proof does not import confinement, an area law, or the
spectral gap.

###### Master UV Closure Theorem For The Positive-Flow Core

Searchable master closure tag:

`V4P39-C0-UV-OPEN-CORE-MASTER-CLOSURE-THEOREM`.

Assume M1, M2, M3, and M4-UV.  Then the ultraviolet positive-flow versions of
the clauses in subsection 10.28g close:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{M1}+\mathrm{M2}+\mathrm{M3}+\mathrm{M4\text{-}UV}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{U}_{UV}+\mathrm{LF}_{UV}+\mathrm{ER}_{UV}+\mathrm{ZF}_{ren}
+\mathrm{NT}_{UV}.
}
$$

Proof.  M1 gives packet-independent RG and response comparison constants on
positive-flow finite local packets, hence U for the flowed construction.  M2
controls the complement of the small-field chart by a summable polymer
criterion, hence LF.  The small-field response error from M1 and the
large-field polymer error from M2 are both summable along the cofinal cutoff
sequence, hence ER at positive flow.  M3 chooses a flow schedule for which the
small-flow remainder and the lattice-flow discretization error are summable;
therefore the positive-flow limits descend to the zero-flow local
gauge-invariant algebra, hence ZF.  M4 supplies a nonzero normalization and a
positive finite local readout in the weak-coupling positive-flow window, hence
NT at UV positive flow.  Together these are the ultraviolet receipt versions of
the five missing clauses listed in subsection 10.28g.

Therefore the route to a conventional C0 proof is not finished by M1 through
M4-UV.  One must still prove the fixed-physical-scale IR bridge in subsection
10.28k.

$$
\square
$$

###### Recommended Order Of Attack

The clauses should not be attacked in alphabetical order.  The mathematically
efficient order is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{LF}
\longrightarrow
\mathrm{U+ER}
\longrightarrow
\mathrm{ZF}
\longrightarrow
\mathrm{NT}.
}
$$

Reason.  LF must come first because no uniform RG chart is global until the
large-field complement is dominated.  Once LF is available, M1 can be upgraded
from packetwise small-field control to uniform projective control, and ER
becomes a derived summability statement.  ZF should come after positive-flow
uniformity, because zero-flow composites are singular before the flowed
counterterm matrix is controlled.  NT should come last, because a
nontriviality lower bound is meaningful only after the continuum trajectory
and the physical scale readout have been fixed without using the desired gap
conclusion.

This is the rigorous version of the Einstein/Feynman strategy: invariant
local-net uniqueness supplies the architecture, and finite estimates supply
the receipts.

##### 10.28g2: Execution I -- Heat-Kernel Large-Field Polymer Domination

Searchable execution-I tag:

`V4P39-C0-EXECUTE-LF-HEAT-KERNEL-POLYMER`.

This subsection executes the first step of the attack:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{LF}
}
$$

The result is deliberately scoped.  It proves the large-field polymer
suppression needed by M2 for the heat-kernel regulator at positive flow and
bounded finite source strength.  It does not prove the packet-uniform RG chart
M1, the zero-flow theorem M3, or the fixed-scale nontriviality bridge IR2.

###### Definition 10.28g2.1: Heat-Kernel Large-Field Cells

Fix a compact group:

$$
\boxed{
G=SU(N).
}
$$

Let $d_G$ be the bi-invariant Riemannian distance on $G$, normalized on a
fixed compact fundamental ball.  The heat-kernel plaquette density at time
$t>0$ is denoted:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_t(U).
}
$$

Choose once and for all a radius:

$$
\boxed{
0<\delta<\delta_{inj}/8.
}
$$

A plaquette is small-field when:

$$
\boxed{
d_G(U_p,{\bf 1})\le \delta.
}
$$

It is large-field when:

$$
\boxed{
d_G(U_p,{\bf 1})>\delta.
}
$$

Partition the plaquette set into disjoint coarse blocks, each a fixed finite
union of plaquettes of bounded combinatorial diameter.  A block is bad when it
contains at least one large-field plaquette.  A large-field polymer is a
connected union of bad blocks in the coarse-block adjacency graph.

For the large-field probability estimate, first take the source $J$ to be real,
positive-flow local, and bounded in the following absolute sense:

$$
\boxed{
|e^{J({\mathcal U})}|
\le
\exp(C_J\,|\operatorname{supp}J|).
}
$$

Here $C_J$ depends on the chosen physical source-radius ball but not on the
cutoff, volume, or packet index inside that ball.  Complex source responses are
then recovered by applying the same estimates on the boundary of the bounded
complex source polydisc and using Cauchy's formula for the finite source
derivatives.  Thus the normalized probability measure below is always positive
when it is used as a measure.

Flat-sector convention.  LF in this subsection means curvature-large
plaquette events.  Plaquette-small configurations with nontrivial global
holonomy, center flux, toron data, or topological charge are not counted as
large-field errors.  They are sector data.  On a contractible local support,
the lattice small-curvature Poincare lemma puts plaquette-small configurations
into a local small-link gauge after choosing a tree gauge.  On a noncontractible
support, the residual flat data are finite-dimensional global labels and are
handled by the sector packet, not by large-field suppression.  Thus the LF
receipt below suppresses only the complement of the local small-curvature
chart; it does not claim that flat global sectors are exponentially rare.

###### Lemma 10.28g2.1a: Lattice Small-Curvature Poincare Lemma

Let $K$ be a finite connected plaquette complex contained in a coordinate ball
of the lattice.  Assume $K$ is contractible and every plaquette in $K$ obeys:

$$
\boxed{
d_G(U_p,{\bf 1})\le\delta.
}
$$

For $\delta$ sufficiently small, there is a lattice gauge transformation and a
spanning tree gauge such that every link in $K$ obeys:

$$
\boxed{
d_G(U_\ell,{\bf 1})\le C_K\delta.
}
$$

Here $C_K$ depends only on the combinatorial diameter of $K$.  If $K$ is not
contractible, the same conclusion holds after adjoining one flat holonomy
parameter for each generator of the first lattice homology of $K$:

$$
\boxed{
h_1,\ldots,h_{b_1(K)}\in SU(N).
}
$$

These residual parameters are sector labels and not LF errors.

Proof.  Choose a spanning tree in the one-skeleton of $K$ and gauge transform
all tree links to the identity.  For a non-tree link $\ell$, the unique tree
path closing $\ell$ gives a fundamental lattice loop.  Since $K$ is
contractible, this loop is homologous to a product of at most $C_K$ plaquette
boundaries.  The holonomy of $\ell$ in tree gauge is therefore an ordered
product of at most $C_K$ plaquette holonomies and their conjugates.  For
$\delta$ inside the injectivity radius, the logarithm map and the
Baker-Campbell-Hausdorff estimate give:

$$
\boxed{
d_G(U_\ell,{\bf 1})\le C_K\delta.
}
$$

If $K$ is not contractible, the same construction leaves one unfilled loop for
each independent one-cycle.  Those loop holonomies cannot be controlled by
local plaquette curvature and are exactly the displayed flat sector labels.

$$
\square
$$

The finite-volume heat-kernel expectation with source $J$ is:

$$
\boxed{
\langle F\rangle_{t,J,\Lambda}
=
\frac{1}{Z_{t,J,\Lambda}}
\int F({\mathcal U})e^{J({\mathcal U})}
\prod_{p\subset\Lambda}\rho_t(U_p)
\prod_{\ell\subset\Lambda}dU_\ell.
}
$$

The partition function is:

$$
\boxed{
Z_{t,J,\Lambda}
=
\int e^{J({\mathcal U})}
\prod_{p\subset\Lambda}\rho_t(U_p)
\prod_{\ell\subset\Lambda}dU_\ell.
}
$$

All large-field activities below are defined relative to this normalized
measure or to finite-volume polymer activities obtained from its Mayer
expansion.  No unnormalized denominator is suppressed.

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2: Uniform Heat-Kernel Bad-Plaquette Cost

There are constants $c_\delta>0$, $C_\delta<\infty$, and $t_\delta>0$ such
that for all $0<t<t_\delta$:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{d_G(U,{\bf 1})>\delta}
\frac{\rho_t(U)}{\rho_t({\bf 1})}
\le
C_\delta\exp(-c_\delta/t).
}
$$

Proof.  The heat kernel on a compact Lie group satisfies the standard small-time
Gaussian upper and lower bounds.  For every radius below the injectivity
radius, there are constants $C_1,C_2,c_1,c_2$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_t(U)
\le
C_1t^{-d/2}
\exp[-c_1 d_G(U,{\bf 1})^2/t]
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_t({\bf 1})
\ge
C_2^{-1}t^{-d/2}.
}
$$

On the large-field set, the distance is at least $\delta$.  Taking the ratio
gives the displayed estimate after changing constants.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2a: Heat-Kernel Defect Domination

For every $\alpha>1$ there are constants $K_\delta(\alpha)<\infty$,
$c_\delta'(\alpha)>0$, and $t_\delta'(\alpha)>0$ such that for all
$0<t<t_\delta'(\alpha)$ and all $U\in SU(N)$:

$$
\boxed{
{\bf 1}_{\{d_G(U,{\bf 1})>\delta\}}\rho_t(U)
\le
K_\delta(\alpha)e^{-c_\delta'(\alpha)/t}\rho_{\alpha t}(U).
}
$$

Proof.  Use the sharp compact-group Varadhan bounds.  For every small
$\varepsilon>0$ and all sufficiently small $t$:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_t(U)
\le
C_\varepsilon t^{-d/2}
\exp[-(d_G(U,{\bf 1})^2-\varepsilon)/(4t)]
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\rho_{\alpha t}(U)
\ge
C_\varepsilon^{-1}(\alpha t)^{-d/2}
\exp[-(d_G(U,{\bf 1})^2+\varepsilon)/(4\alpha t)].
}
$$

On the large-field set, $d_G(U,{\bf 1})\ge\delta$.  Taking the ratio gives an
exponent bounded above by:

$$
\boxed{
-\frac{1}{4t}
\left[
(1-\alpha^{-1})\delta^2
-\varepsilon(1+\alpha^{-1})
\right].
}
$$

Choose $\varepsilon$ smaller than one half of
$(1-\alpha^{-1})\delta^2/(1+\alpha^{-1})$.  The bracket is then positive.
Absorb the polynomial prefactor into $K_\delta(\alpha)$ and call the positive
coefficient $c_\delta'(\alpha)$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b: Finite-Energy Plaquette-Time Replacement

Fix $\alpha>1$ and write:

$$
\boxed{
c_\delta'=c_\delta'(\alpha),
\qquad
K_\delta=K_\delta(\alpha).
}
$$

Fix also a bounded positive-flow source radius.  There are constants
$A_{FE}(\alpha)\ge0$ and $B_{FE}(\alpha)<\infty$, independent of volume, cutoff,
and packet index inside that source radius, such that for every finite
plaquette set $S$:

$$
\boxed{
\frac{
\int e^{J({\mathcal U})}
\prod_{p\in S}\rho_{\alpha t}(U_p)
\prod_{p\notin S}\rho_t(U_p)
\prod_\ell dU_\ell
}{
Z_{t,J,\Lambda}
}
\le
\exp[(A_{FE}(\alpha)/t+B_{FE}(\alpha))|S|].
}
$$

The replacement is useful only when the finite-energy margin is positive:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}:=c_\delta'-A_{FE}(\alpha)>0.
}
$$

Proof.  The proof is local.  Replace the plaquette times one at a time.  At
each step, condition on all links outside a fixed collar of the plaquette being
replaced.  The collar contains a bounded number of links and plaquettes.  The
one-step replacement ratio is a ratio of two finite-dimensional compact-group
integrals.  Its Radon-Nikodym factor is:

$$
\boxed{
\frac{\rho_{\alpha t}(U_p)}{\rho_t(U_p)}.
}
$$

The compact-group heat-kernel upper and lower bounds imply that this ratio is
bounded inside the collar by:

$$
\boxed{
\exp[A_{FE}(\alpha)/t+B_{FE}(\alpha)]
}
$$

after integrating the collar variables.  The constants are independent of the
exterior boundary condition because the collar has fixed size and the heat
kernel is strictly positive.  The real bounded source changes the collar
integral by at most a fixed multiplicative factor, absorbed into
$B_{FE}(\alpha)$.  Iterating over $|S|$ selected plaquettes gives the displayed
bound.

This lemma is the finite-energy replacement certificate.  The strict margin
$m_{FE}>0$ is the check that the softening cost does not consume the bad-field
defect cost.  Without that margin, LF is not closed.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b1: Local Collar Variational Formula For The Finite-Energy Margin

The coefficient $A_{FE}(\alpha)$ in Lemma 10.28g2.2b is a local collar
constant.  More precisely, let $\mathfrak C$ be the fixed plaquette collar used
in the one-step replacement proof, let $\eta$ denote its exterior boundary
links, and let $J_{\mathfrak C}$ range over the bounded real positive-flow
source ball restricted to the collar.  Define the one-plaquette replacement
ratio:

$$
\boxed{
R_t^\alpha(\eta,J_{\mathfrak C})
=
\frac{
\int_{\mathfrak C}
e^{J_{\mathfrak C}}
\rho_{\alpha t}(U_{p_0})
\prod_{p\ne p_0}\rho_t(U_p)
\prod_{\ell\in\mathfrak C}dU_\ell
}{
\int_{\mathfrak C}
e^{J_{\mathfrak C}}
\rho_t(U_{p_0})
\prod_{p\ne p_0}\rho_t(U_p)
\prod_{\ell\in\mathfrak C}dU_\ell
}.
}
$$

Then the sharp replacement exponent is:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}(\alpha)
=
\limsup_{t\downarrow0}
t\log
\sup_{\eta,J_{\mathfrak C}}
R_t^\alpha(\eta,J_{\mathfrak C}).
}
$$

Consequently the finite-energy margin is closed by the finite-dimensional
strict inequality:

$$
\boxed{
c_\delta'
>
\limsup_{t\downarrow0}
t\log
\sup_{\eta,J_{\mathfrak C}}
R_t^\alpha(\eta,J_{\mathfrak C}).
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g2.2b replaces plaquette times one collar at a time.  The
only possible exponential-in-$1/t$ loss comes from the supremum of the
one-step collar ratio above; all source and Jacobian factors outside this
ratio are bounded by exponential constants independent of $1/t$.  Compactness
of the exterior boundary-link space and boundedness of the real source ball
allow the supremum to be taken over a compact set.

Lemma 10.28g2.2b1v gives the required finite-dimensional compact-collar
Varadhan bounds uniformly in the exterior data and bounded source ball.
Therefore the displayed limsup is the exact local Laplace exponent of the
plaquette-time replacement.  Iterating the one-step replacement over $|S|$
plaquettes gives the coefficient $A_{FE}(\alpha)$ and no additional
exponential-in-$1/t$ loss, because the collar size and overlap number are fixed.
The final displayed inequality is precisely the condition $m_{FE}>0$.

This lemma converts the remaining margin check into a finite-dimensional
collar estimate.  It is not a global clustering assumption and it is not an
infinite-volume input.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a0: Tree-Gauge Collar Coercivity Constants

Fix the plaquette-star collar $\mathfrak C$ and a maximal tree $T_{\mathfrak C}$
in its link graph.  Let $E_{\mathfrak C}^{0}$ be the non-tree collar links and
let $P_{\mathfrak C}^{0}$ be the plaquettes in the collar whose boundary uses at
least one non-tree link.  Linearizing the plaquette logarithm map at the
identity gives a finite real linear map:

$$
\boxed{
D_{\mathfrak C}:
\mathfrak g^{E_{\mathfrak C}^{0}}
\longrightarrow
\mathfrak g^{P_{\mathfrak C}^{0}} .
}
$$

This map has a strictly positive smallest singular value:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\mathfrak C}
=
\inf_{\|X\|=1}\|D_{\mathfrak C}X\|
>0.
}
$$

Moreover, for sufficiently small chart radius $r_{\mathfrak C}$, the nonlinear
collar plaquette logarithms satisfy:

$$
\boxed{
\Omega(X,\eta)
=
D_{\mathfrak C}X+B(\eta)+Q(X,\eta),
\qquad
\|Q(X,\eta)\|
\le
C_Q(\|X\|+\|B(\eta)\|)^2,
}
$$

and the Hessian of the collar rate obeys the uniform coercivity bound:

$$
\boxed{
\nabla_X^2 I_\eta
\ge
\sigma_{\mathfrak C}^2/8
}
$$

on the chart ball, provided $\|B(\eta)\|\le r_{\mathfrak C}$.

Consequently the unconstrained minimizer in this chart is unique and satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\|X_\eta\|
\le
C_1\|B(\eta)\|,
\qquad
\|\Omega(X_\eta,\eta)\|
\le
C_2\|B(\eta)\|,
}
$$

where $C_1$ and $C_2$ depend only on the finite collar shape and on $G$.

Proof.  If $D_{\mathfrak C}X=0$, the infinitesimal curvature of all collar
plaquettes is zero.  With the tree links fixed by maximal-tree gauge, the
standard finite lattice Poincare lemma on the simply connected plaquette-star
collar says the remaining infinitesimal connection is a pure gauge with zero
tree values, hence $X=0$.  Thus $D_{\mathfrak C}$ is injective.  Since it is a
finite matrix, its smallest singular value on the unit sphere is positive.

The expansion of the group commutator around the identity gives the displayed
quadratic remainder.  Choose the normal-coordinate radius so that the operator
norm of the first derivative of $Q$ is at most $\sigma_{\mathfrak C}/4$.  The
quadratic part of the rate is then a perturbation of
$D_{\mathfrak C}^*D_{\mathfrak C}/2$, and the displayed Hessian lower bound
follows after reducing the radius once more.  The unique minimizer and the two
estimates follow from the finite-dimensional implicit-function theorem and the
coercive Euler-Lagrange equation:

$$
\boxed{
D_{\mathfrak C}^*
\left(D_{\mathfrak C}X_\eta+B(\eta)+Q(X_\eta,\eta)\right)
=
O(r_{\mathfrak C})
\left(D_{\mathfrak C}X_\eta+B(\eta)\right).
}
$$

All constants are finite matrix constants for the fixed collar.  They do not
depend on volume, lattice spacing, source packet, or boundary condition.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a: Collar Dirichlet Minimizer Gap

Let $\mathfrak C$ be the fixed plaquette-star collar of $p_0$ in maximal-tree
gauge.  Choose the smaller exterior small-curvature radius in the definition of
$\mathfrak K$ so that the collar lies inside a single normal-coordinate chart and
so that the discrete collar Dirichlet operator has norm at most $C_{\mathfrak C}$.
Then, after decreasing that exterior radius once more if necessary:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\eta\in\mathfrak K}
\sup_{X\in{\rm Argmin}\,I_\eta}
d_G(U_{p_0}(X,\eta),{\bf 1})
\le
\delta/4.
}
$$

Consequently the constrained collar gap:

$$
\boxed{
\gamma_\delta
=
\inf_{\eta\in\mathfrak K}
\left[
\inf_{d_G(U_{p_0},{\bf 1})\ge\delta} I_\eta
-
\inf I_\eta
\right]
}
$$

is strictly positive.

Proof.  In maximal-tree gauge the collar variables are finitely many elements of
$G$.  For $\delta$ below the injectivity radius and for exterior data in
$\mathfrak K$, all minimizing configurations that can compete with the
small-curvature extension lie in one product normal-coordinate ball.  This is a
finite-dimensional statement: outside that ball at least one collar plaquette has
a group distance bounded below by a fixed multiple of $\delta$, while the
small-curvature extension has rate bounded by the square of the chosen exterior
radius.  Decreasing the exterior radius makes the outside-ball rate strictly
larger, uniformly in $\eta$.

Inside the normal-coordinate ball, write the remaining link variables as
Lie-algebra coordinates.  The plaquette logarithms have the form:

$$
\boxed{
\Omega_p(X,\eta)=d_{\mathfrak C}X_p+B_p(\eta)+Q_p(X,\eta),
}
$$

where $d_{\mathfrak C}$ is the finite collar coboundary, $B_p(\eta)$ is the
boundary curvature term, and $Q_p$ is quadratic in the coordinates.  The collar
rate is:

$$
\boxed{
I_\eta(X)
=
\frac14\sum_{p\subset\mathfrak C}|\Omega_p(X,\eta)|^2
+O(\delta)\sum_{p\subset\mathfrak C}|\Omega_p(X,\eta)|^2.
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a0 gives the finite matrix coercivity of the tree-gauge
collar operator and its nonlinear stability.  Hence the minimizer is unique in
the competing ball and obeys the finite-dimensional Dirichlet estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\max_{p\subset\mathfrak C}|\Omega_p(X_\eta,\eta)|
\le
C_{\mathfrak C}\max_{q\subset\partial\mathfrak C}|B_q(\eta)|.
}
$$

The exterior small-curvature radius defining $\mathfrak K$ was chosen so that
the right-hand side is at most $\delta/4$ for the central plaquette.  Therefore
every unconstrained minimizer has central plaquette distance at most $\delta/4$.

The graph of minimizers over $\mathfrak K$ is compact because $\mathfrak K$ is
compact and the minimizer is continuous in the finite-dimensional Dirichlet
problem.  The closed constrained set:

$$
\boxed{
\{(\eta,X):\eta\in\mathfrak K,\ d_G(U_{p_0}(X,\eta),{\bf 1})\ge\delta\}
}
$$

is disjoint from that compact minimizer graph.  Since $I_\eta(X)-\inf I_\eta$ is
continuous and vanishes exactly on the graph, its infimum on the constrained set
is positive.  This positive infimum is $\gamma_\delta$.

This is the missing finite collar calculation: the large-field gap is not being
imported from an infinite-volume clustering theorem, but from a uniformly
strict finite-dimensional Dirichlet minimum.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b1v: Uniform Compact-Collar Heat-Kernel Laplace Principle

Let $\mathfrak C$ be the fixed finite collar, let $\eta$ range in the compact
exterior set $\mathfrak K$, and let $J_{\mathfrak C}$ range in a bounded real
positive-flow source ball.  For every $\varepsilon>0$ there are constants
$C_\varepsilon<\infty$ and $t_\varepsilon>0$, depending only on the collar,
$G$, $\mathfrak K$, the source radius, and $\varepsilon$, such that for every
$0<t<t_\varepsilon$ and every plaquette-time multiplier vector
$\beta_p\in[1,\alpha_0]$:

$$
\boxed{
C_\varepsilon^{-1}
\exp\left[
-\frac{1}{t}
\left(\inf_X I_{\eta,\beta}(X)+\varepsilon\right)
\right]
\le
\int_{\mathfrak C}
e^{J_{\mathfrak C}}
\prod_{p\subset\mathfrak C}\rho_{\beta_p t}(U_p)
\prod_{\ell\in\mathfrak C}dU_\ell
\le
C_\varepsilon
\exp\left[
-\frac{1}{t}
\left(\inf_X I_{\eta,\beta}(X)-\varepsilon\right)
\right].
}
$$

Here:

$$
\boxed{
I_{\eta,\beta}(X)
=
\frac14\sum_{p\subset\mathfrak C}
\beta_p^{-1}d_G(U_p(X,\eta),{\bf 1})^2.
}
$$

With an inserted indicator of any closed condition $F(X,\eta)\in C$, the upper
bound holds with the infimum restricted to that closed set.  With an inserted
indicator of any open condition, the lower bound holds with the corresponding
open-set infimum and the usual $\varepsilon$ slack.  These are exactly the two
sides needed below: closed bad-plaquette events are used only for upper bounds,
and lower bounds are used only on open neighborhoods of minimizers.

Proof.  The compact Lie-group heat kernel has the global short-time bounds:

$$
\boxed{
c_\varepsilon t^{-d_G/2}
\exp[-(d_G(g,{\bf 1})^2+\varepsilon)/(4t)]
\le
\rho_t(g)
\le
C_\varepsilon t^{-d_G/2}
\exp[-(d_G(g,{\bf 1})^2-\varepsilon)/(4t)]
}
$$

for $0<t<t_\varepsilon$, uniformly in $g\in G$.  Apply these bounds to the
finitely many plaquettes in the collar.  The polynomial powers of $t$, the
bounded Haar-density Jacobians in finitely many charts, and the bounded source
factor $e^{J_{\mathfrak C}}$ are all absorbed into $C_\varepsilon$, since
$t\log t$ tends to zero; equivalently, one first proves the estimate with
$\varepsilon/2$ and spends the remaining $\varepsilon/2$ on these finite
prefactors.  A finite normal-coordinate partition of the compact collar manifold
gives the matching lower bound by integrating over a small ball around a
minimizer.  For a closed condition one keeps only the upper half of the
argument; for an open condition one integrates over a small ball contained in
the condition.  This gives the conditional versions stated above.

The estimate is uniform because the collar has fixed dimension, the multiplier
range $[1,\alpha_0]$ is compact, and the exterior set $\mathfrak K$ is compact.
This is the exact finite-dimensional input used when Theorem 10.28g2.2b2 writes
the replacement exponent as an infimum difference and when it extracts the
bad-plaquette cost from the heat-kernel ratio.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g2.2b2: Finite Collar Inequality

For the heat-kernel plaquette-star collar and every sufficiently small
large-field radius $\delta$ below the injectivity radius, there is a choice of
$\alpha>1$ such that the pre-history collar margin is positive:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}^{\rm coll}=c_\delta'(\alpha)-A_{FE}(\alpha)>0.
}
$$

More precisely, if $\lambda_\alpha=1-\alpha^{-1}$, the effective margin after
finite collar charging, but before exploration entropy is subtracted, can be
chosen to obey:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}^{\rm coll}
\ge
\frac{3}{32N_{FE}}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2
>0.
}
$$

Hence the finite-energy collar margin entering the large-field polymer estimate
is a computed local heat-kernel collar rate inequality, not an independent
admissibility assumption.  The exploration entropy is subtracted explicitly in
Theorem 10.28g2.2b4 below.

Proof.  Work in the plaquette-star collar $\mathfrak C$ of a fixed plaquette
$p_0$.  Gauge fix a maximal tree in the collar.  The remaining link variables
are a finite-dimensional compact manifold, and for $\delta$ below the
injectivity radius the small-curvature region is covered by finitely many
Lie-algebra charts.  Exterior boundary links are parameters.

Let $I_{\eta}$ be the collar heat-kernel rate function at fixed exterior
boundary $\eta$:

$$
\boxed{
I_{\eta}(X)
=
\frac14
\sum_{p\subset\mathfrak C}
d_G(U_p(X,\eta),{\bf 1})^2.
}
$$

Let $\mathfrak K$ be the compact set of exterior boundary data for which the
boundary plaquettes outside the collar are in the smaller small-curvature chart
whose radius is chosen so that the lattice small-curvature Poincare constant
sends exterior small curvature to central-plaquette distance at most
$\delta/4$.  If an exterior boundary datum is not in $\mathfrak K$, the exterior
already contains a charged exterior defect handled by the bounded exploration
lemma, so no isolated one-plaquette collar replacement is used at that step.
If $\epsilon_{\mathfrak K}$ is that smaller chart radius, define the exterior
defect exponent:

$$
\boxed{
\gamma_{\rm ext}=\epsilon_{\mathfrak K}^2/8.
}
$$

The collar Dirichlet estimate in Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\eta\in\mathfrak K}
\sup_{X\in{\rm Argmin}\,I_\eta}
d_G(U_{p_0}(X,\eta),{\bf 1})
\le
\delta/4.
}
$$

Define:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_\alpha=1-\alpha^{-1},
\qquad
q_0(X,\eta)=\frac14 d_G(U_{p_0}(X,\eta),{\bf 1})^2 .
}
$$

Softening only the central plaquette replaces the collar rate by:

$$
\boxed{
I_\eta^\alpha(X)
=
I_\eta(X)-\lambda_\alpha q_0(X,\eta).
}
$$

By the uniform compact-collar heat-kernel Laplace principle in Lemma
10.28g2.2b1v, the raw one-collar replacement exponent is:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
=
\sup_{\eta\in\mathfrak K}
\left[
\inf_X I_\eta(X)-\inf_X I_\eta^\alpha(X)
\right].
}
$$

Bounded positive-flow sources do not enter this exponent because they are not
multiplied by $1/t$.

We now estimate this exponent.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
Q_G=\frac14\sup_{g\in G}d_G(g,{\bf 1})^2<\infty .
}
$$

By compactness of the minimizer graph over $\mathfrak K$, choose an open
neighborhood $\mathcal N$ of that graph such that:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{(X,\eta)\in\mathcal N}q_0(X,\eta)
\le
\delta^2/32.
}
$$

The same compactness gives a positive variational gap outside the neighborhood:

$$
\boxed{
\Gamma_{\mathcal N}
=
\inf_{\eta\in\mathfrak K}
\left[
\inf_{X\notin\mathcal N}I_\eta(X)-\inf_X I_\eta(X)
\right]
>0 .
}
$$

Choose $\alpha>1$ so close to one that:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_\alpha Q_G<\Gamma_{\mathcal N}/2,
\qquad
\frac{3}{32}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2\le \gamma_{\rm ext}.
}
$$

Then every minimizer of $I_\eta^\alpha$ lies in $\mathcal N$.  Outside
$\mathcal N$ the gain from the negative perturbation is at most
$\lambda_\alpha Q_G$, while the unperturbed loss is at least
$\Gamma_{\mathcal N}$.  Hence:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
\le
\lambda_\alpha\delta^2/32.
}
$$

Now compute the competing bad-plaquette heat-kernel cost with the same
$\lambda_\alpha$.  The compact-group heat-kernel ratio for the central plaquette
has the Varadhan exponent:

$$
\boxed{
-\lambda_\alpha q_0(U_{p_0})/t.
}
$$

On the bad event $d_G(U_{p_0},{\bf 1})\ge\delta$, Lemma 10.28g2.2b1v gives the
exact leading rate $\lambda_\alpha\delta^2/4$.  Reserving half of that rate for
the two-sided heat-kernel prefactors, chart partition, and bounded collar source
constants, the raw local defect exponent may be chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\rm bad}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
\ge
\lambda_\alpha\delta^2/8.
}
$$

Therefore the one-collar strict margin is:

$$
\boxed{
c_{\rm bad}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)-A_{FE}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
\ge
\lambda_\alpha\delta^2
\left(\frac18-\frac1{32}\right)
=
\frac{3}{32}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2
>0.
}
$$

Finally include the finite geometry loss from collar overlap and exterior
charging.  The exterior alternative costs at least $\gamma_{\rm ext}/t$, and the
choice of $\alpha$ makes this no smaller than the raw collar margin.  Let
$N_{FE}$ be the bounded exploration constant from Lemma
10.28g2.2b3.  Since the exploration selects charged finite collars with
cardinality at least a $1/N_{FE}$ fraction of the charged plaquette set, the
effective margin per charged plaquette may be chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}^{\rm coll}
=
\frac{1}{N_{FE}}
\left(
c_{\rm bad}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)-A_{FE}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
\right)
\ge
\frac{3}{32N_{FE}}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2
>0.
}
$$

Equivalently, in the shorthand used by Lemmas 10.28g2.2b and 10.28g2.2c, write
$m_{FE}^{\rm coll}=c_\delta'(\alpha)-A_{FE}(\alpha)$ after absorbing the fixed
finite overlap and charging loss into the effective constants.  The important
point is that both constants are computed from the same raw one-collar
inequality above; no positive exponent is inserted by hand.

This proves the finite collar inequality.  The proof is finite-dimensional,
local, and uniform in volume and cutoff because the collar shape, source
radius, exterior compact set, and exploration constant are fixed.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2b3: Bounded Collar Exploration And Charging

Fix the plaquette-star collar shape and the exterior compact set
$\mathfrak K$.  Let $\Delta_{\mathfrak C}$ be the maximal degree of the plaquette
adjacency graph in which two plaquettes are adjacent when one lies in the fixed
collar of the other.  Let $r_{\mathfrak C}$ be the graph radius needed to ensure
that two plaquettes at distance greater than $r_{\mathfrak C}$ have disjoint
replacement collars.  Define:

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathfrak C}^{(r)}
=
1+\Delta_{\mathfrak C}+
\sum_{j=2}^{r_{\mathfrak C}}
\Delta_{\mathfrak C}(\Delta_{\mathfrak C}-1)^{j-1},
\qquad
N_{\rm sep}=\Delta_{\mathfrak C}^{(r)}+1.
}
$$

Let $D_{\mathfrak C}$ be the maximal number of collar exteriors containing any
fixed plaquette.  Set:

$$
\boxed{
N_{FE}=D_{\mathfrak C}N_{\rm sep},
\qquad
C_{\mathfrak C}^{\rm exp}=8e\Delta_{\mathfrak C}.
}
$$

These constants depend only on the fixed collar shape and spacetime dimension.
The constant $N_{FE}$ is the same finite geometry loss used in Theorem
10.28g2.2b2.

For every finite selected plaquette set $S$, the event that all plaquettes in
$S$ are large is covered by a finite union of exploration histories
$\mathcal H$ with associated finite charged-defect plaquette sets
$T(\mathcal H)$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
S\subset T(\mathcal H),
\qquad
|T(\mathcal H)|\ge |S|,
\qquad
\#\{\mathcal H:|T(\mathcal H)|=n\}
\le
(C_{\mathfrak C}^{\rm exp})^n .
}
$$

Along each history there is a subcollection
$Q(\mathcal H)\subset T(\mathcal H)$ of charged plaquettes with mutually bounded
collar overlap and:

$$
\boxed{
|Q(\mathcal H)|\ge |T(\mathcal H)|/N_{FE}.
}
$$

For every $q\in Q(\mathcal H)$, either the exterior of its collar lies in
$\mathfrak K$, so Theorem 10.28g2.2b2 supplies the collar defect, or $q$ is
itself an exterior-defect plaquette produced by a failed exterior-smallness
condition.  An exterior-defect plaquette means a plaquette outside the smaller
chart defining $\mathfrak K$.  If
$\epsilon_{\mathfrak K}$ is that chart radius, set:

$$
\boxed{
\gamma_{\rm ext}=\epsilon_{\mathfrak K}^2/8.
}
$$

After reserving half of the heat-kernel rate for finite prefactors, the
heat-kernel cost of such an exterior defect is at least $\gamma_{\rm ext}/t$ up
to bounded constants.  Each charged-defect plaquette is charged at most
$D_{\mathfrak C}$ times.

Proof.  Start from $S$ and perform a deterministic breadth-first exploration in
the plaquette adjacency graph whose edges join plaquettes lying in one another's
fixed collar.  When the exterior of the current collar is in $\mathfrak K$, mark
the current plaquette as scored.  When it is not in $\mathfrak K$, the definition
of $\mathfrak K$ says that one of the finitely many boundary plaquettes in the
collar exterior is outside the smaller small-curvature chart.  Add the first
such exterior-defect plaquette in a fixed ordering to the exploration queue and
record one charge.  The heat-kernel rate of this smaller-chart defect is the
positive exterior rate used as the exterior alternative in Theorem
10.28g2.2b2.

The graph degree is bounded by $\Delta_{\mathfrak C}$ because the collar shape is
fixed.  A connected explored set of size $n$ containing one prescribed root has
at most $(e\Delta_{\mathfrak C})^n$ possible rooted shapes by the standard
depth-first encoding of finite connected subgraphs of a bounded-degree graph.
The deterministic rule has at most four local labels per newly discovered
plaquette: scored, exterior-charged, already-seen, or terminal.  This gives the
printed bound $(C_{\mathfrak C}^{\rm exp})^n$ after summing over the finitely
many possible roots in $S$, which is absorbed into the same exponential because
$n\ge |S|$ and $n\le 2^n$.

To construct $Q(\mathcal H)$, first collapse repeated exterior charges: if the
same exterior-defect plaquette was produced by several failed collars, keep one
copy and charge the discarded copies to that kept plaquette.  This costs at most
$D_{\mathfrak C}$ because a fixed plaquette can belong to only
$D_{\mathfrak C}$ collar exteriors.  Then color the graph power in which two
remaining charged plaquettes are connected when their replacement collars
overlap.  The degree of this graph power is at most
$\Delta_{\mathfrak C}^{(r)}$, hence a greedy coloring uses at most $N_{\rm sep}$
colors.  One color class contains at least a $1/N_{\rm sep}$ fraction of the
remaining charged plaquettes and has pairwise disjoint replacement collars.
That color class is $Q(\mathcal H)$ and satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
|Q(\mathcal H)|
\ge
|T(\mathcal H)|/(D_{\mathfrak C}N_{\rm sep})
=
|T(\mathcal H)|/N_{FE}.
}
$$

The same collar-counting definition of $D_{\mathfrak C}$ proves the charge
multiplicity bound: an exterior-defect plaquette can be charged only by collars
whose exterior contains it, and there are at most $D_{\mathfrak C}$ such
collars.

The construction is finite-volume and deterministic.  It does not assume decay
of correlations; it only uses the local finite geometry of the plaquette-star
collar and the definition of the exterior compact set.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g2.2b4: Explicit Entropy-Subtracted Large-Field Margin

The large-field polymer margin can be chosen from an explicit interval of
softening parameters.  Define:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_{\max}
=
\min\left\{
\frac12,\,
\frac{\Gamma_{\mathcal N}}{4Q_G},\,
\frac{16\gamma_{\rm ext}}{3\delta^2}
\right\}.
}
$$

Define the admissible softening interval by:

$$
\boxed{
I_\alpha
=
\left[
\frac{1}{1-\lambda_{\max}/4},
\frac{1}{1-\lambda_{\max}/2}
\right].
}
$$

For every $\alpha\in I_\alpha$, one has:

$$
\boxed{
\frac{\lambda_{\max}}4
\le
\lambda_\alpha
\le
\frac{\lambda_{\max}}2,
\qquad
\lambda_\alpha=1-\alpha^{-1}.
}
$$

The conditions used in Theorem 10.28g2.2b2 are then automatic:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_\alpha Q_G<\Gamma_{\mathcal N}/2,
\qquad
\frac{3}{32}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2\le \gamma_{\rm ext}.
}
$$

Let the bounded exploration entropy be:

$$
\boxed{
\mu_{\rm explore}
=
\max\{2,C_{\mathfrak C}^{\rm exp}\}.
}
$$

Let the pre-entropy action advantage per original selected plaquette be:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)
=
\frac{1}{N_{FE}}
\left(
c_{\rm bad}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)-A_{FE}^{\rm raw}(\alpha)
\right).
}
$$

Then for every $\alpha\in I_\alpha$:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)
\ge
\frac{3}{128N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2.
}
$$

The heat-kernel ratio constants in Lemma 10.28g2.2a are uniform on the compact
interval $I_\alpha$.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
t_\delta^{I}
=
\inf_{\alpha\in I_\alpha}t_\delta'(\alpha)
>0.
}
$$

Let $C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)$ be the logarithmic prefactor loss per charged
plaquette after the exploration entropy has been separated.  It contains the
finite chart partition constants, the powers of $t$ already paid for in the
compact heat-kernel bounds, the bounded positive-flow source envelope, the
bounded overlap-coloring loss, and the finite exterior-charge labels.  It does
not contain $C_{\mathfrak C}^{\rm exp}$.  Because the collar shape is fixed and
$I_\alpha$ is compact:

$$
\boxed{
C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)<\infty .
}
$$

Choose the plaquette heat-kernel time inside the explicit small-time window:

$$
\boxed{
0<t<t_{FE}^{\rm exp},
\qquad
t_{FE}^{\rm exp}
=
\min\left\{
t_\varepsilon,\,
t_\delta,\,
t_\delta^I,\,
\frac{3\lambda_{\max}\delta^2}
{256N_{FE}\left(\log\mu_{\rm explore}+C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)\right)}
\right\}.
}
$$

The entropy-subtracted large-field margin is:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}(\alpha,t)
=
A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)
-t\log\mu_{\rm explore}.
}
$$

For every $\alpha\in I_\alpha$ and every $0<t<t_{FE}^{\rm exp}$:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}(\alpha,t)
\ge
\frac{3}{256N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2
>0.
}
$$

Equivalently, in the exponent units used by the polymer expansion:

$$
\boxed{
\frac{m_{FE}(\alpha,t)}{t}
=
\frac{A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)}{t}
-\log\mu_{\rm explore}
>0.
}
$$

The full one-step polymer bracket, including the finite non-exponential
prefactor loss, has the explicit positive lower bound:

$$
\boxed{
\widehat m_{FE}(\alpha,t)
=
\frac{A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)}{t}
-C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)
-\log\mu_{\rm explore}
\ge
\frac{3\lambda_{\max}\delta^2}{256N_{FE}t}
>0.
}
$$

This is the promised entropy-and-prefactor-subtracted inequality.  In the
notation of Lemma 10.28g2.2c, the displayed
$C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)$ is one possible uniform upper bound for the finite
loss later written as $B_{FE}(\alpha)+\log K_\delta$.  The strict $1/t$-scale
action margin is the positive quantity $m_{FE}(\alpha,t)$ above.

Proof.  If $\alpha\in I_\alpha$, then $\lambda_\alpha$ lies between
$\lambda_{\max}/4$ and $\lambda_{\max}/2$.  The definition of $\lambda_{\max}$
gives the minimizer-stability condition and the exterior-defect comparison
condition used in Theorem 10.28g2.2b2.

Theorem 10.28g2.2b2 gives:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)
\ge
\frac{3}{32N_{FE}}\lambda_\alpha\delta^2.
}
$$

Using the lower endpoint of the interval:

$$
\boxed{
A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)
\ge
\frac{3}{128N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2.
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g2.2b3 bounds the number of exploration histories of charged size
$n$ by $(\mu_{\rm explore})^n$.  Multiplying a one-history bound by this count
subtracts exactly $t\log\mu_{\rm explore}$ from the heat-kernel rate.  The
chosen small-time window gives:

$$
\boxed{
t\log\mu_{\rm explore}
\le
\frac{3}{256N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2.
}
$$

The same small-time condition also gives:

$$
\boxed{
t\left(\log\mu_{\rm explore}+C_{FE}^{\rm pref}(I_\alpha)\right)
\le
\frac{3}{256N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2.
}
$$

Combining the previous two displayed estimates gives the printed lower bound
for $m_{FE}(\alpha,t)$ and for the complete bracket
$\widehat m_{FE}(\alpha,t)$.  No further choice of $\alpha$ is made after the
interval $I_\alpha$ is fixed.  The lower bound $t_\delta^I>0$ follows because
Lemma 10.28g2.2a is proved from compact-group heat-kernel bounds that are
uniform for $\alpha$ in any compact subset of $(1,\infty)$; the interval
$I_\alpha$ is compact and lies inside that set.

For the remainder of the paper, $m_{FE}$ denotes any fixed positive lower bound
for $m_{FE}(\alpha,t)$ with $\alpha\in I_\alpha$ and
$0<t<t_{FE}^{\rm exp}$, for instance:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}
=
\frac{3}{256N_{FE}}\lambda_{\max}\delta^2.
}
$$

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.2c: Multi-Bad-Plaquette Domination

For every finite plaquette set $S$:

$$
\boxed{
\left\langle
\prod_{p\in S}{\bf 1}_{\{d_G(U_p,{\bf 1})>\delta\}}
\right\rangle_{t,J,\Lambda}
\le
\exp[-(m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta)|S|].
}
$$

Proof.  Apply the bounded exploration lemma to the event that all plaquettes in
$S$ are large.  For one exploration history $\mathcal H$, apply Theorem
10.28g2.2b2 on the charged collars in $Q(\mathcal H)$.  Bounded collar overlap
lets the plaquette-time replacements be ordered after splitting
$Q(\mathcal H)$ into finitely many disjoint-overlap classes.  The fixed loss from
that splitting has already been included in the computed collar margin
$A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)$.  Thus one history contributes at most:

$$
\boxed{
K_1^{|T(\mathcal H)|}
\exp[-A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)|T(\mathcal H)|/t]
}
$$

times a softened finite-energy integral with only non-exponential collar and
source losses.  The finitely many unscored charges and overlap classes only
change the constants, because every unscored failure is charged to a nearby
large plaquette with bounded multiplicity.

Summing over histories uses the exponential history count in Lemma
10.28g2.2b3.  Theorem 10.28g2.2b4 subtracts the exploration entropy
$\log\mu_{\rm explore}$ from the $1/t$-scale action advantage and replaces
$A_{FE}^{\rm gap}(\alpha)$ by the positive entropy-subtracted margin $m_{FE}$.
The remaining non-exponential constants are absorbed into $K_\delta$.  This
yields a bound of the same form as a one-step reveal but now with the charging,
collar replacement, and exploration entropy made explicit.

More explicitly, after the finite-energy replacement and the raw bad-collar or
exterior-defect cost are paired on the charged collars, the normalized
contribution of all histories of size $n$ is bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{n\ge |S|}
\left[
K_\delta
\exp[-m_{FE}/t+B_{FE}(\alpha)]
\right]^n .
}
$$

For sufficiently small $t$, the bracket is less than one.  The geometric tail is
bounded by twice its first term, and the harmless factor two is absorbed into
$K_\delta^{|S|}$.  The exponent is:

$$
\boxed{
-m_{FE}/t+B_{FE}(\alpha)+\log K_\delta
=
-(m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta).
}
$$

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.3: Bad-Block Activity Bound

Let $B$ be one block.  The normalized absolute activity of the event that $B$
is bad satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
|\zeta_t(B;J)|
\le
C_B
\exp[-(m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta)].
}
$$

Here $C_B$ depends only on the fixed block shape and $G$.

Proof.  If $B$ is bad, at least one of its finitely many plaquettes is
large-field.  Use the union bound over plaquettes in $B$.  For each selected
large plaquette, apply the normalized one-plaquette case of Lemma
10.28g2.2c.  The number of plaquettes in the block is fixed, so all
combinatorial factors are absorbed into $C_B$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g2.3a: Connected Bad-Block Ursell Activity

For a finite set $X$ of coarse blocks, let:

$$
\boxed{
E_X=\prod_{B\in X}{\bf 1}_{\{B\ {\rm bad}\}}.
}
$$

The connected bad-block activity on $X$ is the finite-volume Ursell
coefficient:

$$
\boxed{
\zeta_t(X;J)
=
\sum_{\pi\in{\mathsf{Part}}(X)}
(|\pi|-1)!(-1)^{|\pi|-1}
\prod_{Y\in\pi}
\langle E_Y\rangle_{t,J,\Lambda}.
}
$$

When $X$ is disconnected in the coarse-block adjacency graph, set:

$$
\boxed{
\zeta_t(X;J)=0.
}
$$

A polymer $\Gamma$ is a connected set of coarse blocks, and its polymer
activity is this connected coefficient:

$$
\boxed{
\zeta_t(\Gamma;J).
}
$$

Thus the activity bounded below is a genuine connected Mayer/Ursell
coefficient, not an unnormalized probability.

###### Lemma 10.28g2.3a1: Finite-Volume Dependency Graph Tree Bound

Let $\mathcal B_\Lambda$ be the finite block set in volume $\Lambda$.  Enlarge
each block by one collar radius and connect two blocks when the enlarged blocks
intersect.  This gives a finite dependency graph with degree bounded by a
constant $D_B$ depending only on the block shape and dimension.

Suppose the bad-block indicators satisfy the uniform joint rare-event estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\left\langle
\prod_{B\in Y}{\bf 1}_{\{B\ {\rm bad}\}}
\right\rangle_{t,J,\Lambda}
\le
p_t^{|Y|}
\qquad
{\rm for\ every\ finite}\ Y\subset\mathcal B_\Lambda .
}
$$

Then the finite-volume Ursell coefficient of Definition 10.28g2.3a obeys, for
every connected block set $X$:

$$
\boxed{
|\zeta_t(X;J)|
\le
\exp(C_T|X|)\,p_t^{|X|}.
}
$$

The constant $C_T$ depends only on $D_B$.

Proof.  Work first at finite volume.  Condition on all link variables outside
the union of enlarged blocks.  The heat-kernel plaquette measure is a
finite-range Markov random field: after the separating collar variables are
fixed, observables supported in different connected components of the enlarged
block graph factor.  The connected activity is therefore the dependency-graph
cumulant obtained after this collar normalization; disconnected block sets have
zero connected activity by Definition 10.28g2.3a.

For connected $X$, use the standard finite graph tree identity for cumulants.
It writes the absolute cumulant as a sum over spanning trees on $X$, with each
tree edge selecting one dependency edge of the enlarged block graph.  The
remaining integrations are positive finite compact-group integrals.  The joint
rare-event estimate supplies one factor $p_t$ for each vertex of the tree.  The
number of possible dependency-tree embeddings is bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
\#\{{\rm dependency\ trees\ on}\ X\}
\le
\exp(C_T|X|),
}
$$

because the dependency graph has degree at most $D_B$.  This gives the displayed
bound uniformly in volume.  No infinite-volume clustering assumption enters the
argument; it is a finite Markov-field cumulant estimate.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.3b: Tree-Graph Bound For Bad-Block Ursell Activities

Let:

$$
\boxed{
p_t
=
C_B\exp[-(m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta)].
}
$$

There is a constant $C_T$ depending only on the coarse-block degree such that,
for every connected polymer $\Gamma$:

$$
\boxed{
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|
\le
\exp(C_T|\Gamma|)\,p_t^{|\Gamma|}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g2.2c gives the joint rare-event estimate for any finite
choice of one large plaquette in each bad block.  Taking the union bound over
the fixed finite set of plaquettes in each block gives the joint bad-block bound
with the displayed $p_t$.  Apply Lemma 10.28g2.3a1 to the finite dependency
graph of enlarged blocks.  The constants are volume-independent because the
block shape and collar radius are fixed.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.4: Connected Polymer Activity Bound

Let $\Gamma$ be a connected large-field polymer.  Then:

$$
\boxed{
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|
\le
\exp[-\mu(t,J)|\Gamma|].
}
$$

The decay rate may be chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
\mu(t,J)
=
m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta-C_0.
}
$$

The constant $C_0$ depends only on $G$, the dimension, and the fixed block
shape.

Proof.  Apply Lemma 10.28g2.3b.  Absorb the finite block constant, the
tree-graph combinatorial factor, and the finite internal choices of bad
plaquettes, local charts, and block-shape attachments into $C_0|\Gamma|$.
The remaining exponential cost is the finite-energy margin $m_{FE}/t$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g2.5: Lattice-Animal Entropy Bound

There is a constant $\chi_d<\infty$ such that for every block $x$:

$$
\boxed{
\#\{\Gamma\ni x:|\Gamma|=n\}
\le
\exp(\chi_d n).
}
$$

Proof.  The adjacency graph of fixed-shape blocks in a hypercubic lattice has
uniformly bounded degree.  The number of connected subgraphs of size $n$
containing a fixed root in a graph of bounded degree is bounded exponentially
in $n$.  The exponent depends only on the degree and therefore only on the
spacetime dimension and block shape.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g2.6: Heat-Kernel Kotecky-Preiss Large-Field Bound

Two polymers are incompatible, written $\Gamma\not\sim\Gamma'$, when their
coarse-block distance is at most one.  Fix a positive polymer weight $\lambda$
and a bounded positive-flow source radius.  For all sufficiently small
heat-kernel times $t$:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|
\le
\exp[-\kappa(t,J)].
}
$$

The exponent satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa(t,J)
\ge
m_{FE}/t-B_{FE}(\alpha)-\log K_\delta-C_0-\chi_d-\lambda-\log 2.
}
$$

In particular, if the asymptotically free trajectory has:

$$
\boxed{
t(a)\le \frac{C_t}{\log(a^{-1})},
}
$$

then for every sufficiently small cutoff:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_{t(a)}(\Gamma;J)|
\le
C a^{\kappa_{LF}}.
}
$$

Here:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa_{LF}
=
\frac{m_{FE}}{2C_t}.
}
$$

Moreover the standard Kotecky-Preiss incompatibility criterion holds.  There
is a constant $C_{\partial}$ depending only on the block adjacency graph such
that, for all sufficiently small $t$:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\Gamma:\Gamma\not\sim\Gamma_0}
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|e^{\lambda|\Gamma|}
\le
C_{\partial}|\Gamma_0|e^{-\kappa(t,J)}
}
$$

for every polymer $\Gamma_0$.  In particular, after decreasing $t$ if
necessary:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\Gamma:\Gamma\not\sim\Gamma_0}
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|e^{\lambda|\Gamma|}
\le
\lambda|\Gamma_0|.
}
$$

Proof.  Combine Lemma 10.28g2.4 with Lemma 10.28g2.5:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|
&\le
\sum_{n\ge 1}
\exp[(\chi_d+\lambda-\mu(t,J))n].
\end{aligned}
}
$$

For small enough $t$, the exponent is below $-\log 2$.  The geometric series is
then bounded by twice its first term, which gives the first displayed estimate.
The asymptotic-freedom bound on $t(a)$ converts the exponential in $1/t(a)$ to
a positive power of $a$.  Shrinking the cutoff if necessary absorbs
$B_{FE}(\alpha)$, $\log K_\delta$, $C_0$, $\chi_d$, $\lambda$, and $\log 2$ into
half of the leading finite-energy margin.  This gives the stated power bound.

For the incompatibility criterion, every polymer incompatible with $\Gamma_0$
contains at least one coarse block in the one-neighborhood of $\Gamma_0$.  The
number of such root blocks is at most $C_{\partial}|\Gamma_0|$.  Applying the
rooted bound at each such block gives the displayed incompatibility estimate.
For sufficiently small $t$, the exponential factor is less than
$\lambda/C_{\partial}$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Corollary 10.28g2.6a: Finite-Volume KP Consequence

Under the hypotheses of Theorem 10.28g2.6, the finite-volume polymer
partition function and all connected polymer cumulants are absolutely
convergent in a neighborhood of the positive-flow source packet.  More
precisely, if $\mathcal P_\Lambda$ is the finite set of bad-block polymers in
the volume $\Lambda$, then:

$$
\boxed{
\log
\sum_{\mathcal G\subset\mathcal P_\Lambda\ {\rm compatible}}
\prod_{\Gamma\in\mathcal G}\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)
}
$$

has the absolutely convergent cluster expansion:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{n\ge1}
\frac1{n!}
\sum_{\Gamma_1,\ldots,\Gamma_n\in\mathcal P_\Lambda}
\phi_T(\Gamma_1,\ldots,\Gamma_n)
\prod_{i=1}^n\zeta_t(\Gamma_i;J),
}
$$

where $\phi_T$ is the usual Ursell coefficient of the incompatibility graph.
For every coarse block $x$, the sum of all connected clusters touching $x$ is
bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\mathcal C\ni x}
\left|
\phi_T(\mathcal C)
\prod_{\Gamma\in\mathcal C}\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)
\right|
\le
C_{KP}e^{-\kappa(t,J)}.
}
$$

The constant $C_{KP}$ is independent of the volume and cutoff once the small
heat-kernel window has been entered.

Proof.  Theorem 10.28g2.6 proves the standard Kotecky-Preiss condition on the
finite incompatibility graph:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{\Gamma:\Gamma\not\sim\Gamma_0}
|\zeta_t(\Gamma;J)|e^{\lambda|\Gamma|}
\le
\lambda|\Gamma_0|.
}
$$

The finite-volume KP theorem then gives absolute convergence of the cluster
expansion and the rooted cluster bound.  The constants are volume-independent
because the block degree, the incompatibility range, the polymer weights, and
the KP margin are uniform in $\Lambda$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Corollary 10.28g2.7: LF Receipt For The Heat-Kernel Branch

For the heat-kernel regulator, bounded positive-flow source packets, and a
cofinal cutoff sequence satisfying:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n a_n^{\kappa_{LF}}<\infty,
}
$$

the large-field clause LF of subsection 10.28g is discharged in the following
precise sense:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n
\sup_x
\sum_{\Gamma\ni x}
\exp(\lambda|\Gamma|)
|\zeta_{t(a_n)}(\Gamma;J)|
<
\infty.
}
$$

Proof.  This is exactly the power estimate of Theorem 10.28g2.6 summed over
the cofinal cutoff sequence.

$$
\square
$$

###### What This Does And Does Not Close

The theorem above executes the large-field part of M2 for the heat-kernel
branch at positive flow.  The finite-energy margin is supplied by Theorem
10.28g2.2b2.  The receipt now consists of a heat-kernel bad-plaquette cost, a
plaquette-time replacement constant, a connected Ursell polymer activity, a
lattice-animal entropy constant, and a Kotecky-Preiss margin.

The formerly compressed steps are now explicit: Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a0 gives the
finite tree-gauge collar coercivity constants, Lemma 10.28g2.2b1a gives the
finite collar minimizer gap, Lemma 10.28g2.2b1v gives the uniform compact-collar
heat-kernel Laplace principle, Lemma 10.28g2.2b3 gives the bounded exploration
and charging map, and Lemma 10.28g2.3a1 gives the finite-volume dependency-graph
tree bound.

It does not yet close the whole C0 open core.  Three limitations remain.

First, the theorem assumes the asymptotically free heat-kernel trajectory enters
the small-time window with the stated logarithmic bound.  That input belongs to
M1.

Second, the theorem controls large-field polymer activities for bounded
positive-flow sources.  The zero-flow transfer of this estimate belongs to M3.

Third, the theorem gives suppression of the large-field complement but does
not by itself produce a nonzero fixed-scale continuum readout.  The UV readout
is M4-UV; full nontriviality is IR2.

Thus the current status after Execution I is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{LF}_{heat,\tau>0}
\quad
\hbox{closed at Execution I; the M1 receipt is discharged in Execution III}.
}
$$

The next attack target is M1: upgrade the packetwise small-field response
chart to a packet-uniform flowed RG chart using the large-field receipt above.

##### 10.28g3: Execution II -- Projective Bootstrap For U And ER

Searchable execution-II tag:

`V4P39-C0-EXECUTE-U-ER-PROJECTIVE-BOOTSTRAP`.

This subsection executes the functional-analytic part of:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{U+ER}.
}
$$

It proves that once the one-step flowed RG receipts are uniform and summable,
the continuum source functional is packet-independent and the error ledger is
summable.  The analytic construction of those one-step receipts remains the
M1 burden.

###### Definition 10.28g3.1: Projective Packet System

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal P}_1\subset{\mathcal P}_2\subset\cdots
}
$$

be the cofinal finite source-packet tower.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_m
}
$$

be the finite-dimensional real Banach space generated by the gauge-invariant
flowed source coordinates in packet $m$.  The packet tower is not arbitrary.
It is obtained by choosing a single separable positive-flow source envelope:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}
}
$$

on a fixed physical support radius $R$, Sobolev order $k$, and flow time
$\tau>0$, and then taking finite coordinate projections in a Riesz frame of
that envelope.  This envelope is a source/test-function space on Euclidean
space, not an assumed continuum Yang-Mills state.  Thus:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_m=P_m{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow},
\qquad
P_m\to I\hbox{ strongly on }{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}.
}
$$

The restriction map is:

$$
\boxed{
\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}:{\mathcal A}_{m'}\to{\mathcal A}_m
\qquad
(m'\ge m).
}
$$

The maps are required to be contractive:

$$
\boxed{
\|\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}X\|_m\le \|X\|_{m'}.
}
$$

The projective local source space is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_{loc}
=
\varprojlim_m{\mathcal A}_m.
}
$$

It carries the locally convex projective-limit topology generated by the
seminorms:

$$
\boxed{
p_m(X)=\|\pi_m X\|_m.
}
$$

The response object below is the finite source jet of the logarithmic
