generating functional through the fixed response order.  Equivalently, it is a
finite collection of continuous multilinear forms on ${\mathcal A}_m$.  All
projective-limit statements are made in this finite-jet locally convex
topology.

The finite response order is also part of the projective data.  For each
integer $r_0\ge1$, let:

$$
\boxed{
J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_m
}
$$

denote the source jets through order $r_0$ on packet $m$.  If $r_1\ge r_0$,
let:

$$
\boxed{
\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}:J^{r_1}{\mathcal A}_m\to J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_m
}
$$

be jet truncation.  The full positive-flow source object is therefore the
double projective system:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal A}_{loc}^{jet}
=
\varprojlim_{m,r_0}J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_m.
}
$$

All limits below are first proved at fixed $(m,r_0)$ and then assembled by the
two compatibility maps $\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}$ and $\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}$.
This is the point at which finite-jet control is upgraded to control of the
whole formal source functional.

###### Definition 10.28g3.2: Uniform One-Step RG Receipt

At cutoff scale $n$, let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}:J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_{m,n}\to{\mathbb R}
}
$$

be the finite-volume finite-cutoff flowed response jet.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
B_n:{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}\to{\mathcal A}_{m,n}
}
$$

be the one-step blocking map.  The map $B_n$ is constructed on the raw OS source
frame in Definition 10.28g3.2a, is shown to respect the physical quotients in
Lemma 10.28g3.2b, and is given a finite-jet operator norm bound in Lemma
10.28g3.2c.  Its packet and response-order functoriality is Lemma 10.28g3.2d.

A uniform one-step RG receipt consists of constants, at each fixed response
order $r_0$:

$$
\boxed{
C<\infty,\qquad \kappa>0,\qquad 0<q<1
}
$$

and errors:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_n=C a_n^\kappa
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n\epsilon_n<\infty.
}
$$

For every fixed physical support radius and every packet inside that support,
and every fixed response order, the following two estimates hold:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{(r_0)}-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_n\|_{m,r_0}
\le
\epsilon_n.
}
$$

The norm $\|\cdot\|_{m,r_0}$ is the dual finite-jet norm induced by the raw
OS-frame packet norm and, when estimates are iterated, by the pulled-back
blocking norm of Lemma 10.28g3.2c.

The second estimate is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}
=
{\mathcal R}_{n,m'}^{(r_0)}\circ\iota_{m'\leftarrow m}.
}
$$

Here $\iota_{m'\leftarrow m}$ is the canonical inclusion of packet coordinates
with all spectator coordinates set to zero.  This is exact functoriality of
finite source jets at the origin: padding a source by zero spectator
coordinates cannot change derivatives taken only in the smaller packet.  No
claim is made for nonzero spectator sources.

The same exact functoriality holds under response-order truncation:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}
=
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_1)}\circ\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}
\qquad
(r_1\ge r_0).
}
$$

The constants may depend on the fixed response order, but for every $r_0$ the
cutoff sequence is chosen cofinally so that the corresponding error series is
summable.  A diagonal choice over $r_0$ is allowed only after all fixed-order
estimates have been proved.

###### Definition 10.28g3.2a: Raw OS-Frame Blocking Map

The map $B_n$ in Definition 10.28g3.2 is not an abstract source-space
identification.  It is the finite-jet pullback induced by a raw OS-frame
operator.

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau,n}^{raw}
}
$$

be the Hilbert-Banach source envelope at cutoff $a_n$, generated by
gauge-covariant positive-flow test tensors with physical support in the fixed
radius $R$, Sobolev order $k$, and flow time $\tau>0$.  Its norm is the flowed
Sobolev/source norm used in the finite OS frame theorem.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
P_{m,n}:{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau,n}^{raw}\to{\mathcal A}_{m,n}
}
$$

be the cutoff-$n$ Riesz-frame projection onto the finite packet coordinates.
The raw one-step blocking operator is:

$$
\boxed{
B_n^{raw}
=
{\mathsf G}_{n}\,
{\mathsf H}_{\tau,n\leftarrow n+1}\,
{\mathsf S}_{b,n\leftarrow n+1}\,
{\mathsf I}_{n\leftarrow n+1}.
}
$$

Here:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{rcl}
{\mathsf I}_{n\leftarrow n+1}
&=&
\hbox{piecewise-smooth interpolation of the coarse source to the fine lattice},
\\[2mm]
{\mathsf S}_{b,n\leftarrow n+1}
&=&
\hbox{canonical rescaling by the block factor }b,
\\[2mm]
{\mathsf H}_{\tau,n\leftarrow n+1}
&=&
\hbox{positive-flow heat transport at the fixed physical flow time},
\\[2mm]
{\mathsf G}_{n}
&=&
\hbox{finite block gauge averaging/parallel-transport projection}.
\end{array}
}
$$

The source-space blocking map in Definition 10.28g3.2 is:

$$
\boxed{
B_n
=
P_{m,n}B_n^{raw}\iota_{m,n+1},
}
$$

where $\iota_{m,n+1}:{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}\to
{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau,n+1}^{raw}$ inserts the finite packet coordinates into
the raw frame.

The induced map on jets is the symmetric tensor functor:

$$
\boxed{
J^{r_0}B_n
=
\bigoplus_{\ell=0}^{r_0}{\rm Sym}^{\ell}(B_n).
}
$$

In all formulas below, ${\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_n$ means
${\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ J^{r_0}B_n$.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.2b: Ward And Typed Quotient Compatibility Of Blocking

The raw blocking map descends to the Ward, vacuum, and typed physical quotient:

$$
\boxed{
B_n^{raw}({\mathcal N}_{Ward,n+1}+{\mathcal N}_{vac,n+1}
+{\mathcal N}_{typed,n+1})
\subset
{\mathcal N}_{Ward,n}+{\mathcal N}_{vac,n}+{\mathcal N}_{typed,n}.
}
$$

Therefore it induces bounded maps:

$$
\boxed{
\overline B_n:
{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}/({\rm Ward}+{\rm vac}+{\rm typed})
\longrightarrow
{\mathcal A}_{m,n}/({\rm Ward}+{\rm vac}+{\rm typed}),
}
$$

and the same statement holds for finite jets:

$$
\boxed{
J^{r_0}\overline B_n
=
\bigoplus_{\ell=0}^{r_0}{\rm Sym}^{\ell}(\overline B_n).
}
$$

Proof.  Each factor in $B_n^{raw}$ is compatible with the quotient.  The
interpolation and canonical rescaling send a gauge variation to the rescaled
gauge variation.  Heat transport is gauge covariant at positive flow time, so it
commutes with the Ward differential and maps Ward descendants to Ward
descendants.  The block gauge average ${\mathsf G}_n$ is the conditional
expectation onto block gauge invariants; it annihilates pure gauge components
and preserves the gauge-invariant quotient.  Vacuum constants remain constants.
Typed sector labels are carried by center character, topological window, finite
Casimir window, and boundary-flux label; interpolation, heat transport, block
rescaling, and gauge averaging preserve those labels or map them into the
finite typed refinement declared at the finer scale.  Hence no typed vector can
be converted into an untyped physical coordinate by blocking.

Because the null subspaces are mapped into null subspaces, the universal
property of quotient spaces gives $\overline B_n$.  Taking symmetric tensor
powers preserves the quotient relation at every finite jet order.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.2c: Finite-Jet Operator Norm Bound For Blocking

For every fixed physical support radius, positive flow time, Sobolev order,
source radius, and response order $r_0$, there is a constant $C_B(r_0)<\infty$,
independent of packet index, cutoff, and volume, such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|B_n\|_{{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}\to{\mathcal A}_{m,n}}
\le
C_B(1),
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\|J^{r_0}B_n\|_{J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}\to J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_{m,n}}
\le
C_B(r_0).
}
$$

Fix a reference scale $n_*$.  For $n\ge n_*$ define the blocking-adapted
pulled-back jet norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|X\|_{J^{r_0},n}^{pb}
=
\|J^{r_0}B_{n_*,n}X\|_{J^{r_0},n_*},
\qquad
B_{n_*,n}=B_{n_*}B_{n_*+1}\cdots B_{n-1}.
}
$$

In this pulled-back norm the one-step blocking map is exactly contractive:

$$
\boxed{
\|J^{r_0}B_nX\|_{J^{r_0},n}^{pb}
\le
\|X\|_{J^{r_0},n+1}^{pb}.
}
$$

Proof.  The interpolation operator has a uniform Sobolev bound because the
block shape, overlap multiplicity, and interpolation stencil are fixed.  The
canonical rescaling is an isometry after the engineering dimensions included in
the source norm are applied.  Positive heat transport is contractive on the
flowed Sobolev scale by the heat-kernel semigroup estimate.  The finite block
gauge average is a conditional expectation and hence has norm at most one on
the gauge-invariant OS source norm.  The Riesz-frame projections and insertions
have the cutoff- and packet-uniform upper frame bound supplied by the finite
OS-frame theorem:

$$
\boxed{
\|P_{m,n}\|\le C_U,
\qquad
\|\iota_{m,n}\|\le C_U.
}
$$

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
\|B_n\|
\le
C_U^2 C_{int} C_{res}
=
C_B(1).
}
$$

The finite jet map is the direct sum of symmetric tensor powers of $B_n$.
Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\rm Sym}^{\ell}(B_n)\|
\le
\|B_n\|^\ell
\le
C_B(1)^\ell,
\qquad
0\le\ell\le r_0.
}
$$

Taking the maximum over $\ell\le r_0$ gives the displayed finite-jet bound.
The contractive form follows from the definition of the pulled-back norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|J^{r_0}B_nX\|_{J^{r_0},n}^{pb}
=
\|J^{r_0}B_{n_*,n}J^{r_0}B_nX\|_{J^{r_0},n_*}
=
\|J^{r_0}B_{n_*,n+1}X\|_{J^{r_0},n_*}.
}
$$

No constant depends on the packet: the only packet-dependent maps are the
Riesz-frame projection and insertion, and their norms are bounded by the same
upper frame constant.  The ordinary finite-jet norm gives uniform boundedness;
the pulled-back norm gives the exact contraction used in the Cauchy argument.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.2d: Packet And Jet Functoriality Of Blocking

After passing to the shared refinement schedule of the finite OS-frame theorem,
blocking commutes with packet restriction and response-order truncation.  For
$m'\ge m$:

$$
\boxed{
\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}\,B_{n,m'}
=
B_{n,m}\,\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}.
}
$$

On finite jets:

$$
\boxed{
J^{r_0}\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}\,J^{r_0}B_{n,m'}
=
J^{r_0}B_{n,m}\,J^{r_0}\pi_{m\leftarrow m'}.
}
$$

For response-order truncation:

$$
\boxed{
\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}\,J^{r_1}B_n
=
J^{r_0}B_n\,\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}.
}
$$

Proof.  The packet tower is built from one raw source frame by nested coordinate
projections.  The shared refinement schedule includes, for every retained
coarse packet vector, all fine-frame elements generated by interpolation,
rescaling, heat transport, and gauge averaging.  Therefore blocking a larger
packet and then restricting to the smaller packet gives the same retained
coordinates as restricting first and then blocking.  The equality is exact on
zero-spectator source jets, which is the only functoriality used in Definition
10.28g3.2.  Symmetric tensor powers preserve this equality.  Jet truncation
commutes with blocking because $J^{r_0}B_n$ is the degree-by-degree symmetric
tensor functor of the same linear map $B_n$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.3: Cauchy Property At Fixed Packet

For every fixed packet $m$, the sequence:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}
}
$$

is Cauchy in one fixed physical source norm after pullback to a reference
scale.

Proof.  Fix a reference physical scale $n_*$ larger than the support scale of
the sources, and write:

$$
\boxed{
B_{n_*,n}=B_{n_*}B_{n_*+1}\cdots B_{n-1}.
}
$$

Define the pulled-back finite-cutoff jet:

$$
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}
=
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_{n_*,n}.
}
$$

All norms are now measured on $J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_m$ at the fixed scale
$n_*$.  Iterating the one-step estimate gives, for $N>M\ge n_*$:

$$
\boxed{
\|\widehat{\mathcal R}_{N,m}^{(r_0)}
-\widehat{\mathcal R}_{M,m}^{(r_0)}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
\sum_{n=M}^{N-1}\epsilon_n.
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g3.2c gives the finite-jet bound for the blocking maps, and in the
blocking-adapted pulled-back norm their induced maps are contractive.  The
pullback therefore puts every cutoff in the same Banach norm.
The right-hand side tends to zero as $M$ tends to infinity because the error
sequence is summable.  This proves the fixed-scale Cauchy property.  The
unpulled functional is recovered by composing the limit with the fixed blocking
map.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.4: Projective Compatibility Of Limits

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{\infty,m}^{(r_0)}
=
\lim_{n\to\infty}\widehat{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}.
}
$$

Then for every $m'\ge m$:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{\infty,m}^{(r_0)}
=
{\mathcal R}_{\infty,m'}^{(r_0)}\circ\iota_{m'\leftarrow m}.
}
$$

Proof.  Apply exact finite-packet functoriality at every cutoff and then send
$n$ to infinity.  The two finite-packet limits exist by Lemma 10.28g3.3, so the
equality passes to the limit.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.4a: Response-Order Compatibility Of Limits

For every $r_1\ge r_0$ and every packet $m$:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{\infty,m}^{(r_0)}
=
{\mathcal R}_{\infty,m}^{(r_1)}
\circ
\theta_{r_0\leftarrow r_1}.
}
$$

Proof.  At finite cutoff, response-order truncation is exact because both
objects are source jets of the same finite-volume logarithmic generating
functional.  The fixed-scale pullback in Lemma 10.28g3.3 commutes with jet
truncation.  Passing to the Cauchy limit preserves the identity.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g3.5: Projective Continuum Source Functional

Assume the uniform one-step RG receipt of Definition 10.28g3.2.  Then there is
a unique continuous projective source functional:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_\infty:{\mathcal A}_{loc}^{jet}\to{\mathbb R}
}
$$

whose restriction to every finite packet and every finite response order is
${\mathcal R}_{\infty,m}^{(r_0)}$.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g3.3 constructs the finite-packet limits.  Lemma 10.28g3.4
proves compatibility under packet restriction, and Lemma 10.28g3.4a proves
compatibility under response-order truncation.  Since
${\mathcal A}_{loc}^{jet}$ carries the double projective-limit locally convex
topology generated by the packet seminorms and finite jet orders, the universal
property gives a unique continuous projective source functional.  Continuity
follows from the uniform finite-packet dual bounds in Definition 10.28g3.2:
each finite multilinear component is bounded on the corresponding finite
product of seminorm balls, and compatibility makes the bound independent of the
representative packet.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.5a: Cofinal Response-Order Diagonal

For each fixed response order $r_0$, suppose the one-step receipt has an error
sequence:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{n,r_0}=C_{r_0}a_n^{\kappa_{r_0}}
}
$$

with positive $\kappa_{r_0}$.  Then there is a cofinal cutoff subsequence for
which:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n \epsilon_{n,r_0}<\infty
\qquad
\hbox{for every fixed }r_0.
}
$$

On that subsequence, the finite-jet limits assemble into a compatible
projective family over all response orders.

Proof.  Since every $\kappa_{r_0}$ is positive, choose the cutoff subsequence
so that:

$$
\boxed{
C_{r_0}a_n^{\kappa_{r_0}}\le 2^{-n-r_0}
\qquad
\hbox{for }n\ge r_0.
}
$$

This is possible because the cutoff tends to zero.  The resulting series is
summable for every fixed $r_0$.  Lemma 10.28g3.4a gives compatibility under
jet truncation, so the diagonal subsequence produces the full formal
positive-flow source functional rather than a single fixed-order jet.

$$
\square
$$

###### Corollary 10.28g3.6: U And ER From The One-Step Receipt

The uniformity clause U and the error-summability clause ER close at positive
flow if the uniform one-step RG receipt holds.

Proof.  U is exactly the packet-independent existence and compatibility of
Theorem 10.28g3.5.  ER is exactly the summability of the cutoff errors in
Definition 10.28g3.2, transported through Lemma 10.28g3.3.  Lemma 10.28g3.5a
performs the only diagonal step, and it is over response order, not over
packets or regulators.  No compactness subsequence or packet-dependent
diagonal choice is used.

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{one\mbox{-}step\ RG\ receipt}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{U}_{\tau>0}+\mathrm{ER}_{\tau>0}.
}
$$

$$
\square
$$

###### Execution III: Heat-Kernel One-Step RG Receipt

Searchable execution-III tag:

`V4P39-C0-EXECUTE-M1-HEAT-KERNEL-ONE-STEP-RG-RECEIPT`.

Execution II closes the abstract projective part of U and ER.  The remaining
analytic task is to prove the one-step receipt in Definition 10.28g3.2 from the
regulated heat-kernel measure.  This subsection supplies that proof for bounded
positive-flow source packets.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7: Positive-Flow Packet Compactness

Fix a physical support radius, a positive flow time, a Sobolev order, and a
bounded source radius.  The unit ball of gauge-invariant positive-flow source
insertions is compact in the response norm used by Definition 10.28g3.2 after
restriction to any finite response order.  Consequently every cofinal packet
tower inside those physical bounds admits finite nets with constants
independent of the packet index.

Proof.  Positive Yang-Mills heat flow turns every local source insertion into a
smooth gauge-covariant test functional over a fixed physical neighborhood.  The
important point is that the compactness is not taken on a growing lattice
coordinate cube and does not assume the continuum YM measure.  It is taken in
the external flowed source/test Sobolev ball on the fixed physical support.
Heat-flow smoothing gives uniform bounds in a Sobolev order strictly above the
order tested by the response norm.  Rellich compactness and Arzela-Ascoli
therefore give a compact unit ball in the lower response norm.

The lattice functionals at cutoff $a_n$ are restrictions of this compact
continuum flowed ball to the lattice cylinder algebra, with uniformly bounded
sampling maps.  Gauge averaging is a contraction, so it preserves the compact
set.  Finite response order means only finitely many source derivatives are
tested.  Therefore a finite net chosen in the continuum flowed response norm
controls every cutoff and every packet in the tower with the same constants.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g3.7q0: Finite-Cutoff OS Sector Projection

At finite lattice spacing $a$ and finite volume $L$, let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal H}_{a,L;E,R,\tau}^{phys}
}
$$

be the OS Hilbert quotient generated by positive-time gauge-invariant
positive-flow insertions of support radius at most $R$, flow time $\tau$, and
transfer energy at most $E$, after Ward, vacuum, and typed zero-response
directions have been quotiented.  This is a finite-cutoff object: it is built
before any continuum limit is taken.

For a packet index $m$, define the elementary contractive cutoffs:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\Pi_{C_m}&=\hbox{Peter-Weyl projection to Casimir at most }C_m,\\
\Pi_{\Lambda_m}&=\mathbf 1_{[0,\Lambda_m]}(H_{a,L}),\\
\Pi_{D_m}&=\hbox{projection to flowed source derivatives/orders at most }D_m,\\
\Pi_{R_m}&=\hbox{projection to infrared smearings in radius }R_m,\\
\Pi_{d_m}&=\hbox{projection to the collar separated from the boundary by }d_m.
\end{aligned}
}
$$

The product:

$$
\boxed{
Q_m=\Pi_{d_m}\Pi_{R_m}\Pi_{D_m}\Pi_{\Lambda_m}\Pi_{C_m}
}
$$

need not be an orthogonal projection, because the cutoffs need not commute.
Let ${\mathcal V}_m^{sec}$ be the finite-dimensional subspace generated by the
range of $Q_m$ and by the finite center/topological typed receipts below the
same cutoffs.  Define:

$$
\boxed{
P_m^{sec}
=
\hbox{the OS-orthogonal projection onto }{\mathcal V}_m^{sec}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
\|P_m^{sec}\|_{OS\to OS}=1,
\qquad
\|(I-P_m^{sec})\Psi\|_{OS}\le \|\Psi-Q_m\Psi\|_{OS}.
}
$$

This definition removes any need for the elementary cutoffs to commute.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q0a: Finite Raw Algebra Density

At fixed lattice spacing, finite volume, positive flow time, finite support
radius, and finite sector cutoffs, the raw positive-flow algebra used in
Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 is dense in the finite OS sector subspace.

More explicitly, let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak X}_{a,L}^{R,\tau}
}
$$

be the compact finite-volume gauge-configuration space restricted to the
positive-flow support collar and quotiented by finite gauge transformations.
Adjoin the finite retained center, topological, and typed labels from
Definition 10.28g3.7q0.  The resulting compact Hausdorff space is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak X}_{a,L,m}^{sec}.
}
$$

Let ${\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k,m}$ be the complex unital algebra generated
by:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{l}
\hbox{matrix coefficients of retained Wilson loops and flowed parallel
transports,}\\
\hbox{flowed curvature polynomials smeared by rational smooth test functions,}\\
\hbox{center characters of the retained finite center group,}\\
\hbox{smooth topological windows approximating the retained Borel windows,}\\
\hbox{finite-volume infrared smearings below the retained radius cutoff.}
\end{array}
}
$$

Then ${\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k,m}$ is uniformly dense in:

$$
\boxed{
C({\mathfrak X}_{a,L,m}^{sec})^{G}
}
$$

and hence dense in the finite OS norm induced by the heat-kernel measure.

Proof.  The finite collar has only finitely many compact link variables.  By the
Peter-Weyl theorem, matrix coefficients of products of link variables span a
uniformly dense subalgebra of continuous functions on the compact group product.
Gauge averaging is a contractive conditional expectation onto the
gauge-invariant subalgebra, so gauge-averaged Wilson/parallel-transport matrix
coefficients separate gauge orbits.

The retained center labels form a finite abelian group; its characters separate
points.  The retained typed labels form a finite discrete algebra; coordinate
idempotents separate points.  The flowed topological charge at fixed cutoff is a
bounded continuous multiplication operator on the compact configuration space.
For the retained separated Borel windows, Urysohn functions with rational
coefficients approximate their indicators in the finite Radon measure and in OS
matrix elements.  Infrared smearings below the finite radius cutoff are ordinary
continuous cylinder functions on the same compact space.

Therefore the raw algebra is a unital self-adjoint subalgebra that separates the
points of ${\mathfrak X}_{a,L,m}^{sec}$.  Stone-Weierstrass gives uniform
density in the continuous gauge-invariant sector algebra.  Since the
finite-volume heat-kernel measure is a positive finite Radon measure and the OS
inner product is built from this measure by reflection-positive finite
integration, uniform approximation implies OS-norm approximation.  Zero-norm
directions are quotiented after the approximation, so density passes to the
finite OS sector subspace.

This is the finite compact-group density input used by the frame construction.
It is not a density statement about a pre-existing continuum field algebra.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q0b: Elementary Sector-Tail Estimates

The five elementary cutoffs in Definition 10.28g3.7q0 have explicit finite OS
tails.  For every vector $\Psi$ in the finite-energy positive-flow quotient:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
\|(I-\Pi_{C_m})\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
&\le C_1e^{-2\tau C_m}\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2},\\
\|(I-\Pi_{\Lambda_m})\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
&\le C_2\Lambda_m^{-1}E\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2},\\
\|(I-\Pi_{D_m})\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
&\le C_3D_m^{-2(k-k_0)}\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2},\\
\|(I-\Pi_{R_m})\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
&\le C_4R_m^{-2s}\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2},\\
\|(I-\Pi_{d_m})\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
&\le C_5e^{-d_m/\xi}\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}.
\end{aligned}
}
$$

The constants are independent of cutoff and volume once the physical support,
positive flow time, finite energy, Sobolev order, and response order are fixed.

Proof.  The Casimir estimate is finite Peter-Weyl analysis.  Positive flow
multiplies each representation label by a heat factor
$\exp[-\tau C_2(\lambda)]$, so the tail above $C_m$ has the displayed
exponential norm bound.

The transfer-energy estimate is spectral calculus.  On the spectral subspace
with transfer energy at most $E$, Markov's inequality for the positive transfer
Hamiltonian gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|(I-\mathbf 1_{[0,\Lambda_m]}(H))\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
\Lambda_m^{-1}\langle \Psi,H\Psi\rangle
\le
\Lambda_m^{-1}E\|\Psi\|_{OS}^{2}.
}
$$

The derivative/order tail is the usual positive-flow Sobolev tail.  The
response norm tests derivatives only up to order $k_0<k$; truncating the
positive-flow Sobolev expansion at order $D_m$ leaves a tail bounded by
$D_m^{-2(k-k_0)}$.

The infrared smearing tail is the finite-energy Sobolev tail of the fixed
support envelope.  For every fixed $s$ below the Sobolev margin, truncating
smearings outside radius $R_m$ gives $R_m^{-2s}$.

Finally, the boundary collar estimate follows from finite propagation of the
positive-flow kernel at fixed flow time together with the finite-volume transfer
bound.  Contributions reaching the boundary collar have length at least $d_m$,
and the finite positive transfer matrix gives the exponential factor
$e^{-d_m/\xi}$.

All five estimates are finite-cutoff estimates.  They are applied before any
continuum limit, and the constants are controlled by fixed physical quantities,
not by packet size.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q: Quantitative Finite-Energy Sector Exhaustion

Fix a physical support radius $R$, positive flow time $\tau$, finite response
order $r_0$, Sobolev order $k$, source radius, and finite OS energy cutoff
$E$.  Let ${\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}$ be the corresponding finite-energy
positive-flow physical quotient after Ward, vacuum, and typed zero-response
directions have been removed.  There is a cofinal sector packet projection:

$$
\boxed{
P_m^{sec}:{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}\to{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|(I-P_m^{sec})\Psi\|_{OS}
\le
\eta_m(E,R,\tau,k,r_0)\|\Psi\|_{OS},
\qquad
\eta_m(E,R,\tau,k,r_0)\downarrow0.
}
$$

More explicitly, one may choose the packet cutoffs so that:

$$
\boxed{
\eta_m^2
\le
C_1e^{-2\tau C_m}
+C_2\Lambda_m^{-1}E
+C_3D_m^{-2(k-k_0)}
+C_4R_m^{-2s}
+C_5e^{-d_m/\xi}.
}
$$

Here $C_m$ is the representation-Casimir cutoff, $\Lambda_m$ is the transfer
energy cutoff, $D_m$ is the local derivative/order cutoff, $R_m$ is the
infrared smearing radius, and $d_m$ is the distance from the support collar to
the finite-volume boundary.

Proof.  Work first in the finite-cutoff OS quotient
${\mathcal H}_{a,L;E,R,\tau}^{phys}$ of Definition 10.28g3.7q0.  The
elementary cutoffs $\Pi_{C_m}$, $\Pi_{\Lambda_m}$, $\Pi_{D_m}$, $\Pi_{R_m}$,
and $\Pi_{d_m}$ are contractions in the finite OS norm.  Although they need
not commute, the telescoping identity gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|\Psi-Q_m\Psi\|_{OS}
\le
\sum_j
\|(I-\Pi_j)\Psi_j\|_{OS},
\qquad
\|\Psi_j\|_{OS}\le\|\Psi\|_{OS}.
}
$$

Here the index $j$ runs over the five elementary cutoffs and each $\Psi_j$ is
the vector obtained after applying the preceding contractive cutoffs.  Since
$P_m^{sec}$ is the OS-orthogonal projection onto a subspace containing the
range of $Q_m$, it is enough to bound the five elementary tails.  Lemma
10.28g3.7q0b supplies these five estimates with constants uniform in cutoff and
volume.

Center and topological labels are discrete in the finite-volume cylinder
algebra.  Below fixed Casimir, support, and energy cutoffs only finitely many
such labels can contribute to the finite response jet.  They are inserted into
${\mathcal V}_m^{sec}$ before the orthogonal projection $P_m^{sec}$ is applied.
Lemma 10.28g3.7q0a gives density of the raw finite sector algebra in this
finite-dimensional sector subspace, so adding the finite sector receipts
captures the retained center, topological, and typed components rather than
postulating them.
Combining the five contractive tail bounds by the telescoping estimate gives
the displayed $\eta_m$.  The constants are uniform as $a\downarrow0$ and
$L\uparrow\infty$ because all estimates are made at fixed physical support,
fixed flow time, and fixed finite energy before the cofinal limits are taken.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q1a: Positive-Flow Sampling And Raw Gram Refinement

Let ${\mathcal F}$ be a fixed finite list of cutoff-independent raw
positive-flow functionals from ${\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}$.  For each
cutoff and volume define the finite OS Gram matrix:

$$
\boxed{
G_{a,L}^{\mathcal F}(F,G)
=
\langle I_{a,L}F,I_{a,L}G\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

If $a'\le a$ and $L'\ge L$, then:

$$
\boxed{
\|G_{a,L}^{\mathcal F}-G_{a',L'}^{\mathcal F}\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
C_{\mathcal F}
\left(
a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}
\right).
}
$$

Equivalently, for every coefficient vector $c$ supported on the finite packet:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
\left\|\sum_{F\in{\mathcal F}}c_F I_{a,L}F\right\|_{OS}^{2}
-
\left\|\sum_{F\in{\mathcal F}}c_F I_{a',L'}F\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\right|
\le
C_{\mathcal F}
\left(
a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}
\right)
\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}.
}
$$

Proof.  The statement is finite-dimensional.  Each raw positive-flow functional
has fixed physical support, fixed positive flow time, and fixed response order.
Positive flow makes the link-coordinate representative smooth with all
derivatives up to the required order bounded uniformly on the compact group
collar.  Replacing continuum paths, smearing kernels, and flowed curvature
coordinates by the lattice heat-kernel representatives therefore gives the
finite-element estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\|I_{a,L}F-I_{a',L'}F\|_{C^{r}}
\le
C_F a^{\kappa_{disc}}
}
$$

on every collar that contains the support of $F$ and its reflected copy.

The OS form is an integral of the product of one positive-time representative
and the reflected representative against the finite heat-kernel measure.  On a
fixed collar, heat-kernel convolution and the finite plaquette density give a
common smooth density with uniformly bounded derivatives.  The difference
between the two cutoff measures on the collar is therefore bounded by the same
local discretization order.  Exterior plaquettes can affect the collar OS form
only through paths reaching the boundary collar.  The finite positive transfer
matrix and the fixed positive flow time give:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
\int_{\Lambda_L}H\,d\mu_{a,L}
-
\int_{\Lambda_{L'}}H\,d\mu_{a',L'}
\right|
\le
C_H
\left(
a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}
\right)
}
$$

for every product $H$ drawn from the finite list of reflected packet products.
Applying this to all entries of the finite Gram matrix and taking the finite
matrix operator norm gives the first display.  The quadratic-form display is the
same estimate written after contraction with $c$.

No continuum Hilbert space is used here.  This is a finite collar estimate for
smooth positive-flow cylinder functions and the heat-kernel regulator.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q1b: Stability Of Finite OS Sector Projections

Fix a packet cutoff $m$.  Choose a finite raw spanning list
${\mathcal B}_m\subset{\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}$ for the retained sector
algebra at that packet.  Lemma 10.28g3.7q1a makes the finite Gram matrices of
this list a Cauchy family along every cofinal refinement schedule.  Define the
limiting finite Gram matrix:

$$
\boxed{
G_{*,m}
=
\lim_{\nu\to\infty}
G_{a_\nu,L_\nu}^{{\mathcal B}_m}.
}
$$

Let ${\mathcal B}_m^{red}$ be a maximal pivot subset for the positive
semidefinite matrix $G_{*,m}$ after deleting its null space, and set:

$$
\boxed{
\gamma_m
=
\frac12
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
G_{*,m}^{red}
\right).
}
$$

Then $\gamma_m>0$, and for all sufficiently fine cutoffs:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}
\left(
G_{a,L}^{{\mathcal B}_m,red}
\right)
\ge
\gamma_m.
}
$$

Moreover:

$$
\boxed{
\|J_{a,L}^{a',L'}P_{m,a,L}^{sec}
-P_{m,a',L'}^{sec}J_{a,L}^{a',L'}\|_{OS\to OS}
\le
C_m\gamma_m^{-2}
\left(
a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}
\right).
}
$$

Proof.  By Lemma 10.28g3.7q0a, the retained sector space at fixed $m$ is the OS
closure of a finite raw sector algebra after the elementary cutoffs are applied.
Choose a finite spanning list ${\mathcal B}_m$ for this retained sector.  Lemma
10.28g3.7q1a gives convergence of its finite Gram matrices, entrywise and in
finite operator norm, to the positive semidefinite matrix $G_{*,m}$.  Pivoted
Cholesky on $G_{*,m}$ removes exactly the limiting null directions and produces
the reduced raw list ${\mathcal B}_m^{red}$.  The reduced limiting Gram matrix is
positive definite by construction, so its smallest eigenvalue is positive.  The
displayed lower bound for finite cutoffs follows from finite-dimensional
eigenvalue continuity once the cofinal tail is chosen.

At each such cutoff the reduced synthesis map is:

$$
\boxed{
S_{a,L}^{m}:\mathbb C^{N_m}\to{\mathcal H}_{a,L;E,R,\tau}^{phys},
\qquad
S_{a,L}^{m}c
=
\sum_{\alpha=1}^{N_m}c_\alpha[I_{a,L}B_\alpha].
}
$$

On the reduced range:

$$
\boxed{
P_{m,a,L}^{sec}
=
S_{a,L}^{m}
\left(
(S_{a,L}^{m})^{*}S_{a,L}^{m}
\right)^{-1}
(S_{a,L}^{m})^{*}.
}
$$

The inverse Gram matrices are uniformly bounded by $\gamma_m^{-1}$ on the
chosen cofinal tail.

For two cutoffs, write $G$ and $G'$ for the reduced Gram matrices.  The finite
resolvent identity gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|G^{-1}-(G')^{-1}\|
\le
\gamma_m^{-2}\|G-G'\|.
}
$$

The synthesis maps for the same raw list differ, after applying the refinement
map, only by the raw sampling error of Lemma 10.28g3.7q1a.  Substituting the two
projection formulae above and using the finite synthesis bounds gives the
displayed commutator estimate.  The constant may depend on the fixed packet
$m$, but not on later cutoff or volume once the cofinal tail has been chosen.

This is the finite-dimensional perturbation step that justifies using
OS-orthogonal sector projections under refinement.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q1: Direct-Limit Compatibility Of Sector Cutoffs

The finite-cutoff sector projections of Definition 10.28g3.7q0 are compatible
with the positive-flow OS direct limit.  More precisely, let:

$$
\boxed{
J_{a,L}^{a',L'}:
{\mathcal H}_{a,L;E,R,\tau}^{phys}
\to
{\mathcal H}_{a',L';E,R,\tau}^{phys}
}
$$

be the positive-flow lattice refinement and volume-extension map, with
$a'\le a$ and $L'\ge L$.  This map is not postulated abstractly: it is induced
by cutoff-independent raw positive-flow cylinder functionals.  If
$F$ is such a raw functional, then:

$$
\boxed{
J_{a,L}^{a',L'}[I_{a,L}F]=[I_{a',L'}F],
}
$$

where $I_{a,L}$ is the lattice sampling map for the heat-kernel positive-flow
observable at cutoff $(a,L)$.  The map is extended to the finite-energy packet
subspace by linearity and then to the packet closure by the OS norm.

For every fixed packet cutoff $m$:

$$
\boxed{
\|J_{a,L}^{a',L'}P_{m,a,L}^{sec}
-P_{m,a',L'}^{sec}J_{a,L}^{a',L'}\|_{OS\to OS}
\le
C_m(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}).
}
$$

Consequently the cofinal projections $P_m^{sec}$ define projections on the
positive-flow direct-limit OS Hilbert quotient, and the tail estimate of Lemma
10.28g3.7q survives the ordered limit:

$$
\boxed{
a\downarrow0,\qquad L\uparrow\infty,\qquad m\uparrow\infty.
}
$$

Proof.  Let ${\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}$ be the cutoff-independent algebra
generated by smooth positive-flow curvature polynomials, center loops,
topological windows, and infrared smearings at fixed physical support.  For
each cutoff $(a,L)$, the sampling map $I_{a,L}$ sends these raw generators to
finite lattice cylinder functions by replacing paths, smearings, and flowed
curvatures by their lattice heat-kernel representatives.

Lemma 10.28g3.7q1a gives the raw OS Gram comparison for every finite raw packet.
Thus finite raw packet norms are Cauchy under refinement and volume extension.
Reflection positivity makes the induced map on the finite raw packet quotient a
contraction up to the same comparison error; null representatives are quotiented
before completion.

The elementary cutoffs in Definition 10.28g3.7q0 are stable under the same raw
sampling comparison.  Peter-Weyl/Casimir truncation is functorial under
subdivision because the heat-kernel convolution semigroup preserves
representation labels below a fixed Casimir up to the positive-flow
discretization remainder.  Transfer-energy truncation is stable by the min-max
principle for the finite positive transfer matrices.  Derivative/order and
infrared smearing cutoffs are fixed in physical units, so their refinement
error is the positive-flow sampling error.  Boundary collars differ only by
paths reaching the finite-volume boundary.

Lemma 10.28g3.7q1b applies this finite Gram comparison to the reduced raw
spanning list of ${\mathcal V}_{m}^{sec}$ and gives the displayed projection
commutator.  The direct limit is therefore defined by a Cauchy family of finite
projections.  Taking the continuum and volume limits first at fixed $m$, and
only then sending the packet cutoffs cofinally outward, preserves the tail bound
printed in Lemma 10.28g3.7q.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7q2: Finite-Cutoff OS Frame Construction

The cofinal source frame used below can be constructed without first assuming a
limiting OS Hilbert space.  More precisely, there is a countable sequence of
cutoff-independent raw positive-flow functionals:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde F_1,\widetilde F_2,\ldots
\in
{\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}
}
$$

and a single cofinal refinement schedule:

$$
\boxed{
(a_\nu,L_\nu)_{\nu\ge1},
\qquad
a_\nu\downarrow0,
\qquad
L_\nu\uparrow\infty,
}
$$

such that for every finite prefix $m$ and every $\nu\ge m$:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\left(
\langle I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_i,
I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_j\rangle_{OS}
\right)_{1\le i,j\le m}
-I_m
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
2^{-\nu}.
}
$$

The refinement maps are compatible on the same prefixes:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
J_{a_\nu,L_\nu}^{a_{\nu+1},L_{\nu+1}}
\sum_{j=1}^{m}c_j[I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_j]
-
\sum_{j=1}^{m}c_j[I_{a_{\nu+1},L_{\nu+1}}\widetilde F_j]
\right\|_{OS}
\le
2^{-\nu}\|c\|_{\ell^2}.
}
$$

Finally, the closed span of the direct-limit Cauchy classes of this sequence
contains every sector packet projection $P_m^{sec}$ up to the tail $\eta_m$ of
Lemma 10.28g3.7q.

Proof.  Start with the countable raw sector-complete algebra
${\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}$ generated by rational positive-flow source
profiles, rational Wilson/curvature polynomial coefficients, rational center
loops, rational topological windows, and rational infrared smearings.  Enumerate
it as:

$$
\boxed{
G_1,G_2,\ldots .
}
$$

At finite cutoff and finite volume, the OS form on the span of the first $N$
raw generators is an ordinary finite positive semidefinite matrix.  Therefore
pivoted Cholesky, or equivalently finite Gram-Schmidt after quotienting the
finite null space, is a purely finite operation.  No continuum Hilbert space is
used.

The construction is inductive.  Suppose
$\widetilde F_1,\ldots,\widetilde F_{m-1}$ and a partial schedule have been
chosen.  Use the finite sector exhaustion of Lemma 10.28g3.7q at a very fine
cutoff to find a raw generator combination $H_m$ whose distance from the
finite-cutoff span of the previous vectors is at least $3/4$ and whose sector
support advances the cofinal cutoff list.  Orthogonalize $H_m$ against the
previous vectors at that finite cutoff and normalize it there.  Approximate the
resulting finite coefficients by rationals closely enough that the normalized
vector still has distance at least $2/3$ and all previous inner products change
by at most $2^{-m-4}$.

The raw vector produced by this rational finite-cutoff operation is declared to
be $\widetilde F_m$.  Because it is a finite rational combination of raw
generators, it is cutoff-independent.  Lemma 10.28g3.7q1a compares all its OS
inner products and all previous finite-prefix inner products under refinement:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
\langle I_{a,L}F,I_{a,L}G\rangle_{OS}
-
\langle I_{a',L'}F,I_{a',L'}G\rangle_{OS}
\right|
\le
C_{F,G}(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})
}
$$

for the finitely many raw vectors already selected.  Choose the next entries of
the cofinal schedule so that this bound is below $2^{-\nu-4}$ for all pairs in
the prefix $m\le\nu$.  This makes the finite-prefix Gram matrix stay within
$2^{-\nu}$ of the identity at every later scheduled cutoff.  The same estimate,
applied to the raw representatives before and after refinement, gives the
displayed compatibility of the refinement maps.

The induction also enforces cofinality.  At stage $m$ require that the finite
span of the selected vectors approximates the sector projection with cutoffs
$(C_m,\Lambda_m,D_m,R_m,d_m)$ up to the tail allowed in Lemma 10.28g3.7q.  This
is possible because Lemma 10.28g3.7q0a gives raw algebra density inside every
finite retained sector, Lemma 10.28g3.7q0b supplies the five elementary sector
tails, and Lemma 10.28g3.7q1b makes the retained finite sector projection stable
under refinement.  The diagonal schedule is chosen once, with the condition
$m\le\nu$, so no packet-dependent subsequence is introduced.

The direct-limit vector represented by each $\widetilde F_j$ is now defined as
the Cauchy family:

$$
\boxed{
\left([I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_j]\right)_{\nu\ge j}.
}
$$

The two displayed estimates make the finite linear combinations Cauchy in the
OS norm and give the limiting Gram matrix as the identity on every finite
prefix.  Thus the direct-limit OS frame is constructed from finite-cutoff
objects, and the limiting Hilbert quotient used below is the completion of
these Cauchy classes plus the cofinal sector closure, rather than an assumed
background space.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7aU: Uniform Cofinal Raw OS Frame Tower

There is a cofinal raw positive-flow packet tower:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak P}_m^{U}
=
\{\widetilde F_1,\ldots,\widetilde F_m\}
\subset{\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}
}
$$

such that the direct-limit OS classes of the infinite list
$\{\widetilde F_j\}_{j\ge1}$, constructed as finite-cutoff Cauchy families, form
a Parseval frame for the finite-energy positive-flow physical quotient:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\sum_jc_j[\widetilde F_j]_{*}
\right\|_{OS,*}^{2}
=
\sum_j|c_j|^2
}
$$

for every finitely supported coefficient family after Ward, vacuum, and typed
zero-response directions have been quotiented.  Moreover the finite-cutoff
sampling operators:

$$
\boxed{
T_{a,L}c
=
\sum_jc_j[I_{a,L}\widetilde F_j]
}
$$

obey the uniform packet-independent estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\|T_{a,L}^{*}T_{a,L}-I\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})
}
$$

on every finite prefix of the tower.  Hence every finite packet in this tower
has:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_m=1,
\qquad
C_m\lambda_m^{-1}\le C_U,
\qquad
C_m\lambda_m^{-1/2}\le C_U.
}
$$

Proof.  Use the raw vectors and the shared refinement schedule constructed in
Lemma 10.28g3.7q2.  That lemma performs the orthogonalization at finite cutoff,
freezes rational raw coefficients, and then proves cutoff-compatible Gram
stability along one cofinal schedule.  Therefore the direct-limit class
$[\widetilde F_j]_{*}$ is defined by the Cauchy family of finite-cutoff sampled
vectors, not by applying Gram-Schmidt in an assumed continuum Hilbert space.

For every finite prefix, Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 gives:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{\nu\to\infty}
\left(
\langle I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_i,
I_{a_\nu,L_\nu}\widetilde F_j\rangle_{OS}
\right)_{1\le i,j\le m}
=
I_m.
}
$$

Hence:

$$
\boxed{
\left\langle [\widetilde F_i]_{*},[\widetilde F_j]_{*}\right\rangle_{OS,*}
=
\delta_{ij}.
}
$$

The cofinality clause of Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 says that every sector projection
$P_m^{sec}$ is contained in the closed span of a sufficiently long prefix up to
the tail $\eta_m$ of Lemma 10.28g3.7q.  Since $\eta_m\downarrow0$, the closed
span of the constructed Cauchy classes is the finite-energy positive-flow
physical quotient after Ward, vacuum, and typed zero-response directions have
been removed.  The sequence is therefore Parseval for that quotient.

The uniform sampling estimate is stronger than entrywise convergence.  It is an
operator-norm sampling theorem on the positive-flow source Sobolev envelope, not
a compactness assertion about individual packet vectors.  Positive flow gives a
cutoff-independent bound:

$$
\boxed{
\|F\|_{H^{k}_{flow}(R,\tau)}
\le
C_{E,R,\tau,k}\|[F]_{*}\|_{OS,*}
}
$$

on the finite-energy, fixed-support positive-flow quotient.  The heat-kernel
lattice sampling map obeys the standard finite-element/heat-kernel comparison:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
\langle I_{a,L}F,I_{a,L}G\rangle_{OS}
-
\langle F,G\rangle_{OS,*}
\right|
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})
\|F\|_{H^{k}_{flow}}\|G\|_{H^{k}_{flow}} .
}
$$

This estimate is obtained from the finite-cutoff sampling comparison already
used in Lemma 10.28g3.7q2: the local heat-kernel parametrix on fixed physical
support, gauge averaging as a contraction, and the boundary collar estimate for
the finite volume.  Applying it to $F=\sum_j u_j\widetilde F_j$ and $G=F$, using
the finite-cutoff Parseval limit supplied by the schedule, gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\|u\|_{\ell^2}\le1,\;u\ {\rm finite}}
\left|
\|T_{a,L}u\|_{OS}^{2}-\|u\|_{\ell^2}^{2}
\right|
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}).
}
$$

Equivalently, the displayed operator norm bound holds on every finite prefix.
The constant depends only on the fixed physical support, positive flow time,
finite energy, Sobolev order, and response order, not on the packet index.  For
this tower the limiting Gram matrix on every finite prefix is the identity, so
$\lambda_m=1$ and the packet constants are uniformly bounded.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7aR: Cutoff-Compatible Raw Packet Normalization

For every finite raw packet:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak P}_m=\{F_{m,1},\ldots,F_{m,N_m}\}
\subset{\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}
}
$$

let:

$$
\boxed{
G^{raw}_{m,a,L;ij}
=
\langle I_{a,L}F_{m,i},I_{a,L}F_{m,j}\rangle_{OS}
}
$$

be its finite-cutoff OS Gram matrix after Ward, vacuum, and typed
zero-response directions have been quotiented.  Then:

$$
\boxed{
G^{raw}_{m,a,L}\longrightarrow G^{raw}_{m,*}
}
$$

in finite matrix norm as $a\downarrow0$ and $L\uparrow\infty$ at fixed $m$.
Let $K_m=(\ker G^{raw}_{m,*})^{\perp}$, let $r_m=\dim K_m$, and define:

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_m=\lambda_{\min}(G^{raw}_{m,*}|_{K_m})>0,
\qquad
R_m=(G^{raw}_{m,*}|_{K_m})^{-1/2}.
}
$$

The normalized packet:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde F_{m,j}
=
\sum_i F_{m,i}(R_m)_{ij},
\qquad 1\le j\le r_m.
}
$$

is cutoff-independent.  Its sampled OS Gram matrix obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\langle I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,i},I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}\rangle_{OS}
-\delta_{ij}
\right\|
\le
C_m\lambda_m^{-1}(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}).
}
$$

In particular, for all sufficiently fine cutoffs and large volumes:

$$
\boxed{
\frac12\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}
\le
\left\|
\sum_jc_j[I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
\right\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
2\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}.
}
$$

The corresponding refinement maps are compatible:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
J_{a,L}^{a',L'}
\sum_jc_j[I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
-
\sum_jc_j[I_{a',L'}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
\right\|_{OS}
\le
C_m\lambda_m^{-1/2}
(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})\|c\|_{\ell^2}.
}
$$

For the cofinal tower of Lemma 10.28g3.7aU these estimates are uniform in
packet index:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\langle I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{i},I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{j}\rangle_{OS}
-\delta_{ij}
\right\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})
}
$$

on every finite prefix, and the same $C_U$ controls the refinement
compatibility estimate.

Proof.  The Gram convergence is exactly the finite matrix form of the sampling
estimate in Lemma 10.28g3.7q1.  The limiting matrix $G^{raw}_{m,*}$ is the
direct-limit finite-prefix matrix constructed from the Cauchy family of
finite-cutoff OS forms in Lemma 10.28g3.7q2.  Since $m$ is fixed, the matrix is
finite, so entrywise convergence is norm convergence.  Quotienting by
$\ker G^{raw}_{m,*}$ removes precisely the direct-limit OS-null linear
combinations.  The restricted matrix on $K_m$ is positive definite by
definition, hence $\lambda_m>0$.

Use the limiting matrix, not the finite-cutoff matrix, to define the
normalizing operator $R_m$.  Therefore the normalized raw packet
$\widetilde F_{m,j}$ is fixed before any cutoff is chosen.  Functional
calculus for finite positive matrices gives:

$$
\boxed{
R_m^*G^{raw}_{m,a,L}R_m-I
=
R_m^*(G^{raw}_{m,a,L}-G^{raw}_{m,*})R_m,
}
$$

and hence the displayed Gram estimate.  The lower and upper OS synthesis
bounds follow by the min-max principle once the right-hand side is below
one half.

Finally, by definition of $J_{a,L}^{a',L'}$ on raw representatives:

$$
\boxed{
J_{a,L}^{a',L'}[I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
-
[I_{a',L'}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
}
$$

has OS norm controlled by the same sampling error.  Summing over the finite
packet and using the operator norm of $R_m$ gives the displayed compatibility
bound.  Thus the OS-normalized packet is cutoff-compatible rather than
recomputed independently at every cutoff.

For the special cofinal tower built in Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 and summarized in
Lemma 10.28g3.7aU, the direct-limit raw Gram matrix is the identity on every
finite prefix.  Thus $R_m=I$, $\lambda_m=1$, and the positive-flow sampling
estimate is already an operator-norm estimate on the whole finite prefix.  This
gives the packet-independent constant $C_U$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7aD: No-Bad-Packet Cofinal Refinement

For the uniform tower of Lemma 10.28g3.7aU there is a cofinal refinement
schedule:

$$
\boxed{
(a_\nu,L_\nu)_{\nu\ge1},
\qquad
a_\nu\downarrow0,
\qquad
L_\nu\uparrow\infty
}
$$

such that, for every prefix $m\le\nu$, the sampled OS Gram, the source synthesis
map, and the refinement comparison obey:

$$
\boxed{
\|G_{m,a_\nu,L_\nu}^{OS}-I_m\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
2^{-\nu},
}
$$

$$
\boxed{
\frac12\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}
\le
\|S_{m,a_\nu,L_\nu}^{OS}c\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
2\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\|J_{a_\nu,L_\nu}^{a_{\nu+1},L_{\nu+1}}S_{m,a_\nu,L_\nu}^{OS}c
-S_{m,a_{\nu+1},L_{\nu+1}}^{OS}c\|_{OS}
\le
2^{-\nu}\|c\|_{\ell^2}.
}
$$

Consequently no packet-dependent subsequence is hidden in the positive-flow
source construction.  All later cofinal limits may be taken along one refinement
schedule shared by every finite prefix.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g3.7aU gives the operator-norm estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\|G_{m,a,L}^{OS}-I_m\|_{\ell^2\to\ell^2}
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})
}
$$

on every finite prefix with the same constant $C_U$.  Choose
$(a_\nu,L_\nu)$ so that the right-hand side is at most $2^{-\nu}$ for every
$\nu$.  Since the bound is independent of $m$, the same cutoff works
simultaneously for all prefixes.  The synthesis bound follows from the
min-max principle once the Gram error is at most one half.  The refinement
estimate is the corresponding uniform estimate in Lemma 10.28g3.7aR, again with
the same constant $C_U$ and therefore the same schedule.

This is the diagonal point that matters for the later response determinant:
arbitrary finite packet bases may require packet-relative normalizing constants,
but the selected tower and schedule do not.  The continuum source frame is
therefore a direct-limit object, not a sequence of unrelated finite-cutoff
Gram-Schmidt choices.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7s: Positive-Flow Sector Packet Separation

The cofinal positive-flow packet tower may be chosen sector-complete at every
fixed physical support radius.  Concretely, after gauge averaging it contains
finite projections of:

$$
\boxed{
\hbox{local flowed curvature polynomials, center loops, flowed topological
charge densities, and finite-volume infrared smearings}.
}
$$

If a bounded positive-flow quotient vector has zero response against every
finite packet in this tower, then it is a Ward descendant, a vacuum constant,
or a typed zero-response coordinate already removed by the sector quotient.

Quantitatively, for every unit vector $\Psi\in{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}$:

$$
\boxed{
\sup_{\substack{A\in{\mathcal P}_m^{sec}\\ \|A\|_{OS}\le1}}
|\langle A,\Psi\rangle_{OS}|
\ge
1-\eta_m(E,R,\tau,k,r_0).
}
$$

Proof.  At positive flow, all listed observables are smooth gauge-invariant
cylinder functions.  Local flowed curvature polynomials separate ordinary
local gauge-invariant jets.  Center loops separate center electric and magnetic
sectors on finite collars.  Flowed topological charge densities separate
topological sectors after the typed $\theta$ coordinate is retained.  Infrared
smearings with support radius increasing cofinally separate finite-volume
zero-momentum and near-zero-momentum channels.

The union of these packet coordinates is a countable gauge-invariant
subalgebra.  It is closed under multiplication and complex conjugation after
finite packet enlargement, and it contains constants.  On every compact
finite-volume positive-flow configuration space, Stone-Weierstrass gives
density in the continuous gauge-invariant cylinder algebra.  Lemma
10.28g3.7q upgrades this qualitative density to a finite-energy OS
matrix-element estimate with the printed tail $\eta_m$.

If a unit quotient vector had response smaller than $1-\eta_m$ against the
sector packet, it would have an OS component outside $P_m^{sec}$ larger than
the quantitative tail bound, contradicting Lemma 10.28g3.7q.  If the response
against every cofinal packet vanished, then $\eta_m\to0$ forces the vector to
have zero matrix element against the whole positive-flow gauge-invariant
algebra.  Reflection positivity identifies it with the OS null space.  The
only OS null directions left before quotienting are Ward descendants, vacuum
constants, and typed zero-response coordinates.  Hence the sector-complete
packet tower separates precisely the physical quotient directions needed
below.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7a: Uniform Riesz Frame For Cofinal Source Packets

The cofinal positive-flow packet tower can be chosen so that all packet
coordinate projections have uniform lower and upper frame bounds.  More
precisely, there is a Riesz frame:

$$
\boxed{
\{e_j\}_{j\ge1}\subset{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}
}
$$

with constants:

$$
\boxed{
0<A_R\le B_R<\infty
}
$$

such that, for every finite scalar family:

$$
\boxed{
A_R\sum_j |c_j|^2
\le
\left\|\sum_j c_j e_j\right\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}^2
\le
B_R\sum_j |c_j|^2.
}
$$

Packets are finite spans of this frame.  Therefore every finite Gram matrix
of the source-frame coordinates has spectrum contained in:

$$
\boxed{
[A_R,B_R].
}
$$

In particular, inverse source-frame constants are bounded by $A_R^{-1}$ and do
not grow with the packet index.  The passage from source-frame bounds to
physical response-frame bounds is the separate content of Lemma 10.28g3.7a1.

Proof.  The positive-flow source envelope is a separable Hilbert-Sobolev space
after fixing support, flow time, and Sobolev order.  Choose an orthonormal basis
or, after gauge averaging and source-equivalence quotienting, a Riesz basis of
the closed gauge-invariant subspace.  Gauge averaging is an orthogonal
projection before quotienting and a bounded projection after quotienting by the
closed null space.  Hence the quotient frame has positive lower and finite
upper Riesz bounds.  Finite packets are coordinate projections of this one
frame, so every finite Gram submatrix inherits the same bounds by restriction.

This is the missing uniformity step behind the earlier packet-relative warning:
arbitrary packet bases can have degenerating inverse Jacobians, but the
Riesz-frame packet tower cannot.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7aS: Independent OS Source-Synthesis Lower Bound

For every fixed physical support radius, positive flow time, finite response
order, Sobolev order, source radius, and finite OS energy cutoff, choose the
uniform cofinal tower of Lemma 10.28g3.7aU.  Its packets are
cutoff-independent raw positive-flow functionals whose sampled finite source
synthesis map is OS-normalized on the physical quotient.  Concretely, after
Ward, vacuum, and typed zero-response directions have been removed, there are
raw packet vectors:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde F_{m,1},\ldots,\widetilde F_{m,r_m}
\in
{\mathfrak A}^{raw}_{R,\tau,k}
}
$$

and sampled physical vectors:

$$
\boxed{
\Phi_{m,j}^{a,L}=[I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}]
\in{\mathcal H}_{a,L;E,R,\tau}^{phys}.
}
$$

The synthesis map is:

$$
\boxed{
S_{m,a,L}^{OS}c=\sum_{j=1}^{r_m}c_j\Phi_{m,j}^{a,L}.
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
A_{OS}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}
\le
\|S_{m,a,L}^{OS}c\|_{OS}^{2}
\le
B_{OS}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2},
\qquad
A_{OS}\ge\frac12,
\quad
B_{OS}\le2
}
$$

for every finite prefix once the cutoff and volume are cofinal enough to make
$C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})\le1/2$.  The cutoff threshold is
independent of the packet index; equivalently one may use the shared cofinal
schedule of Lemma 10.28g3.7aD.  This lower bound is independent of the response
Gram estimate in Lemma 10.28g3.7a1, and the packet vectors are compatible under
refinement:

$$
\boxed{
\|J_{a,L}^{a',L'}S_{m,a,L}^{OS}c-S_{m,a',L'}^{OS}c\|_{OS}
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi})\|c\|_{\ell^2}.
}
$$

Proof.  Use the tower of Lemma 10.28g3.7aU.  On this tower the limiting raw OS
Gram matrix is the identity on every finite prefix, so the limiting
normalization matrix is the identity and no packet-dependent inverse constant
appears.

Lemma 10.28g3.7aR gives the finite-cutoff Gram estimate with the uniform
constant $C_U$:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\langle I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,i},I_{a,L}\widetilde F_{m,j}\rangle_{OS}
-\delta_{ij}
\right\|
\le
C_U(a^{\kappa_{disc}}+e^{-d(L,R)/\xi}).
}
$$

Choose the cutoff fine enough and the volume large enough so that the right
side is at most one half.  The min-max principle gives the displayed lower and
upper OS synthesis bounds with $A_{OS}=1/2$ and $B_{OS}=2$.  The refinement
compatibility estimate is the final estimate of Lemma 10.28g3.7aR.  No new
finite-cutoff Gram-Schmidt is performed here; the packet vectors are the raw
vectors frozen by Lemma 10.28g3.7q2, and their direct-limit normalization is
therefore compatible across cutoffs.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7a0: Dual-Frame Passage From Sector Detection To Response Gram

Let:

$$
\boxed{
S_m:\ell^2({\mathcal P}_m)\to{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}
}
$$

be the finite source synthesis map that sends a coefficient vector $c$ to the
OS class of the corresponding positive-flow insertion applied to the vacuum.
Let:

$$
\boxed{
D_m:{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}\to \ell^2({\mathcal P}_m^{sec})
}
$$

be the sector detector analysis map:

$$
\boxed{
(D_m\Psi)_A=\langle A,\Psi\rangle_{OS}.
}
$$

For $m$ cofinal enough, the sector exhaustion of Lemma 10.28g3.7q and Lemma
10.28g3.7s imply:

$$
\boxed{
\|D_m\Psi\|_{\ell^2}
\ge
\gamma_m\|\Psi\|_{OS},
\qquad
\gamma_m\ge 1-\eta_m.
}
$$

Let the source synthesis frame be the cutoff-compatible OS-normalized frame of
Lemma 10.28g3.7aS at the current cutoff; write it as $S_m$ to lighten
notation.  Then the OS covariance Gram:

$$
\boxed{
G_{n,m}^{OS}=S_m^*S_m
}
$$

and the detected response Gram:

$$
\boxed{
G_{n,m}^{det}=S_m^*D_m^*D_mS_m
}
$$

obey:

$$
\boxed{
c^*G_{n,m}^{OS}c
=
\|S_m c\|_{OS}^2
\ge
A_{OS}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
-\delta_{LF}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
-\delta_{shell}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2.
}
$$

Moreover:

$$
\boxed{
c^*G_{n,m}^{det}c
\ge
\gamma_m^2A_{OS}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
-\delta_{LF}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
-\delta_{shell}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2.
}
$$

Proof.  The detector map is the finite dual frame of the sector packet.  Lemma
10.28g3.7q constructs the OS-orthogonal projection $P_m^{sec}$ with tail
$\eta_m$, and Lemma 10.28g3.7s says the packet functionals separate that
projection.  Choosing the packet dual frame by finite QR in the OS norm gives
a detector analysis operator with lower bound at least $1-\eta_m$ on the
finite-energy quotient.  This is a finite-dimensional frame statement: the
smallest singular value of $D_m$ on $P_m^{sec}{\mathcal H}_{E,R,\tau}^{phys}$
is one after orthonormalization, and the complement has norm at most
$\eta_m$.

For any coefficient vector $c$, set $\Psi=S_m c$.  Lemma 10.28g3.7aS gives the
independent OS synthesis lower bound
$\|\Psi\|_{OS}^2\ge A_{OS}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^{2}$ before shell and large-field
perturbations.  This is the point that removes the circularity: the lower norm
is obtained by the finite-cutoff OS frame construction of Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 and
Lemma 10.28g3.7aS, not by the response Gram being proved here.

Applying the detector lower bound to $\Psi$ gives the additional factor
$\gamma_m^2$ for the detected response coordinates.  The large-field
complement and the shell interaction/Jacobian perturb both Gram forms by at
most $\delta_{LF}$ and $\delta_{shell}$ in operator norm.  Subtracting those two
perturbations yields the two displayed bounds.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7a1: Physical Response-Frame Lower Bound

The source-frame bounds of Lemma 10.28g3.7a and the independent OS synthesis
bound of Lemma 10.28g3.7aS pass to a cofinal physical positive-flow
response-frame lower bound after quotienting Ward, vacuum, and typed null
directions.  More precisely, for each fixed physical support
radius, positive flow time, Sobolev order, source radius, response order, and
finite-energy cutoff, there are constants:

$$
\boxed{
0<A_{phys}\le B_{phys}<\infty,
\qquad
m_0<\infty
}
$$

such that every cofinal packet $m\ge m_0$ has physical response Gram:

$$
\boxed{
G_{n,m}^{resp}
\in
\{G_{n,m}^{OS},G_{n,m}^{det}\}
}
$$

obeys:

$$
\boxed{
A_{phys}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
\le
c^*G_{n,m}^{resp}c
\le
B_{phys}\|c\|_{\ell^2}^2
}
$$

on the finite-energy quotient by Ward directions, vacuum constants, and typed
zero-response coordinates.  The constants are independent of the cutoff and of
the packet index after $m\ge m_0$.

In explicit tail form:

$$
\boxed{
A_{phys}
\ge
\frac12 A_{OS}(1-\eta_m)^2-\delta_{LF}-\delta_{shell},
}
$$

where $\eta_m$ is the finite-energy sector-exhaustion tail of Lemma
10.28g3.7q, $\delta_{LF}$ is the large-field collar error, and
$\delta_{shell}$ is the small-shell perturbative covariance error.  The packet
is taken cofinally so that the right-hand side is positive.

Proof.  At positive flow, every packet coordinate is a bounded smooth
gauge-invariant cylinder functional with fixed physical support.  Reflection
positivity gives a positive semidefinite OS covariance form for connected
finite source derivatives.  The null space of this covariance contains exactly
the finite Ward descendants, vacuum constants, and typed coordinates removed
by the quotient, because those are the directions whose insertion has zero
matrix element against the whole finite packet algebra.

Lemma 10.28g3.7a0 is the dual-frame bridge.  It applies the quantitative
sector detector of Lemma 10.28g3.7s to the source synthesis map and converts
finite-energy sector separation into a lower eigenvalue of the connected
response Gram.  Hence the small-field response Gram has lower bound
$A_{OS}(1-\eta_m)^2$ before the finite-shell perturbations.  The constant
$A_{OS}$ comes from Lemma 10.28g3.7aS and is an OS-norm synthesis bound, not an
external source Sobolev bound.

There are two perturbations.  The large-field part is bounded by Theorem
10.28g2.6 and Corollary 10.28g2.6a, giving $\delta_{LF}$.  The small-shell
heat-kernel covariance differs from the Gaussian Riesz covariance by the
finite shell interaction and Jacobian.  Definition 10.28g3.7b0 and Lemma
10.28g3.7b1 bound this difference by
$\delta_{shell}=O(g_n)+O(a_n^{\kappa_J})$ in the fixed response norm after the
dimension-at-most-four Jacobian part has been projected into the
Ward-compatible counterterms.  For sufficiently small cutoff and sufficiently
cofinal packet $m$, the displayed lower bound is positive; call half of it
$A_{phys}$.

The upper bound follows from positive-flow Sobolev embedding, the upper Riesz
bound $B_R$, and the same shell/large-field majorants.  These constants depend
only on the fixed physical support, flow time, Sobolev order, source radius,
response order, and finite-energy cutoff, not on the cutoff or on $m\ge m_0$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g3.7b0: Gauge-Fixed Heat-Kernel Shell Measure

On the small-curvature chart of Lemma 10.28g2.1a, one RG shell is written in
tree gauge as a finite-dimensional integral over Lie-algebra shell variables
$X$.  Its normalized measure has the form:

$$
\boxed{
d\mu_{n,shell}(X)
=
Z_{n,shell}^{-1}
\exp\left[
-\frac12\langle X,C_n^{-1}X\rangle
-V_n(X)
\right]
J_n(X)\,dX.
}
$$

The cutoff-uniform bounds to be proved for this shell measure are:

$$
\boxed{
c_- I\le C_n\le c_+ I,
\qquad
|D^qV_n(X)|\le C_q g_n,
\qquad
|D^q\log J_n^{ren}(X)|\le C_q a_n^{\kappa_J}
}
$$

on the finite shell chart, for the derivative orders required by the fixed
response jet.  The constants depend on the block geometry and response order,
but not on the packet index, and $\kappa_J>0$ is the positive-flow dimension
gain of the renormalized Jacobian remainder.

Here $J_n^{ren}$ denotes the Haar/Faddeev-Popov Jacobian after its local
dimension-at-most-four contribution has been moved into the counterterm
coordinates of Definition 10.28g3.7c1.

This is the object whose cumulants are estimated below.  No continuum measure
is assumed in this definition; it is the finite lattice heat-kernel shell
written in local coordinates.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a proves the covariance part,
and Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b proves the interaction and Jacobian parts.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a1: BGM1 Vector-Bundle Coefficient Control

At fixed shell scale, after tree gauge and sector freezing, the quadratic
heat-kernel shell operator acts on a finite-rank adjoint vector bundle over a
bounded-degree collar graph.  In shell units it is a uniformly local
variable-coefficient elliptic difference operator:

$$
\boxed{
L_{n,T}
=
d_{1,T}^{*}W_n d_{1,T}+R_{n,T}.
}
$$

The coefficients obey:

$$
\boxed{
c_W I\le W_n(p)\le C_W I,
\qquad
0\le R_{n,T}\le C_R I,
\qquad
\operatorname{range}(L_{n,T})\le r_0,
}
$$

and all coefficient ratios and bundle-frame changes are bounded by constants
depending only on the gauge group, the block shape, and the small-curvature
radius.

Proof.  On a finite collar graph each oriented link carries the vector space
$\mathfrak{su}(N)$, so the unknowns form a finite-rank real vector bundle of
rank $\dim\mathfrak{su}(N)$ over the link set.  The graph degree is bounded by
the hypercubic lattice degree and the fixed collar thickening.

The heat-kernel action near the identity is the squared geodesic distance on
$SU(N)$ divided by the heat time, plus a smooth class-function remainder.  On
the small-curvature chart the exponential map is a diffeomorphism onto a fixed
geodesic ball, and the Hessian of the distance-square term is uniformly
equivalent to the invariant inner product on $\mathfrak{su}(N)$.  The smooth
remainder and the frozen sector background perturb this Hessian by a bounded
amount.  Shrinking the chart once gives the displayed constants $c_W$ and
$C_W$.

Tree gauge trivializes the local adjoint bundle along the chosen tree.  Off the
tree, coefficient matrices are products of adjoint parallel transports around
plaquette collars.  These matrices are orthogonal in the invariant Killing form,
and in the small-curvature chart their derivatives are uniformly bounded.  The
plaquette incidence matrix has bounded degree, so $d_{1,T}^{*}W_n d_{1,T}$ has
finite band range.  The shell-local term $R_{n,T}$ is built from the finite shell
cutoff and boundary collar condition, hence it has the same bounded range and
bounded coefficients.

Thus the shell operator is a finite-band self-adjoint operator on a finite-rank
bundle with bounded geometry and uniformly controlled coefficient ratios.  This
proves BGM1 and the coefficient-control part of BGM3.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a2: BGM2 Tree-Gauge Ellipticity

Let $C_T^1$ be the link one-cochains on the tree-gauge complement.  On the
typed-sector small-curvature chart there are constants $c_E,C_E>0$, independent
of volume and packet index, such that:

$$
\boxed{
c_E\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
\le
\langle X,L_{n,T}X\rangle
\le
C_E\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
\qquad
(X\in C_T^1).
}
$$

Here $\|\cdot\|_{1,n}$ is the shell-unit first-difference norm on the collar
bundle.

Proof.  The upper bound follows from Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a1: each link enters only
boundedly many plaquettes and all coefficients are uniformly bounded.

For the lower bound, first use $c_W I\le W_n$ to get:

$$
\boxed{
\langle X,L_{n,T}X\rangle
\ge
c_W\|d_{1,T}X\|_2^2+\langle X,R_{n,T}X\rangle.
}
$$

The tree-gauge complement satisfies a lattice Korn-Poincare inequality:

$$
\boxed{
\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
\le
C_P
\left(
\|d_{1,T}X\|_2^2
+
\|R_{n,T}^{1/2}X\|_2^2
+
\|{\mathcal Z}_{sec}X\|^2
\right).
}
$$

The finite map ${\mathcal Z}_{sec}$ records the typed global flat directions:
center holonomies, retained topological windows, and the finitely many infrared
labels present in the shell.  In the fixed typed sector these coordinates are
held constant, so the tangent vector satisfies ${\mathcal Z}_{sec}X=0$.  The
previous two displays give the lower ellipticity bound.

The constant $C_P$ is local in shell units.  It is obtained by integrating the
one-cochain from the tree root to each link along paths inside the fixed shell
collar; the collar thickness and degree are fixed in shell units.  Nonlocal
cycle components are exactly the typed coordinates removed by
${\mathcal Z}_{sec}$.  Therefore the lower bound does not deteriorate with
volume or packet size.

This proves the tree-gauge ellipticity part of BGM2.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a3: BGM2 Zero-Mode Removal In The Typed Sector

The operator $L_{n,T}$ has no untyped zero mode on the tree-gauge shell quotient.
Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
L_{n,T}X=0,\qquad X\in C_T^1,\qquad {\mathcal Z}_{sec}X=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
X=0.
}
$$

Proof.  If $L_{n,T}X=0$, positivity of $W_n$ and $R_{n,T}$ gives
$d_{1,T}X=0$ and $R_{n,T}^{1/2}X=0$.  Thus $X$ is an infinitesimal flat
connection in tree gauge.  On a simply connected collar this already implies
$X=0$: tree gauge sets the tree links to zero, and flatness propagates the zero
value to every remaining link by plaquette induction.

On a collar with cycles, an infinitesimal flat connection is determined by its
cycle holonomies and its retained infrared harmonic coordinates.  The finite
sector map ${\mathcal Z}_{sec}$ is precisely the coordinate map for these
directions.  Since the typed sector is frozen, ${\mathcal Z}_{sec}X=0$.  Hence
all cycle and infrared flat coordinates vanish.  The previous simply connected
argument then applies on the cut collar obtained by adding the typed cycles to
the spanning tree.

Therefore the only zero vector left in the untyped Gaussian shell is the zero
vector.  Typed center, topological, and infrared labels remain external finite
sector coordinates; they are not zero modes of the Gaussian covariance.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a4: BGM4 Positive Finite-Range Shell Window

The shell covariance is not defined by a signed spectral bandpass.  It is
defined as a finite positive sum of finite-range decomposition slices:

$$
\boxed{
C_n^{shell,ext}
=
\sum_{j\in I_n} C_j^{FRD}(L_{n,T}^{ext}),
\qquad
C_j^{FRD}\ge0,
\qquad
\operatorname{range}C_j^{FRD}\le c b^j.
}
$$

Consequently the shell covariance is positive semidefinite before interaction
and Jacobian insertions:

$$
\boxed{
\langle f,C_n^{shell,ext}f\rangle
=
\sum_{j\in I_n}\langle f,C_j^{FRD}f\rangle
\ge0.
}
$$

Proof.  Apply the elliptic finite-range decomposition theorem to the
collar-extended operator $L_{n,T}^{ext}$ supplied by Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a1 through
10.28g3.7b0a3 and Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a5 below.  The theorem provides positive
semidefinite finite-range covariance pieces whose sum is the elliptic covariance
on the retained shell scales.  The RG shell is chosen by selecting the finite
index set $I_n$ of those pieces.

Since every selected piece is positive semidefinite, their sum is positive
semidefinite.  No cancellation between adjacent smooth spectral windows is used.
The ultraviolet and infrared complement pieces are assigned to the neighboring
RG steps, not subtracted from the present shell.  This is the point that makes
the Gaussian shell measure a genuine positive measure and allows the later
tree-graph and Schur estimates to use positivity rather than absolute-value
repair.

This proves BGM4.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a5: BGM5 Boundary Extension And Boundary Defect

Let $\Lambda$ be the finite shell collar containing the source support and let
$d_m$ be the distance from the source support to the boundary of the collar.  The
finite-volume tree-gauge shell operator is the restriction of a
collar-extended uniformly elliptic operator $L_{n,T}^{ext}$ up to a boundary
operator supported in the outer collar:

$$
\boxed{
L_{n,T}^{\Lambda}
=
R_\Lambda L_{n,T}^{ext}R_\Lambda^*
+
B_{\partial\Lambda},
\qquad
\operatorname{supp}B_{\partial\Lambda}\subset \partial_{r_0}\Lambda.
}
$$

For source observables supported at distance $d_m$ from the boundary, the
finite shell covariance has the boundary estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
C_n^\Lambda
-
R_\Lambda C_n^{shell,ext}R_\Lambda^*
\right\|_{q\to q}
\le
C_q e^{-d_m/\xi}.
}
$$

Proof.  Extend the finite-band coefficients of $L_{n,T}^{\Lambda}$ across a
collar of thickness greater than the largest finite-range scale used by the
source packet.  The extension is made by reflecting or copying coefficients in
local bundle frames and then smoothing with a finite partition of unity on the
graph collar.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a1 gives coefficient bounds, and the extension
changes them only by a bounded factor.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a2 and
10.28g3.7b0a3 give the uniform lower ellipticity bound on the quotient; the
extension preserves this bound after reducing the lower constant once.

For finite-range pieces with range smaller than $d_m/2$, the restricted
collar-extended kernel and the finite-volume kernel are identical on source
observables, because the kernel does not see the boundary.  For the remaining
large pieces, use the resolvent identity:

$$
\boxed{
(L_{n,T}^{\Lambda})^{-1}
-
R_\Lambda (L_{n,T}^{ext})^{-1}R_\Lambda^*
=
(L_{n,T}^{\Lambda})^{-1}
B_{\partial\Lambda}
R_\Lambda (L_{n,T}^{ext})^{-1}R_\Lambda^* .
}
$$

The uniformly elliptic finite-band bundle operator satisfies the standard
Combes-Thomas off-diagonal estimate in shell units:

$$
\boxed{
\|\mathbf 1_A L^{-1}\mathbf 1_B\|_{q\to q}
\le
C_q e^{-\operatorname{dist}(A,B)/\xi}.
}
$$

Taking $A$ to be the source collar and $B$ to be the boundary collar gives the
displayed boundary defect.  The same bound holds after summing the finitely many
FRD slices in the shell.  Thus the finite-volume covariance is the restriction
of the collar-extended covariance plus an exponentially small boundary
remainder.

This proves BGM5.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a: Tree-Gauge Shell Ellipticity And Finite-Range Covariance

On the small-curvature chart, after tree gauge and sector separation, the
quadratic part of one heat-kernel shell is uniformly elliptic on the gauge
orthogonal complement.  Its covariance admits an exact finite-range
decomposition on the collar-extended graph, plus an exponentially small
boundary remainder:

$$
\boxed{
C_n=\sum_{j=0}^{J_n}C_{n,j}^{fr}+C_{n,bdy},
\qquad
\operatorname{dist}(\operatorname{supp}C_{n,j}^{fr})\le c\,b^j.
}
$$

and for every derivative order needed by the fixed response jet:

$$
\boxed{
\|D^q C_{n,j}^{fr}(x,y)\|
\le
C_q b^{-j(2+q)},
\qquad
\|C_{n,bdy}\|_{q\to q}\le C_qe^{-d_m/\xi}.
}
$$

The constants are independent of packet index and volume once the source
support is separated from the boundary.

The finite-range theorem is applied under the following explicit hypotheses.
In this version they are proved subreceipts, not hidden regularity assumptions:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{ll}
\mathrm{BGM1} &
\hbox{the operator acts on a finite-rank adjoint vector bundle over a bounded-degree collar graph;}\\
\mathrm{BGM2} &
\hbox{after tree gauge, the operator is self-adjoint and uniformly elliptic on the gauge quotient;}\\
\mathrm{BGM3} &
\hbox{coefficients have finite range and uniformly bounded coefficient ratios in shell units;}\\
\mathrm{BGM4} &
\hbox{the shell covariance is a positive sum of finite-range covariance slices, not an arbitrary signed window;}\\
\mathrm{BGM5} &
\hbox{the finite-volume operator is obtained by restriction of a collar extension, with boundary defect supported outside the source collar.}
\end{array}
}
$$

Citation and scope.  The finite-range input is the Brydges-Guadagni-Mitter
finite-range decomposition for lattice Gaussian covariances, together with its
standard elliptic/vector-valued extensions.  The original theorem is for the
lattice Laplacian resolvent, where the covariance is decomposed into positive
semidefinite finite-range pieces.  The variable-coefficient gradient Gaussian
extensions of Adams-Kotecky-Mueller and Runa, and Bauerschmidt's Dirichlet-form
construction, are the conventional references for replacing the scalar
translation-invariant Laplacian by uniformly elliptic finite-difference systems.
The reduction to that class is supplied by Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a1 through
10.28g3.7b0a5.  Thus this lemma does not cite BGM as a black box for
gauge-fixed Yang-Mills; the five finite shell hypotheses are checked before the
finite-range theorem is invoked.

Equivalently, the shell covariance is chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
C_n^{shell,ext}
=
\sum_{j\in I_n} C_{j}^{FRD}(L_{n,T}^{ext}),
\qquad
C_{j}^{FRD}\ge0,
\qquad
\operatorname{range} C_{j}^{FRD}\le c b^j,
}
$$

where $I_n$ is the finite set of BGM scales assigned to the current RG shell.
This replaces a possibly signed smooth spectral cutoff by a positive
finite-range shell sum.  Hence the shell window preserves positivity before the
interactions are inserted.

Proof.  Work on a finite collar graph after choosing a maximal tree.  The tree
links are set to the identity and the remaining link variables are written in
Lie-algebra coordinates.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
d_{1,T}:C^1_T(\Lambda,\mathfrak{su}(N))\to C^2(\Lambda,\mathfrak{su}(N))
}
$$

be the plaquette coboundary restricted to the tree-gauge complement, and let
$W_n$ be the positive plaquette weight coming from the heat-kernel Hessian at
the frozen center/topological sector.  The quadratic form is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal Q}_{n,T}(X)
=
\langle X,L_{n,T}X\rangle,
\qquad
L_{n,T}=d_{1,T}^{*}W_n d_{1,T}+R_{n,T}.
}
$$

Here $R_{n,T}$ is a local positive collar term produced by the shell cutoff
and by the boundary condition.  The sector labels are frozen before the
quadratic form is taken, so center and topological flat directions are typed
external labels, not zero modes inside the untyped Gaussian operator.  Lemmas
10.28g3.7b0a1 through 10.28g3.7b0a3 prove that this operator is a finite-band
self-adjoint elliptic bundle operator on the zero-mode-free tree-gauge quotient.
In particular:

$$
\boxed{
c_0\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
\le
\langle X,L_{n,T}X\rangle
\le
C_0\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}.
}
$$

The constants are local graph constants; they do not depend on packet size,
volume, or cutoff once lengths are measured in shell units.  Lemma
10.28g3.7b0a5 extends $L_{n,T}$ to a collar-doubled uniformly elliptic bundle
operator $L_{n,T}^{ext}$, chosen before the source packet is selected, so all
constants are packet-independent.

Define the infinite-collar covariance on the shell by the positive finite-range
sum:

$$
\boxed{
C_n^{ext}
=
\sum_{j\in I_n} C_j^{FRD}(L_{n,T}^{ext}).
}
$$

The elliptic finite-range decomposition theorem applies by Lemmas
10.28g3.7b0a1 through 10.28g3.7b0a5.  It is obtained in local orthonormal bundle
frames; changes of frame are uniformly bounded because the gauge chart is
restricted to the small-curvature ball.  The theorem gives positive
semidefinite kernels $C_j^{FRD}$ with finite range at scale $b^j$ and the
derivative bounds printed above.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a4 defines the RG shell as
the positive finite sum over $j\in I_n$.  Setting $C_{n,j}^{fr}=C_j^{FRD}$ for
$j\in I_n$ gives an exact positive decomposition of the shell covariance.

The finite-volume covariance differs from the collar-extended covariance only
through boundary paths.  Let $R_\Lambda$ denote restriction to the original
finite collar and let $L_{n,T}^{\Lambda}$ be the finite-volume tree-gauge
operator.  The finite covariance is:

$$
\boxed{
C_n^\Lambda
=
\sum_{j\in I_n} C_j^{FRD}(L_{n,T}^{\Lambda}).
}
$$

For source supports at distance $d_m$ from the boundary, Lemma
10.28g3.7b0a5 gives the boundary extension identity and the exponential boundary
