estimate.  In operator form the boundary difference is:

$$
\boxed{
C_n^\Lambda-R_\Lambda C_n^{ext}R_\Lambda^*
=
C_n^\Lambda\,B_{d_m}\,R_\Lambda C_n^{ext}R_\Lambda^*
\;+\;
\mathrm{tail}_{d_m},
}
$$

where $B_{d_m}$ is supported in the boundary collar.  The Combes-Thomas bound
for the uniformly elliptic bundle operator gives the exponential operator
estimate for $C_{n,bdy}$.  The finite-volume covariance therefore has the
printed finite-range decomposition plus an explicit boundary remainder.

Finally, tree-gauge compatibility is harmless: the finite-range kernels are constructed
on the gauge quotient, and pulling them back by the tree-gauge identification
annihilates pure-gauge directions and preserves the Ward quotient.  A different
tree changes the coordinates by a bounded triangular local transformation on
the same small-curvature chart, so ellipticity, positivity, finite range, and
the derivative estimates are stable.  This is the finite-range input used by
the tree-cumulant bound; the exponentially small boundary part is sent to the
existing $e^{-d_m/\xi}$ term in Lemma 10.28g3.7q.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b: Heat-Kernel Interaction And Jacobian Bounds

In the same tree-gauge small-curvature chart, the nonquadratic interaction
$V_n$ and the renormalized Haar/Faddeev-Popov Jacobian remainder $J_n^{ren}$
obey:

$$
\boxed{
|D^qV_n(X)|\le C_q g_n,
\qquad
|D^q\log J_n^{ren}(X)|\le C_q a_n^{\kappa_J}
}
$$

for all derivative orders required by the fixed response jet, uniformly in
packet index.

The scale convention used in this lemma is the following.  The cutoff sequence
is chosen with:

$$
\boxed{
a_n=a_0 b^{-n},
\qquad
\ell_n=b^n a_n=a_0,
}
$$

after the usual RG rescaling of one block to fixed physical size.  Thus a shell
contains order $b^{4n}$ microscopic links inside a fixed physical block, and
the block Sobolev norm is the Riemann-sum normalization of the continuum
energy norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
\simeq
a_n^4\sum_{e\in shell}|X_e|^2
+
a_n^2\sum_{p\in shell}|(d_{1,T}X)_p|^2.
}
$$

Derivatives $D^q$ are always derivatives with respect to this normalized
Hilbert coordinate.  Equivalently, an elementary coordinate derivative
$\partial/\partial X_e$ carries the dual factor $a_n^2$, and a plaquette
derivative $\partial/\partial(dX)_p$ carries the dual factor $a_n$.  This is the
normalization that cancels the shell-volume factor in local Taylor expansions.

Proof.  The heat-kernel plaquette action is analytic in exponential
coordinates inside the small-curvature radius fixed in Lemma 10.28g2.1a.  Use
the normalized shell coordinate:

$$
\boxed{
U_e=\exp(g_n a_n X_e).
}
$$

Derivatives $D^q$ in this lemma are Frechet derivatives in the block Sobolev
norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|X\|_{1,n}^{2}
=
\sum_{e\in shell}a_n^4|X_e|^2
+
\sum_{p\in shell}a_n^2|(d_{1,T}X)_p|^2.
}
$$

This normalization is what prevents local Taylor coefficients from acquiring a
volume factor when they are tested against a fixed positive-flow source jet.
Indeed, if ${\mathcal V}_{n,q}$ is a local $q$-linear vertex obtained by
differentiating a sum of plaquette terms, then the discrete Sobolev embedding
on the fixed physical block and bounded overlap of plaquettes give:

$$
\boxed{
|{\mathcal V}_{n,q}(Y_1,\ldots,Y_q)|
\le
C_q
\prod_{i=1}^q\|Y_i\|_{1,n}.
}
$$

The constant $C_q$ is independent of the number of microscopic plaquettes,
because the factor $a_n^4$ from the local action density is exactly the
Riemann-sum weight in the normalized block norm.  This is the finite-volume
coordinate-scaling estimate used below.

For a plaquette:

$$
\boxed{
\log U_p
=
g_n a_n^2(d_{1,T}X)_p
+g_n^2a_n^2[X,X]_p
+O(g_n^3a_n^3\nabla X\,X^2).
}
$$

After the heat-kernel normalization by the plaquette time, the action has the
local expansion:

$$
\boxed{
S_{hk,n}(X)
=
\frac12\langle X,L_{n,T}X\rangle
+g_nV_{3,n}(X)
+g_n^2V_{4,n}(X)
+a_nV_{lat,n}(X),
}
$$

with all multilinear forms bounded in the shell Sobolev norm on the fixed
small-curvature ball.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a isolates the first term as the
elliptic Gaussian Hessian.  The cubic and higher heat-kernel vertices have the
following normalized derivative bounds:

$$
\boxed{
\|D^q(g_nV_{3,n}+g_n^2V_{4,n})\|_{(\|\cdot\|_{1,n})^q\to\mathbb R}
\le
C_q g_n,
}
$$

after shrinking the small-field radius so that $g_n\|X\|_{1,n}$ is bounded.
The reason is explicit in the plaquette logarithm: every non-Gaussian vertex
contains at least one commutator, hence one factor of $g_n$, and the
Riemann-sum normalization above removes the apparent shell-volume factor.

The lattice correction satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\|D^q(a_nV_{lat,n})\|_{(\|\cdot\|_{1,n})^q\to\mathbb R}
\le
C_q a_n^{\kappa_{lat}},
}
$$

for some $\kappa_{lat}>0$ determined by the positive-flow Sobolev margin.  It
comes from replacing continuum flowed kernels and derivatives by their lattice
heat-kernel representatives on fixed physical support.  Thus every remaining
interaction vertex either has an explicit $g_n$ factor or a positive lattice
power.  This proves the displayed bound for $V_n$.

The Haar density in these coordinates is:

$$
\boxed{
\log J_{Haar,n}(X)
=
\sum_e
\operatorname{tr}
\log\left(
\frac{\sinh(\operatorname{ad}(g_na_nX_e)/2)}
{\operatorname{ad}(g_na_nX_e)/2}
\right).
}
$$

The tree-gauge Faddeev-Popov determinant is the determinant of the local
gauge-variation matrix restricted to the tree complement.  On the same chart
it is analytic and nonzero, with Taylor coefficients local in the collar.
Write its logarithm, together with the Haar logarithm, as:

$$
\boxed{
\log J_n(X)
=
\log J_{n,\le4}(X)+\log J_n^{ren}(X),
}
$$

where $\log J_{n,\le4}$ is the finite local polynomial spanned by the vacuum,
kinetic, anisotropy, topological, Ward, and typed rows of Definition
10.28g3.7c1.  This piece is not claimed to be small; it is absorbed by the
Ward-compatible counterterm projection.  The remainder has positive
Symanzik dimension in the block norm above.  The Taylor remainder theorem for
local analytic functions gives a factor $a_n^{\kappa_J}$ after testing against
fixed positive-flow source derivatives.  Gauge averaging is contractive in the
finite OS norm, so the constants are independent of the finite packet being
tested.

More explicitly, after subtracting all local monomials of engineering dimension
at most four, every remaining Jacobian monomial has dimension $4+\kappa_J$ in
the normalized block norm.  Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\|D^q\log J_n^{ren}\|_{(\|\cdot\|_{1,n})^q\to\mathbb R}
\le
C_q a_n^{\kappa_J}.
}
$$

The constant is uniform because only finitely many derivative orders and source
jets are tested at fixed positive flow time.  The relation
$a_n=a_0b^{-n}$ and the fixed-block normalization above are what turn the
positive Symanzik dimension into the printed cutoff power rather than a
volume-dependent estimate.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g3.7b1a: Shell BK Norm, Edge Weights, And Vertex Weights

Decompose one shell collar into unit shell blocks $\mathcal B_n$.  For a local
smooth functional $A_X$ supported in a connected block set
$X\subset\mathcal B_n$, define the finite shell derivative norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|A_X\|_{p,n}
=
\max_{0\le q\le p}
\sup_{Y_i\ne0}
\frac{|D^qA_X(Y_1,\ldots,Y_q)|}
{\prod_{i=1}^q\|Y_i\|_{1,n;X^+}} .
}
$$

Here $X^+$ is the fixed one-collar enlargement of $X$, $p$ is larger than the
maximum source response order used in the paper, and $\|\cdot\|_{1,n;X^+}$ is
the shell Sobolev norm restricted to the enlarged support.  For a local
interaction family $A=\{A_X\}$ define the weighted BK norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|A\|_{BK,\sigma}
=
\sup_{x\in\mathcal B_n}
\sum_{X\ni x}
e^{\sigma |X|}
e^{\sigma \operatorname{diam}(X)}
\|A_X\|_{p,n}.
}
$$

For the shell covariance define the edge weight between blocks $x,y$ by:

$$
\boxed{
W_n(x,y)
=
\sum_{j\in I_n}
\sup_{\substack{u\in x\\v\in y}}
\max_{0\le q\le p}
b^{j(2+q)}
\|D^qC_{n,j}^{fr}(u,v)\|
+
C_b e^{-d_m/\xi}e^{-\operatorname{dist}(x,y)/\xi}.
}
$$

The covariance edge norm is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathfrak C_\sigma
=
\sup_x\sum_y e^{\sigma\operatorname{dist}(x,y)}W_n(x,y).
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a gives $\mathfrak C_\sigma<\infty$, uniformly in cutoff,
volume, and packet index, for sufficiently small fixed $\sigma>0$.  For the
renormalized shell remainder:

$$
\boxed{
A_n^{rem}
=
Q_{>4}(V_n+\log J_n),
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b gives:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_n
:=
\|A_n^{rem}\|_{BK,\sigma}
\le
C_{rem}a_n^{\kappa_{rem}},
\qquad
\sum_n\epsilon_n<\infty.
}
$$

The dimension-at-most-four part is not included in $A_n^{rem}$; it is routed to
the Ward-compatible counterterm matrix of Definition 10.28g3.7c1.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b1b: Finite-Dimensional BK Tree Formula With Weights

Let $F_1,\ldots,F_N$ be smooth local shell functionals, each supported in a block
set $S_\alpha$.  Their connected Gaussian cumulant with covariance
$C_n^{shell}$ satisfies the finite Brydges-Kennedy tree bound:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
\kappa_N^{G}(F_1,\ldots,F_N)
\right|
\le
\sum_{T\in{\mathcal T}_N}
\sum_{\ell:E(T)\to\mathcal B_n\times\mathcal B_n}
\prod_{\{\alpha,\beta\}\in E(T)}
W_n(x_{\alpha\beta},y_{\alpha\beta})
\prod_{\alpha=1}^N
\|F_\alpha\|_{v_\alpha(T),n}.
}
$$

The edge assignment $\ell$ is restricted so that
$x_{\alpha\beta}\in S_\alpha^+$ and $y_{\alpha\beta}\in S_\beta^+$.  The integer
$v_\alpha(T)$ is the degree of vertex $\alpha$ in the tree, and
$\|F_\alpha\|_{v_\alpha(T),n}$ means the derivative norm from Definition
10.28g3.7b1a at that order.

Proof.  In finite volume the shell field is an ordinary finite-dimensional
Gaussian vector.  Interpolate between independent copies of the Gaussian blocks
by a symmetric matrix $s_{\alpha\beta}$ multiplying cross-covariances.  The
Brydges-Kennedy forest formula for the derivative at the connected point gives:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa_N^{G}(F_1,\ldots,F_N)
=
\sum_{T\in{\mathcal T}_N}
\int_{[0,1]^{E(T)}}
\mathbb E_{C^T(t)}
\left[
\prod_{\{\alpha,\beta\}\in E(T)}
\Delta_{\alpha\beta}
\prod_{\alpha=1}^N F_\alpha(X_\alpha)
\right]
dt .
}
$$

Here $C^T(t)$ is the positive BK interpolated covariance and:

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_{\alpha\beta}
=
\sum_{u,v}
C_n^{shell}(u,v)
\frac{\partial}{\partial X_\alpha(u)}
\frac{\partial}{\partial X_\beta(v)} .
}
$$

Each tree edge therefore contributes one covariance kernel and one derivative at
each incident vertex.  Since $C^T(t)$ is positive and bounded by the same shell
covariance edge norm, the Gaussian expectation is bounded by the product of the
finite derivative norms of the vertices.  Decomposing $C_n^{shell}$ into the
positive finite-range slices from Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a and adding the boundary
remainder gives exactly the edge weight $W_n$.  Summing over the choices of edge
endpoints gives the displayed tree bound.

This is a finite-dimensional identity followed by absolute values.  No
infinite-volume clustering theorem is used.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c: Rooted Forest Summation And Summable Constant

Let $f_1,\ldots,f_r$ be positive-flow source insertions and expand the
renormalized shell remainder as:

$$
\boxed{
A_n^{rem}=\sum_{X}A_{n,X}^{rem}.
}
$$

For every $k\ge1$, the connected contribution with $k$ remainder vertices obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\frac1{k!}
\sum_{X_1,\ldots,X_k}
\left|
\kappa_{r+k}^{G}
\left(
f_1,\ldots,f_r,
A_{n,X_1}^{rem},\ldots,A_{n,X_k}^{rem}
\right)
\right|
\le
C_0^r
\left(C_{BK}\epsilon_n\right)^k
\prod_{i=1}^r
\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}} .
}
$$

The constants may be chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
C_{BK}
=
e\,\mathfrak C_\sigma\,e^{2\sigma}\,C_{loc},
\qquad
C_0
=
e\,\mathfrak C_\sigma\,C_{src}.
}
$$

Here $C_{loc}$ bounds the finite number of derivative placements and local block
enlargements at an internal vertex, while $C_{src}$ is the corresponding
positive-flow source derivative constant.

If $C_{BK}\epsilon_n\le1/2$, then the whole nonzero-remainder series satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{k\ge1}
\frac1{k!}
\sum_{X_1,\ldots,X_k}
\left|
\kappa_{r+k}^{G}
\left(
f_1,\ldots,f_r,
A_{n,X_1}^{rem},\ldots,A_{n,X_k}^{rem}
\right)
\right|
\le
2C_0^r C_{BK}\epsilon_n
\prod_{i=1}^r
\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}} .
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n
2C_0^r C_{BK}\epsilon_n
\le
2C_0^r C_{BK}C_{rem}
\sum_n a_n^{\kappa_{rem}}
<\infty .
}
$$

For the finitely many initial shells where $C_{BK}\epsilon_n>1/2$, the same
finite-dimensional estimate holds with a larger constant, and those finitely
many constants are absorbed into $C_0$ and $C_{BK}$.

Proof.  Apply Lemma 10.28g3.7b1b to the list consisting of the $r$ source
vertices and the $k$ internal remainder vertices.  Root each tree at the finite
source cluster.  For an internal vertex attached to its parent, sum first over
the parent-child covariance endpoint using the edge norm
$\mathfrak C_\sigma$, then over its support $X$ using the BK norm of
$A_n^{rem}$.

The exponential weights in Definition 10.28g3.7b1a pay for the diameter and
collar enlargement of every descendant support.  The number of possible
children orderings and derivative placements at a vertex is bounded by
$e C_{loc}$ after using the standard Cayley/tree-graph inequality:

$$
\boxed{
\frac1{k!}
\sum_{T\in{\mathcal T}_{r+k}}
\prod_{\alpha=1}^{r+k} d_\alpha(T)!
\le
e^k C_r^r .
}
$$

This gives one factor $C_{BK}\epsilon_n$ for each internal remainder vertex and
one factor $C_0$ for each external source vertex.  Summing the resulting
geometric series in $k$ gives the second display.  The last display follows
from the cutoff schedule $a_n=a_0b^{-n}$ and $\kappa_{rem}>0$.

For separated source supports, distribute
$e^{\sigma\operatorname{dist}(x,y)}$ from the edge norm along the unique path in
the rooted tree connecting the separated source clusters.  At least one such
path has total block length bounded below by the source separation, so the same
summation yields:

$$
\boxed{
\exp[-\sigma\,d_{supp}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)]
}
$$

up to a change of constants.  The boundary remainder contributes the already
summable $e^{-d_m/\xi}$ packet-tail term.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g3.7b1d: Conventional Shell Cluster Bound And NT Shell Constants

Let the shell interaction after the Gaussian Hessian and the dimension-at-most
four counterterm block have been separated be:

$$
\boxed{
A_n^{int}
=
g_nA_{3,n}+g_n^2A_{4,n}+A_n^{rem}.
}
$$

Here $A_n^{rem}=Q_{>4}(V_n+\log J_n)$ is the irrelevant shell remainder of
Definition 10.28g3.7b1a.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal E}_{\tau,n}=E_\tau(f_0),
\qquad
{\mathcal V}_{\tau,n}=E_\tau(f)-\omega_G(E_\tau(f)).
}
$$

Define the positive-flow source derivative constants:

$$
\boxed{
C_E^{src}
=
\max_{0\le q\le p}
\|D^q{\mathcal E}_{\tau,n}\|_{(\|\cdot\|_{1,n})^q\to\mathbb R},
\qquad
C_V^{src}
=
\max_{0\le q\le p}
\|D^q{\mathcal V}_{\tau,n}\|_{(\|\cdot\|_{1,n})^q\to\mathbb R}.
}
$$

These are bounded uniformly for $\tau\in W$ because positive flow gives a fixed
smooth source radius and the block Sobolev norm was normalized in Lemma
10.28g3.7b0b.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
C_{vert}
=
\max_{3\le q\le p}
\left(
\|D^qA_{3,n}\|+\|D^qA_{4,n}\|
\right),
}
$$

with the derivative norms measured by Definition 10.28g3.7b1a.  The vertex
estimate of Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b gives $C_{vert}<\infty$ uniformly in cutoff,
volume, and packet index.

For every $\tau\in W$, the non-Gaussian shell correction to the NT energy
readout after the marginal $F^2$ row has been routed to the running coupling
satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
|R_E^{sh}|
\le
B_E^{sh}g_+^4,
}
$$

and the corresponding shell correction to the NT variance satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
|R_V^{sh}|
\le
B_V^{sh}g_+^6.
}
$$

One admissible explicit choice is:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{sh}
=
4(C_E^{src})\,C_{BK}\,C_{vert}^{2}
+
4(C_E^{src})\,C_{BK}\,C_{rem},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
B_V^{sh}
=
8(C_V^{src})^{2}\,C_{BK}\,C_{vert}^{3}
+
8(C_V^{src})^{2}\,C_{BK}\,C_{vert}C_{rem}.
}
$$

The constants $C_{BK}$ and $C_{rem}$ are the finite forest constant and
irrelevant-remainder constant of Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c.

Proof.  This is the finite-volume cluster expansion obtained by applying the
Brydges-Kennedy formula of Lemma 10.28g3.7b1b to:

$$
\boxed{
\log{\mathbb E}_{C_n^{shell}}
\exp\left(
t{\mathcal E}_{\tau,n}
+
s{\mathcal V}_{\tau,n}
+
A_n^{int}
\right)
}
$$

and differentiating once in $t$ for the energy expectation and twice in $s$ for
the variance.  The shell covariance norm is precisely $\mathfrak C_\sigma$ from
Definition 10.28g3.7b1a.  Each edge of a BK tree contributes the printed edge
weight $W_n(x,y)$, and every vertex is bounded by the derivative norm in the same
definition.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c sums the rooted trees and provides the summable
factor $C_{BK}$.

The terms linear in the dimension-four kinetic density are not estimated here:
they are projected onto the marginal $F^2$ row and become part of the running
coupling coordinate in Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta.  Vacuum, Ward, typed, anisotropic,
and topological dimension-at-most-four rows are likewise removed or reset by the
counterterm projection of Definition 10.28g3.7c1.  Therefore every remaining
contribution to the untyped NT energy readout has either two non-Gaussian
small-field vertices after the marginal subtraction, giving $g_+^4$, or one
irrelevant remainder vertex, giving the $C_{rem}$ part.  For the variance, the
connected centered pair requires one additional non-Gaussian attachment after
the leading Gaussian Wick term has been subtracted, hence the $g_+^6$ bound, plus
the displayed irrelevant-remainder contribution.

The numerical factors $4$ and $8$ are harmless tree-graph envelope constants:
they absorb the two possible placements of the source vertex, the centered
variance pairings, and the finite number of derivative placements at each local
vertex.  They are independent of packet index because the source norms are
rooted fixed-support norms and the BK norm sums over roots before packet
projection.

Thus the constants $B_E^{sh}$ and $B_V^{sh}$ used in Lemma 10.28g5.1c are
derived from the shell covariance norm, the BK forest formula, the vertex
derivative bounds, the tree weights, and the final summable forest constant.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b1: Shell Tree-Cumulant Bound

Let $K_{n,r}$ be the connected cumulant obtained from
$d\mu_{n,shell}$ with $r$ positive-flow source insertions.  For each fixed
response order there are constants $C_{tree}<\infty$, $\kappa_{tree}>0$, and
$\xi>0$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
|K_{n,r}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)|
\le
C_{tree}^{r}
a_n^{\kappa_{tree}}
\prod_{i=1}^{r}\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}
}
$$

for the irrelevant and discretization remainder part, and:

$$
\boxed{
|K_{n,r}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)|
\le
C_{tree}^{r}
e^{-d_{supp}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)/\xi}
\prod_{i=1}^{r}\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}
}
$$

for separated supports.

Proof.  Split the shell interaction into the dimension-at-most-four component
and the renormalized remainder:

$$
\boxed{
V_n+\log J_n
=
\Pi_{\le4}(V_n+\log J_n)
+
A_n^{rem}.
}
$$

The first term is routed to the Ward-compatible counterterm matrix and is not
estimated by this lemma.  The connected kernel estimated here is the contribution
of $A_n^{rem}$ and of the lattice/discretization remainder after that projection.

Definition 10.28g3.7b1a gives the BK norm and the covariance edge norm.  Lemma
10.28g3.7b1b prints the finite-dimensional Brydges-Kennedy tree formula with
the edge weights $W_n(x,y)$ and vertex derivative weights.  Lemma
10.28g3.7b1c sums the rooted trees and gives:

$$
\boxed{
|K_{n,r}^{rem}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)|
\le
2C_0^r C_{BK}\epsilon_n
\prod_i
\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}} .
}
$$

With $\epsilon_n\le C_{rem}a_n^{\kappa_{rem}}$, and after absorbing the finitely
many initial shells into the constant, set:

$$
\boxed{
C_{tree}
=
\max(1,C_0)\max(1,2C_{BK}C_{rem}),
\qquad
\kappa_{tree}=\kappa_{rem}.
}
$$

This gives the first displayed bound.  The same rooted-tree summation with the
exponential edge weights retained along the path between source supports gives
the separated-support estimate, with $\xi=\sigma^{-1}$ after changing constants.
The boundary covariance remainder from Lemma 10.28g3.7b0a5 is absorbed into the
existing packet-tail term $e^{-d_m/\xi}$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7b: Uniform Flowed Shell-Kernel Majorant

For the heat-kernel regulator at bounded positive flow, one shell integration
has connected source kernels bounded by a packet-independent majorant.  For
each fixed physical support radius, Sobolev order, response order, and source
radius, there are constants $C_s<\infty$, $\kappa_s>0$, and $\xi>0$ such that
the connected shell kernel with $r$ source entries satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
K_{n,r}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)
\right|
\le
C_s^r
a_n^{\kappa_s}
\prod_{i=1}^r
\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}
}
$$

for the irrelevant and discretization remainder part, while its spatial tail
obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
K_{n,r}(f_1,\ldots,f_r)
\right|
\le
C_s^r
\exp[-\operatorname{dist}(\operatorname{supp}f_1,\ldots,\operatorname{supp}f_r)/\xi]
\prod_{i=1}^r
\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}.
}
$$

The constants are independent of the packet index.

Proof.  Definition 10.28g3.7b0 gives the finite-dimensional shell measure in
tree gauge with cutoff-uniform covariance, interaction, and Jacobian bounds.
Lemma 10.28g3.7b1 applies the tree-cumulant estimate to this measure and gives
the packet-independent connected-kernel bounds in the fixed flowed source
envelope.

Large-field configurations are excluded from the shell chart and are controlled
separately by Theorem 10.28g2.6 and Corollary 10.28g2.6a.  The irrelevant and
discretization remainder gains the power $a_n^{\kappa_s}$ from the
positive-flow Symanzik dimension gap.  Locality of the shell covariance gives
the displayed exponential support tail.  Finally, Lemma 10.28g3.7a and Lemma
10.28g3.7a1 express all packet entries and all physical response coordinates
inside uniformly bounded source and response frames, so the operator norm of
the kernel on any packet is bounded by the same constants.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c: Uniform RG Kernel Norm And Counterterm Projection

Let $K=\{K_r\}_{1\le r\le r_0}$ be a finite source-jet shell kernel through the
fixed response order $r_0$.  Define the flowed RG kernel norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|K\|_{RG}
=
\max_{1\le r\le r_0}
C_s^{-r}
\sup_{\|f_i\|_{{\mathcal H}_{R,k,\tau}^{flow}}\le1}
|K_r(f_1,\ldots,f_r)|
}
$$

together with the exponential-tail seminorm:

$$
\boxed{
\|K\|_{tail}
=
\max_{1\le r\le r_0}
C_s^{-r}
\sup
e^{\operatorname{dist}(\operatorname{supp}f_1,\ldots,\operatorname{supp}f_r)/\xi}
|K_r(f_1,\ldots,f_r)|.
}
$$

The counterterm projection is the bounded projection:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}
:
{\mathcal K}_{RG}
\to
{\mathcal K}_{rel}\oplus{\mathcal K}_{marg}\oplus{\mathcal K}_{typed}
}
$$

defined by the Ward-compatible finite renormalization conditions of Definition
10.28g3.7c1 below.  Its complement is:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{>4}=I-\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}.
}
$$

The projection norms obey:

$$
\boxed{
\|\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}\|+\|Q_{>4}\|
\le
C_{\Pi}(c_{norm}^{-1},c_{typed}^{-1},B_{phys},r_0).
}
$$

The constants $c_{norm}$ and $c_{typed}$ are the determinant lower bounds
constructed in Lemma 10.28g3.7c1a.

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c0: Printed Relevant And Typed Counterterm Basis

The dimension-at-most-four local flowed counterterm basis is chosen as:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
{\mathcal O}_{vac}&=1,\\
{\mathcal O}_{g}&=\frac12\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F_{\mu\nu}),\\
{\mathcal O}_{aniso,\mu\nu}
&=\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F_{\mu\nu})
-\frac16\sum_{\alpha<\beta}\operatorname{tr}(F_{\alpha\beta}F_{\alpha\beta}),\\
{\mathcal O}_{\theta}
&=\operatorname{tr}(F\wedge F),\\
{\mathcal O}_{Ward,\nu}
&=D_{\mu}F_{\mu\nu},\\
{\mathcal O}_{typed,c}
&=\hbox{center-sector or discrete typed-sector density}.
\end{aligned}
}
$$

The Ward descendants are quotient directions in the physical gauge-invariant
sector.  The typed coordinates are retained as typed coordinates and are not
allowed to mix into the untyped coupling coordinate.

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c1: Ward-Compatible Renormalization Conditions

Choose a finite basis of local flowed counterterm directions through dimension
four:

$$
\boxed{
\{{\mathcal O}_a\}_{a\in I_{\le4}}
}
$$

containing the printed basis of Definition 10.28g3.7c0.  Define
renormalization functionals:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_b(K)
}
$$

as follows.  The vacuum functional evaluates the empty-source normalization.
The coupling functional evaluates the two-point flowed curvature response at a
fixed physical normalization scale.  The anisotropy functionals evaluate the
differences of orientation-resolved flowed plaquette-curvature responses.  The
topological functional evaluates the flowed topological-density response, or
equivalently the finite topological sector projector printed in Lemma
10.28g3.7c1s.  The center/typed functionals evaluate the corresponding finite
center-loop or typed-sector receipt.  The Ward rows evaluate gauge-variation
descendants and are then quotiented from the physical block.  The
normalization matrix is:

$$
\boxed{
M_{ba}
=
{\mathcal N}_b({\mathcal O}_a).
}
$$

Ward descendants and vacuum constants are quotient directions.  Typed
coordinates are kept in their typed block and are not allowed to mix into the
untyped Yang-Mills kinetic coordinate.  The renormalization conditions are
admissible only after this finite quotient and block decomposition have been
performed.

The resulting matrix has Ward-triangular block form:

$$
\boxed{
M
=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{phys} & 0 & 0\\
* & M_{typed} & 0\\
0 & 0 & M_{Ward}
\end{pmatrix}
}
$$

after ordering the rows as physical untyped, typed, and Ward quotient rows.
The physical theorem uses only $M_{phys}$ and $M_{typed}$; the Ward block is
recorded to verify that no Ward descendant is being inverted as a physical
counterterm.

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c1p: Finite OS Sector Projector Algebra

At fixed cutoff, finite volume, positive flow time, and finite packet cutoffs,
the retained sector labels form a finite set:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal S}_{m}^{sec}
=
{\mathcal S}_{m}^{cen}
\times
{\mathcal S}_{m}^{top}
\times
{\mathcal S}_{m}^{type}.
}
$$

The sector projectors used in Lemma 10.28g3.7c1s are constructed as follows.

Center projectors.  The retained center data form a finite abelian group
$Z_m^{cen}$ generated by the retained center-flux and twisted-boundary loop
coordinates.  For a retained center character $\chi$ define:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\chi}^{cen}
=
\frac1{|Z_m^{cen}|}
\sum_{z\in Z_m^{cen}}
\overline{\chi(z)}\,U_z .
}
$$

Here $U_z$ is the unitary multiplication operator implementing the center-flux
label.  Haar orthogonality gives:

$$
\boxed{
P_{\chi}^{cen}P_{\chi'}^{cen}
=
\delta_{\chi\chi'}P_{\chi}^{cen},
\qquad
(P_{\chi}^{cen})^*=P_{\chi}^{cen}.
}
$$

Topological projectors.  Let $Q_{\tau,a,L}$ be the flowed lattice topological
charge at the chosen positive flow time.  It is a bounded continuous
gauge-invariant function on the compact finite-volume gauge configuration
space.  Choose finitely many disjoint Borel windows $I_q$ with positive
separation around the retained topological charge receipts and positive finite
OS weight, and define:

$$
\boxed{
P_q^{top}
=
{\bf 1}_{I_q}(Q_{\tau,a,L})
}
$$

by bounded Borel functional calculus for the multiplication operator
$Q_{\tau,a,L}$.  Then:

$$
\boxed{
P_q^{top}P_{q'}^{top}
=
\delta_{qq'}P_q^{top},
\qquad
(P_q^{top})^*=P_q^{top}.
}
$$

For use inside smooth positive-flow source packets, choose smooth functions
$\chi_{q,\epsilon}$ supported in $I_q$ and equal to one on a slightly smaller
window.  Since the finite cutoff measure is Radon and the windows are separated,
Urysohn approximation gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|\chi_{q,\epsilon}(Q_{\tau,a,L})-P_q^{top}\|_{OS\to OS}
\le
\epsilon.
}
$$

The error $\epsilon$ is chosen below the packet tail $\eta_m$, so replacing exact
Borel projectors by smooth positive-flow windows only changes the finite-sector
Gram matrix by an $O(\eta_m)$ term.

Typed projectors.  The typed labels form the finite commutative algebra:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal T}_m
=
\mathbb C^{{\mathcal S}_{m}^{type}}.
}
$$

For a typed label $t$ define the coordinate idempotent:

$$
\boxed{
P_t^{type}(s)=\delta_{ts}.
}
$$

The finite OS space is enlarged by the direct-sum typed sector algebra before
zero-response directions are quotiented.  Its typed inner product is diagonal:

$$
\boxed{
\langle P_t^{type},P_{t'}^{type}\rangle_{OS}
=
w_t\delta_{tt'},
\qquad
w_t\ge0.
}
$$

Labels with $w_t=0$ are exactly typed zero-response coordinates and are removed
before determinants are taken.  The same convention is used for every sector
factor: a center, topological, or typed sector idempotent with zero OS norm is
not retained as a determinant row.

The combined finite-sector projector is:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}
=
P_{\chi}^{cen}P_q^{top}P_t^{type},
\qquad
\alpha=(\chi,q,t)\in{\mathcal S}_{m}^{sec}.
}
$$

The three factors commute because they are multiplication operators in the
finite gauge-invariant cylinder algebra and the finite typed label algebra.
After quotienting all zero-norm sector directions:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}\Pi_{\beta}^{sec}
=
\delta_{\alpha\beta}\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec},
\qquad
\langle \Pi_{\alpha}^{sec},\Pi_{\beta}^{sec}\rangle_{OS}
=
\delta_{\alpha\beta}\|\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}\|_{OS}^{2},
\qquad
\|\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}\|_{OS}>0.
}
$$

This is the standalone finite OS construction behind the phrase "typed receipt
idempotent": it is a finite commutative sector algebra with exact orthogonal
coordinate projections, plus smooth topological approximants whose error is
absorbed into the cofinal packet tail.

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c1s: Finite-Sector Pivot Determinant

The center, topological, and typed rows in Definition 10.28g3.7c1 can be
chosen so that their finite-sector normalization matrix has a cutoff-uniform
lower determinant.  More precisely, for the finite set of retained sector
labels below the packet cutoffs, choose sector projectors:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec},
\qquad
\alpha\in{\mathcal S}_{m}^{sec},
}
$$

generated by Definition 10.28g3.7c1p.  Define the typed normalization rows by:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_{\alpha}^{typed}(K)
=
\frac{\langle \Pi_{\alpha}^{sec},K\rangle_{OS}}
{\|\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}\|_{OS}^{2}}.
}
$$

Then the finite-sector block:

$$
\boxed{
M_{\alpha\beta}^{sec}
=
{\mathcal N}_{\alpha}^{typed}({\mathcal O}_{typed,\beta})
}
$$

obeys:

$$
\boxed{
M^{sec}=I+E^{sec},
\qquad
\|E^{sec}\|\le C(\eta_m+\delta_{LF}+\delta_{shell}),
}
$$

and hence:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(M^{sec})\ge c_{sec}>0
}
$$

for all sufficiently cofinal packets and sufficiently small cutoffs.

Proof.  Definition 10.28g3.7c1p constructs the sector projectors before any
determinant is formed.  At finite cutoff and finite volume, center characters
give exact central idempotents by finite Fourier transform on the retained
center-flux group.  The topological sector projectors are exact Borel spectral
projections of the bounded multiplication operator $Q_{\tau,a,L}$; their smooth
positive-flow window representatives approximate them in OS norm with error
chosen below $\eta_m$.  The typed rows are coordinate projections in the finite
commutative typed label algebra, with zero-weight typed coordinates removed
before the quotient.

The three sector algebras commute, so their products
$\Pi_{\alpha}^{sec}$ are exact orthogonal idempotents in the finite OS quotient.
Only finitely many sector labels lie below the fixed Casimir, energy, support,
and response-order cutoffs, so this is a finite orthogonal family.

Normalize each row by its own OS norm.  At the finite-cutoff sector level this
gives an identity matrix between sector rows and sector columns.  Replacing the
full sector algebra by the cofinal packet contributes the tail $\eta_m$ from
Lemma 10.28g3.7q, including the smooth-window approximation error for the
topological projectors.  The large-field and shell perturbations contribute
$\delta_{LF}$ and $\delta_{shell}$ in finite matrix norm.  Thus
$M^{sec}=I+E^{sec}$ with the displayed bound.  Taking the packet cofinal and
the cutoff small makes $\|E^{sec}\|\le1/2$, and the min-max principle gives
the positive lower determinant constant $c_{sec}$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c1a: Leading-Block Determinant Bound For Normalization Rows

The Ward-compatible normalization matrix has a cutoff-uniform leading block.
After rescaling the printed rows of Definition 10.28g3.7c1 by fixed physical
normalization constants:

$$
\boxed{
M=M^{(0)}+\Delta M,
\qquad
M^{(0)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
I_{phys} & 0 & 0\\
0 & I_{typed} & 0\\
0 & 0 & M^{(0)}_{Ward}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
$$

Moreover:

$$
\boxed{
\|\Delta M\|
\le
C\left(g_n+a_n^{\kappa}+a_n^{\kappa_J}+\eta_m+\delta_{LF}+\delta_{shell}\right).
}
$$

Consequently, after taking the cutoff small enough and the sector packet
cofinal enough:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(M_{phys})\ge c_{norm}>0,
\qquad
\sigma_{\min}(M_{typed})\ge c_{typed}>0.
}
$$

Proof.  The perturbative physical rows are normalized at a fixed positive-flow
physical scale.  At the Gaussian heat-kernel leading point, the vacuum row
evaluates the vacuum coordinate, the curvature two-point row evaluates the
kinetic coordinate, and anisotropy rows evaluate the traceless orientation
block.  With this choice of rows and columns, the untyped perturbative leading
block is the identity.

The topological, center, and typed rows are not assigned to the Gaussian
kinetic block.  Their leading determinant is the finite-sector pivot
determinant of Lemma 10.28g3.7c1s.  Therefore the typed/sector diagonal block
also has a cutoff-uniform lower singular value.  Ward descendants lie in the
separate quotient block and are not inverted as physical counterterms.

The perturbation terms have distinct origins.  Heat-kernel non-Gaussian
interactions contribute $O(g_n)$ by Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b.  Lattice and
positive-flow Symanzik remainders contribute $O(a_n^\kappa)$ by Lemma
10.28g3.7b1.  The renormalized Jacobian remainder contributes
$O(a_n^{\kappa_J})$ by Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b.  Replacing the full sector algebra
by the finite sector packet contributes $\eta_m$ by Lemma 10.28g3.7q.  The
large-field collar and shell covariance perturbations contribute $\delta_{LF}$
and $\delta_{shell}$ by Lemma 10.28g3.7a1.  Thus the displayed perturbation
bound holds in ordinary finite matrix operator norm.

Choose the cutoff and packet so the right-hand side is smaller than one half
on the perturbative physical block and smaller than $c_{sec}/2$ on the
finite-sector block.  The Neumann determinant estimate then gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(M_{phys})\ge\frac12,
\qquad
\sigma_{\min}(M_{typed})\ge\frac12c_{sec}
}
$$

after the row normalization.  Undoing the fixed row normalization gives the
positive constants $c_{norm}$ and $c_{typed}$.  This is independent of the
response Gram lower bound; the Gram bound is used only to identify the rows as
stable physical response coordinates.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c2: Bounded Ward-Compatible Counterterm Projection

The normalization matrix $M$ in Definition 10.28g3.7c1 is invertible on the
finite Ward/vacuum/typed quotient.  Equivalently:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}(M_{phys})\ge c_{norm},
\qquad
\sigma_{\min}(M_{typed})\ge c_{typed}>0.
}
$$

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
\|M^{-1}\|
\le
C_M(c_{norm}^{-1},c_{typed}^{-1},B_{phys},r_0).
}
$$

Consequently the projection $\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}$ is a uniformly bounded
operator on the RG kernel norm, independently of packet index and cutoff.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c1a gives an independent leading-block determinant
bound for the physical and typed diagonal blocks.  This is stronger than
mere response-frame nondegeneracy: it prints the normalization rows so that
the leading heat-kernel block is the identity and all cutoff, packet,
large-field, and shell errors are a small finite-matrix perturbation.

Ward identities make the physical-to-Ward mixing rows vanish after quotienting,
and typed-to-untyped mixing is forbidden by the typed block rule in Definition
10.28g3.7c1.  Thus the matrix is block-triangular with invertible physical and
typed diagonal blocks.  Lemma 10.28g3.7a1 supplies the upper response-frame
bound $B_{phys}$, so the finite matrix norms of the rows are uniformly bounded.
Finite-dimensional linear algebra then gives the displayed inverse bound.

The projection is defined by solving the normalization equations with this
inverse matrix and subtracting the resulting relevant, marginal, and typed
counterterm.  Since $M^{-1}$ is uniformly bounded and the number of retained
counterterm directions is fixed by the response order and dimension cutoff,
the projection norm is uniformly bounded.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c3: Scheme Stability Of The Counterterm Projection

If two Ward-compatible normalization packets satisfy the conditions of
Definition 10.28g3.7c1 and both lie inside the same fixed flowed source
envelope, then their counterterm projections differ by a bounded finite change
of coordinates:

$$
\boxed{
\|\Pi_{\le4}^{(1)}-\Pi_{\le4}^{(2)}\|
\le
C_{sch}\,\|M_1-M_2\|.
}
$$

The constant $C_{sch}$ depends only on the determinant constants
$c_{norm},c_{typed}$, the response upper-frame constant, and the finite
response order.

Proof.  Both projections are obtained by inverting Ward-triangular matrices
whose physical and typed diagonal blocks have lower singular values bounded
away from zero by Lemma 10.28g3.7c2.  The resolvent identity for finite
matrices gives:

$$
\boxed{
M_1^{-1}-M_2^{-1}
=
M_1^{-1}(M_2-M_1)M_2^{-1}.
}
$$

The uniform inverse bounds therefore give the displayed Lipschitz estimate.
This proves that the RG projection is stable under finite changes of
Ward-compatible normalization scheme and cannot generate packet-dependent
inverse constants.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c4a: Packet-Uniform Banach RG Space

Fix the physical support radius, positive flow time, Sobolev order, source
radius, and response order.  Let ${\mathfrak K}_{RG}$ be the Banach space of
connected positive-flow source kernels through that response order, equipped
with the norm of Definition 10.28g3.7c and the tail seminorm.  The
Ward-compatible projection of Definition 10.28g3.7c decomposes it as:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak K}_{RG}
=
{\mathfrak K}_{\le4}^{phys}
\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{typed}
\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{Ward}
\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{irr}.
}
$$

Here:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak K}_{irr}=Q_{>4}{\mathfrak K}_{RG}.
}
$$

The irrelevant norm is the dimension-weighted version of the RG norm.  The
coordinate $H_\alpha$ is the dimensionless coefficient after the canonical
lattice factor $a_n^{\Delta_\alpha}$ has been extracted.  With this convention
block rescaling gains the factor $b^{-\Delta_\alpha}$ in the norm below.

$$
\boxed{
\|H\|_{irr,n}
=
\sup_{\alpha\in I_{>4}}
b^{n\Delta_\alpha}
\|H_\alpha\|_{RG,\alpha},
\qquad
\Delta_\alpha=\dim(\alpha)-4.
}
$$

Only local types with dimension above four enter $I_{>4}$.  At fixed positive
flow time, fixed response order, and fixed Sobolev order, the local type set
below the response cutoff is finite modulo translations and finite typed sector
labels.  Hence:

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_0
=
\min_{\alpha\in I_{>4}}\Delta_\alpha
>0.
}
$$

The norm over translations and packet supports is the rooted BK/RG supremum
norm, not a finite-dimensional Euclidean norm.  Thus enlarging the packet
enlarges the set of roots but does not change the constants.

More explicitly, for a local type $\alpha$ and a root block $x$, write
$H_{\alpha,Y,x}$ for the connected kernel supported on a polymer $Y$ rooted at
$x$.  The component norm used above is:

$$
\boxed{
\|H_\alpha\|_{RG,\alpha}
=
\sup_x
\sum_{Y\ni x}
e^{m\,{\rm diam}(Y)}
w_\alpha(Y)
|H_{\alpha,Y,x}|_{C^k_\tau}.
}
$$

The weight $w_\alpha(Y)$ contains the fixed Casimir, derivative, and sector
weights of Definition 10.28g3.7c.  This is the norm on which the shell forest
bound acts.  It is a Banach lattice norm, so a positive entrywise majorant
controls the operator norm by the Schur row bound.

Equivalently, with the ultraviolet block scale:

$$
\boxed{
L_n=b^n,
}
$$

the irrelevant norm has the conventional weighted form:

$$
\boxed{
\|H\|_{irr,n}
=
\sup_{\alpha\in I_{>4}}
L_n^{\Delta_\alpha}
\|H_\alpha\|_{RG,\alpha}.
}
$$

The untyped marginal Yang-Mills kinetic density:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_g=\frac12\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F_{\mu\nu})
}
$$

is not an irrelevant coordinate.  It is projected into the one-dimensional
running coupling coordinate by $\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}$ before $Q_{>4}$ is applied.
Thus:

$$
\boxed{
Q_{>4}{\mathcal O}_g=0,
\qquad
\Pi_gQ_{>4}=0.
}
$$

This is the formal point at which the marginal $F^2$ direction is removed from
the irrelevant contraction estimate and routed to the beta equation.

###### Definition 10.28g3.7c4b: One-Shell Banach RG Map And Its Derivative

For a connected kernel $K\in{\mathfrak K}_{RG}$, first define the connected
shell transform:

$$
\boxed{
\Gamma_n(K)
=
\log{\mathbb E}_{C_n^{shell}}
\exp(A_n^{shell}+K)
-
\log{\mathbb E}_{C_n^{shell}}
\exp(A_n^{shell})
}
$$

where only connected kernels in the slow fields are retained.  The one-shell
Banach RG map is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathscr R}_n(K)
=
{\mathsf S}_b
\left[
\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}\Gamma_n(K)
+
Q_{>4}\Gamma_n(K)
\right]_{conn}.
}
$$

Here ${\mathsf S}_b$ is the block rescaling back to unit shell block, the
expectation is with the positive finite-range shell covariance of Lemma
10.28g3.7b0a, and:

$$
\boxed{
A_n^{shell}
=
V_n+\log J_n-\Pi_{\le4}(V_n+\log J_n)
}
$$

is the renormalized shell remainder.  The relevant and typed coordinates are
then reset by the normalization equations of Definition 10.28g3.7c1.  This is a
finite-dimensional analytic map at finite cutoff and finite volume, and the
uniform Banach map is obtained by the estimates of Lemmas 10.28g3.7b1 and
10.28g3.7c2.

Its derivative at the origin has the block form:

$$
\boxed{
D{\mathscr R}_n(0)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
L_{\le4,n} & M_{\le4,irr,n}\\
M_{irr,\le4,n} & L_{irr,n}
\end{pmatrix}
}
$$

with respect to ${\mathfrak K}_{\le4}^{phys}\oplus{\mathfrak K}_{typed}\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{irr}$ after Ward quotienting.  The explicit irrelevant block is:

$$
\boxed{
L_{irr,n}
=
Q_{>4}
{\mathsf S}_b
\left(
I+{\mathsf A}_n
\right)
Q_{>4}.
}
$$

The shell insertion operator ${\mathsf A}_n$ is the deviation of the derivative
of the shell transform from canonical identity transport:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf A}_n H
=
\left.
\frac{d}{dt}
\left(
\log{\mathbb E}_{C_n^{shell}}
\exp(A_n^{shell}+tH)
\right)
\right|_{t=0}
-H .
}
$$

Equivalently, ${\mathsf A}_nH$ is the connected cumulant sum with one marked
$H$ vertex and any number of $A_n^{shell}$ vertices.

Thus the derivative of the shell transform and the irrelevant derivative of the
RG map are:

$$
\boxed{
D\Gamma_n(0)H
=
H+{\mathsf A}_nH,
\qquad
Q_{>4}D{\mathscr R}_n(0)Q_{>4}
=
L_{irr,n}.
}
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c4c: Norm Of The Explicit Irrelevant Linear Operator

There are constants $C_A<\infty$ and $\kappa_A>0$, independent of packet index,
cutoff, and volume, such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf A}_n\|_{irr,n\to irr,n}
\le
C_A a_n^{\kappa_A}.
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
\|L_{irr,n}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1}
\le
b^{-\Delta_0}
\;+\;
\widetilde C_A a_n^{\kappa_A}.
}
$$

Choose $n_0$ so large that:

$$
\boxed{
\widetilde C_A a_n^{\kappa_A}
\le
\frac12(1-b^{-\Delta_0})
\qquad(n\ge n_0).
}
$$

Then the strict packet-uniform irrelevant contraction constants are the actual
operator norms:

$$
\boxed{
q_{irr,n}
=
\|L_{irr,n}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1},
\qquad
q_{irr}^{env}
=
\sup_{n\ge n_0}q_{irr,n}
\le
\frac12(1+b^{-\Delta_0})
<1,
\qquad
\|L_{irr,n}\|\le q_{irr}^{env}
\quad(n\ge n_0).
}
$$

Proof.  The operator ${\mathsf A}_nH$ is the connected shell cumulant with one
marked $H$ vertex and $k\ge1$ vertices from the renormalized shell remainder
$A_n^{shell}$.  Apply Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c with one marked external kernel $H$.
The marked vertex is measured in the irrelevant norm; every internal shell
remainder contributes the summable BK factor $\epsilon_n\le C_{rem}
a_n^{\kappa_{rem}}$.  Summing the rooted trees gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf A}_nH\|_{irr,n}
\le
C_A a_n^{\kappa_A}\|H\|_{irr,n},
\qquad
\kappa_A=\kappa_{rem}.
}
$$

The block rescaling ${\mathsf S}_b$ acts diagonally on the leading local type of
an irrelevant kernel:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf S}_bH_\alpha\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
b^{-\Delta_\alpha}\|H_\alpha\|_{irr,n}.
}
$$

Because $\Delta_\alpha\ge\Delta_0$ for all irrelevant types, the canonical
scaling part has norm at most $b^{-\Delta_0}$.  The perturbation
${\mathsf A}_n$ contributes the previous display, after the bounded
Ward-compatible projection and scheme change of Lemmas 10.28g3.7c2 and
10.28g3.7c3.  This proves the bound on $L_{irr,n}$ and the printed envelope
$q_{irr}^{env}$.  In what follows $q_{irr}$ denotes any fixed number strictly
between $q_{irr}^{env}$ and one.

The constant is packet-uniform because the irrelevant norm is rooted and
weighted, the shell cumulant norm is packet-uniform, and the response frame
constants are packet-uniform by Lemmas 10.28g3.7aU through 10.28g3.7a1.

$$
\square
$$

###### Corollary 10.28g3.7c4c0: Weighted Irrelevant Derivative Bound With F-Squared Projected Out

Let:

$$
\boxed{
D_hRG_n(g,0)
=
Q_{>4}D{\mathscr R}_n(g,0)Q_{>4}.
}
$$

This derivative is taken after the Ward-compatible decomposition:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak K}_{RG}
=
\mathbb R{\mathcal O}_g
\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{vac,type,Ward,aniso}
\oplus
{\mathfrak K}_{irr},
}
$$

and after the $\mathbb R{\mathcal O}_g$ component has been routed into the
running coupling coordinate.  Hence the marginal $F^2$ direction is not present
in $D_hRG_n(g,0)$.

In the weighted irrelevant norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|h\|_{irr,n}
=
\sup_{\alpha\in I_{>4}}
L_n^{\Delta_\alpha}|h_\alpha|_{RG,\alpha},
\qquad
L_n=b^n,
}
$$

the linearized irrelevant block satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\|D_hRG_n(g,0)\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1}
\le
q_{irr}^{env}
<1
\qquad(n\ge n_0,\;0<g\le g_*).
}
$$

Proof.  By Definition 10.28g3.7c4b:

$$
\boxed{
D_hRG_n(g,0)
=
Q_{>4}{\mathsf S}_b(I+{\mathsf A}_{n,g})Q_{>4}.
}
$$

The operator ${\mathsf A}_{n,g}$ is the one-marked-irrelevant-vertex shell
cumulant operator in the background with marginal coupling $g$.  Its part
parallel to ${\mathcal O}_g$ is killed by $Q_{>4}$ and separately counted in the
beta coordinate; its Ward, vacuum, typed, anisotropic, and topological
dimension-at-most-four parts are killed or reset by the same projection.  Thus
only output types with $\Delta_\alpha>0$ remain.

Canonical block rescaling gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf S}_b h_\alpha\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
b^{-\Delta_\alpha}\|h_\alpha\|_{irr,n}.
}
$$

The marked shell cumulant perturbation is bounded by Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf A}_{n,g}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n}
\le
C_Aa_n^{\kappa_A}+C_Ag^2a_n^{\kappa_A}.
}
$$

After shrinking $g_*$ and increasing $n_0$, the second term is absorbed into the
same half-margin used in Lemma 10.28g3.7c4c.  Since every surviving irrelevant
type has $\Delta_\alpha\ge\Delta_0>0$, the operator norm is bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
b^{-\Delta_0}+\widetilde C_Aa_n^{\kappa_A}
\le
q_{irr}^{env}
<1.
}
$$

This proves the desired weighted derivative bound and makes explicit that the
uncontracted marginal $F^2$ direction has been projected out before the
irrelevant estimate is made.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c4cS: Weighted Type-Pressure Spectral Bound

The irrelevant contraction in Lemma 10.28g3.7c4c is a spectral bound for the
linearized irrelevant RG block, not merely a packetwise scaling statement.

Let ${\mathfrak X}_{irr}$ be the fixed Banach lattice obtained from
${\mathfrak K}_{irr}$ by forgetting the shell index and retaining the rooted
polymer norm of Definition 10.28g3.7c4a.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
W_nH
=
\{b^{n\Delta_\alpha}H_\alpha\}_{\alpha\in I_{>4}}.
}
$$

Conjugate the linearized irrelevant block to this fixed space:

$$
\boxed{
\widehat L_{irr,n}
=
W_{n+1}L_{irr,n}W_n^{-1}.
}
$$

For irrelevant types $\alpha,\beta$, define the type-pressure matrix:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal P}_n(\beta,\alpha)
=
\sup_{\substack{H=Q_\alpha H\\ \|W_nH\|_{{\mathfrak X}_{irr}}\le1}}
\|Q_\beta W_{n+1}L_{irr,n}H\|_{{\mathfrak X}_{irr}}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal P}_n(\beta,\alpha)
\le
b^{-\Delta_\alpha}\delta_{\alpha\beta}
+
{\mathcal E}_n(\beta,\alpha),
\qquad
\sup_\beta\sum_\alpha{\mathcal E}_n(\beta,\alpha)
\le
C_Ea_n^{\kappa_A}.
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
\|\widehat L_{irr,n}\|_{{\mathfrak X}_{irr}\to{\mathfrak X}_{irr}}
\le
\sup_\beta\sum_\alpha{\mathcal P}_n(\beta,\alpha)
\le
b^{-\Delta_0}+C_Ea_n^{\kappa_A}.
}
$$

After increasing $n_0$ if necessary:

$$
\boxed{
\rho(\widehat L_{irr,n})
\le
\|\widehat L_{irr,n}\|
\le
q_{irr}^{env}
<1
\qquad(n\ge n_0).
}
$$

Moreover the nonautonomous irrelevant cocycle obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\|\widehat L_{irr,n+r-1}\cdots \widehat L_{irr,n}\|
\le
(q_{irr}^{env})^r
\qquad(n\ge n_0,\ r\ge1).
}
$$

Proof.  The conjugation by $W_n$ converts the shell-dependent irrelevant norm
into the fixed rooted Banach lattice norm.  The canonical part of
$L_{irr,n}$ is diagonal in the leading local type and contributes
$b^{-\Delta_\alpha}$ on the $\alpha$ row.  All non-diagonal type changes come
from the marked-shell cumulant operator ${\mathsf A}_n$ and from the bounded
Ward-compatible projection.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c gives the rooted tree estimate
for one marked irrelevant vertex.  Summing over all output roots and types gives
the row bound for ${\mathcal E}_n$ with the same packet-independent constant
$C_E$.

The Banach lattice Schur estimate gives the displayed operator norm.  The
spectral-radius estimate follows from Gelfand's formula, or directly from
$\rho(T)\le\|T\|$ for bounded operators.  The cocycle estimate follows by
submultiplicativity after the same fixed-space conjugation.  Thus every
linearized irrelevant shell step has spectral radius below one uniformly in the
packet, cutoff, and volume after finitely many initial shells are discarded.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c4d: Banach Analytic Remainder Bound

On a fixed small ball in ${\mathfrak K}_{RG}$, the one-shell map
${\mathscr R}_n$ is analytic and satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\|Q_{>4}({\mathscr R}_n(K+H)-{\mathscr R}_n(K)-D{\mathscr R}_n(K)H)\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
C_{irr}\|H\|_{irr,n}^{2}
+
C_{irr}a_n^{\kappa_A}\|H\|_{irr,n}.
}
$$

Proof.  At finite cutoff the map is a logarithm of a finite-dimensional Gaussian
expectation with analytic local interaction, hence analytic on the small-field
ball.  The Cauchy integral estimate for analytic Banach maps reduces the
quadratic remainder to a uniform bound on the second derivative.  The second
derivative is a connected cumulant with two marked $H$ vertices and any number
of $A_n^{shell}$ vertices.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c, applied with two marked external
vertices, gives the uniform quadratic term.  Terms containing at least one
renormalized shell remainder contribute the extra factor
$a_n^{\kappa_A}$.  The bounded counterterm projection from Lemma 10.28g3.7c2 and
the finite scheme stability of Lemma 10.28g3.7c3 preserve the estimate in the
irrelevant quotient.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta: One-Shell Coupling Coordinate Computation

The one-shell heat-kernel RG map has the packet-uniform Yang-Mills one-loop
coupling coordinate:

$$
\boxed{
g_{n+1}
=
g_n-\beta_0g_n^3\log b
+
R_{\beta,n},
\qquad
\beta_0=\frac{11\,C_2(G)}{3(4\pi)^2}.
}
$$

The remainder obeys:

$$
\boxed{
|R_{\beta,n}|
\le
C_{\beta}\left(g_n^5+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\right),
}
$$

with $C_{\beta}$ independent of packet index, cutoff, and volume after the fixed
physical support radius, positive flow time, Sobolev order, source radius, and
response order have been chosen.

Proof.  The coupling coordinate is not read from an arbitrary plaquette
coefficient.  It is the Ward-compatible row of Definition 10.28g3.7c1:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_g(K)
=
\hbox{the fixed-scale two-point response of flowed curvature insertions}.
}
$$

The row is normalized by:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_g({\mathcal O}_g)=1,
\qquad
{\mathcal N}_g({\mathcal O}_{vac})=
{\mathcal N}_g({\mathcal O}_{Ward})=
{\mathcal N}_g({\mathcal O}_{typed})=0,
}
$$

after the finite Ward, vacuum, typed, and anisotropy block decomposition of
Definition 10.28g3.7c1.  Thus the only untyped marginal coordinate measured by
this row is the coefficient of:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_g=\frac12\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F_{\mu\nu}).
}
$$

At finite cutoff and in a background-field chart on the small-curvature cell,
write the fine field as a background plus a shell fluctuation.  The heat-kernel
plaquette action has the small-link expansion:

$$
\boxed{
S_{HK,n}(A+\xi)
=
\frac1{2g_n^2}\langle F_A,F_A\rangle
+
\frac12\langle \xi,\Delta_{1,A}^{shell}\xi\rangle
+
\langle \bar c,\Delta_{0,A}^{shell}c\rangle
+
V_{int}(A,\xi,c,\bar c)
+
E_{lat,n}(A,\xi).
}
$$

Here $\Delta_{1,A}^{shell}$ is the covariant shell operator on transverse
one-forms, $\Delta_{0,A}^{shell}$ is the ghost/Jacobian scalar operator from
the finite gauge fixing and Haar measure, and $E_{lat,n}$ is the heat-kernel
lattice remainder.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a through 10.28g3.7b1c give the
finite-range shell covariance, the gauge-fixed Jacobian bounds, and the BK
forest estimate for $V_{int}$ and $E_{lat,n}$.

The quadratic shell determinant contributes:

$$
\boxed{
\Gamma_{n}^{(1)}(A)
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{shell}\log \Delta_{1,A}
-
\operatorname{Tr}_{shell}\log \Delta_{0,A}.
}
$$

Apply the heat-kernel coefficient expansion to the finite shell
$[b^{-1}a_n^{-1},a_n^{-1}]$.  In background Feynman gauge the vector and ghost
operators have the local endomorphism curvatures:

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_{1,A}
=
-D_A^2\delta_{\mu\nu}
-2\,{\rm ad}(F_{\mu\nu}),
\qquad
\Delta_{0,A}
=
-D_A^2.
}
$$

The logarithmic coefficient is the fourth heat coefficient:

$$
\boxed{
\left[
\frac12 a_4(\Delta_{1,A})
-a_4(\Delta_{0,A})
\right]_{{\mathcal O}_g}
=
\beta_0\,{\mathcal O}_g.
}
$$

Equivalently, using the standard local coefficient for a Laplace-type operator:

$$
\boxed{
a_4(-D^2+E)
=
\frac1{(4\pi)^2}
\operatorname{tr}
\left(
\frac1{12}\Omega_{\mu\nu}\Omega_{\mu\nu}
+\frac12E^2
\right)
\quad
+
\hbox{total derivatives and curvature-free terms},
}
$$

and inserting:

$$
\boxed{
E_{1,\mu\nu}=-2\,{\rm ad}(F_{\mu\nu}),
\qquad
E_0=0,
\qquad
\operatorname{tr}_{ad}({\rm ad}F_{\mu\nu}{\rm ad}F_{\mu\nu})
=
C_2(G)\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}F_{\mu\nu}),
}
$$

gives:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_g
\left(
\frac12 a_4(\Delta_{1,A})
-a_4(\Delta_{0,A})
\right)
=
\frac{11\,C_2(G)}{3(4\pi)^2}.
}
$$

The finite proper-time shell integral contributes the logarithmic scale factor:

$$
\boxed{
\int_{a_n^2}^{b^2a_n^2}\frac{dt}{t}
=
2\log b,
}
$$

with the factor of two already absorbed by the normalization of
${\mathcal O}_g$ and of $1/(2g^2)$ in the coupling coordinate.  Therefore the
coefficient of the background kinetic term is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal N}_g(\Gamma_{n}^{(1)})
=
\beta_0\log b
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
\beta_0=\frac{11\,C_2(G)}{3(4\pi)^2}.
}
$$

The sign in the coupling update follows from writing the kinetic coordinate as
$1/(2g^2)$ and then converting back to $g$:

$$
\boxed{
\frac1{g_{n+1}^2}
=
\frac1{g_n^2}
+
2\beta_0\log b
+
O(g_n^2\log b)
+
O(a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}),
}
$$

which is equivalent to:

$$
\boxed{
g_{n+1}
=
g_n-\beta_0g_n^3\log b
+
O(g_n^5)
+
O(a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}).
}
$$

This coefficient is regulator-independent for the present heat-kernel branch
for three concrete reasons.  First, the heat-kernel plaquette action has the
same principal small-link quadratic operator and the same Haar/Jacobian ghost
operator as the standard gauge-invariant lattice regularization; differences in
the plaquette kernel start in local operators of dimension above four or in a
finite scheme change of the coupling row.  Second, the Ward projection removes
longitudinal and gauge-variation descendants before the physical coupling row
is evaluated, so the determinant contributing to ${\mathcal O}_g$ is the
transverse-minus-ghost background-field determinant.  Third, the positive-flow
normalization multiplies the external curvature insertions by the fixed
nonzero smoothing factors of the heat semigroup at the chosen physical
normalization scale; those factors are already included in the row
normalization ${\mathcal N}_g({\mathcal O}_g)=1$ and cannot change the
logarithmic shell coefficient.

It remains to bound the remainder.  The terms beyond the one-loop determinant
fall into three classes:

$$
\boxed{
R_{\beta,n}
=
R_{\beta,n}^{2loop}
+
R_{\beta,n}^{lat}
+
R_{\beta,n}^{frame}.
}
$$

The two-loop and higher shell diagrams carry at least two interaction vertices
or one higher-order determinant insertion.  The BK tree-cumulant bound of Lemma
10.28g3.7b1c, applied with the two curvature response rows defining
${\mathcal N}_g$, gives:

$$
\boxed{
|R_{\beta,n}^{2loop}|
\le
C g_n^5.
}
$$

The lattice and heat-kernel remainders have positive Symanzik dimension in the
flowed source norm.  Lemma 10.28g3.7d and the weighted irrelevant contraction
of Lemmas 10.28g3.7c4c and 10.28g3.7c4cS give:

$$
\boxed{
|R_{\beta,n}^{lat}|
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}.
}
$$

Finally, changing from a finite packet row to the cofinal raw OS frame changes
the coupling coordinate by a uniformly bounded Ward-compatible normalization
matrix.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7aS, 10.28g3.7a1, 10.28g3.7c1a, 10.28g3.7c2, and
10.28g3.7c3 give:

$$
\boxed{
|R_{\beta,n}^{frame}|
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}.
}
$$

The constants are packet-uniform because all response rows are represented in
the same finite OS frame, the finite-sector determinant and physical
normalization determinant have lower bounds independent of the packet, and the
shell cumulant estimates are rooted estimates with constants depending only on
the physical support radius and response order.  Combining the three remainder
bounds proves the lemma.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e: Coupled M1-Irrelevant RG Corridor

Let the Ward-quotiented one-shell RG coordinate be:

$$
\boxed{
K_n=(g_n,z_n,h_n).
}
$$

Here $g_n$ is the untyped Yang-Mills kinetic coordinate, $z_n$ collects the
vacuum, anisotropy, typed, and Ward-normalization coordinates that are reset by
the finite counterterm equations, and:

$$
\boxed{
h_n=Q_{>4}K_n\in{\mathfrak K}_{irr}.
}
$$

For all sufficiently large $n$, the one-shell map of Definition 10.28g3.7c4b
has the coupled form:

$$
\boxed{
g_{n+1}
=
g_n-\beta_0g_n^3\log b+R_{g,n},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
h_{n+1}
=
L_{irr,n}h_n+G_n(g_n,h_n,a_n).
}
$$

The constants below are independent of packet index, cutoff, and volume.  There
are $C_g,C_h,C_s<\infty$, $\kappa_{RG}>0$, $\kappa_{dim}>0$, and a contraction
constant $0<q_{irr}<1$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
|R_{g,n}|
\le
C_g\left(g_n^5+\|h_n\|_{irr,n}^{2}+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\right),
}
$$

$$
\boxed{
\|L_{irr,n}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1}
\le
q_{irr},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\|G_n(g_n,h_n,a_n)\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
C_h\left(
g_n^2\tau_+^{\kappa_{dim}}
+
a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}
+
\|h_n\|_{irr,n}^{2}
+
\|h_n\|_{irr,n}g_n^2
\right).
}
$$

Moreover, the reset coordinates satisfy:

$$
\boxed{
\|z_{n+1}\|
\le
C_s\left(g_n^2+\|h_n\|_{irr,n}+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\right),
}
$$

and do not feed a new untyped marginal direction into $g_{n+1}$ except through
the displayed remainder $R_{g,n}$.

Choose $g_*>0$, $r_*>0$, and $n_0$ so that:

$$
\boxed{
C_g(g_*^2+r_*^2)\le\frac14\beta_0\log b,
\qquad
C_h(g_*^2+r_*)\le\frac14(1-q_{irr}),
\qquad
\beta_0g_*^2\log b\le\frac12,
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
C_g a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\le\frac14\beta_0g_n^3\log b,
\qquad
C_h a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\le\frac14(1-q_{irr})r_*
\qquad
\hbox{on the chosen cofinal RG tail }(n\ge n_0).
}
$$

Then the corridor:

$$
\boxed{
0<g_n\le g_*,
\qquad
\|h_n\|_{irr,n}\le r_*,
}
$$

is invariant under one RG step for $n\ge n_0$, after the relevant, typed, and
Ward coordinates are reset by the printed counterterm equations.  Inside this
corridor:

$$
\boxed{
g_{n+1}
\le
g_n-\frac12\beta_0g_n^3\log b,
}
$$

on that cofinal tail, and:

$$
\boxed{
\|h_{n+1}\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
q_{irr}\|h_n\|_{irr,n}
+
C_h g_n^2\tau_+^{\kappa_{dim}}
+
C_h a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}
+
C_h\|h_n\|_{irr,n}^{2}
+
C_h g_n^2\|h_n\|_{irr,n}.
}
$$

Consequently the nonautonomous irrelevant cocycle is uniformly stable:

$$
\boxed{
\|h_{n+r}\|_{irr,n+r}
\le
(q_{irr}^{env})^{r}\|h_n\|_{irr,n}
+
\frac{2C_h}{1-q_{irr}^{env}}
\sup_{j\ge n}
\left(g_j^2\tau_+^{\kappa_{dim}}+a_j^{\kappa_{RG}}\right)
}
$$

after decreasing $g_*$ and $r_*$ once more if necessary.

Finally, the positive-flow running-coupling window used later in NT is obtained
inside this same corridor.  Let $\mu=\tau^{-1/2}$ and define $g(\mu)$ by the
one-step coordinate above.  Iterating the beta inequality gives:

$$
\boxed{
\frac1{g(\mu_2)^2}
\ge
\frac1{g(\mu_1)^2}
 +
\beta_0\log(\mu_2/\mu_1)
 -
C
}
$$

for $\mu_2>\mu_1$ in the corridor.  Hence, for sufficiently large $\mu_-$ and a
fixed finite ratio $\mu_+/\mu_-$, the window:

$$
\boxed{
W=[\mu_+^{-2},\mu_-^{-2}]
}
$$

satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
0<g_-\le g(\tau)\le g_+\le g_*,
\qquad
g_+\le2g_-,
\qquad
g_+\hbox{ arbitrarily small}.
}
$$

Proof.  The $g$ equation is Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta, with one addition: if an
irrelevant perturbation $h_n$ is present, the coupling row sees it only through
two marked irrelevant insertions or through one irrelevant insertion followed by
the positive-dimension projection back to the coupling row.  The first
contribution is bounded by the Banach analytic remainder estimate of Lemma
10.28g3.7c4d.  The second is part of the triangular mixing estimate and carries
the same positive Symanzik dimension factor already included in
$a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}$.  This gives the printed bound for $R_{g,n}$.

The $h$ equation is the irrelevant projection of the same Banach map.  Its
linear part is exactly:

$$
\boxed{
L_{irr,n}=Q_{>4}{\mathsf S}_b(I+{\mathsf A}_n)Q_{>4}.
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g3.7c4c gives the strict operator norm bound, Corollary
10.28g3.7c4c0 states the same bound as the weighted derivative estimate
$\|D_hRG(g,0)\|_{irr}\le q_{irr}<1$ after the marginal $F^2$ row is projected
into the running coupling, and Lemma 10.28g3.7c4cS gives the fixed-space spectral
and cocycle version.  The nonlinear
terms are connected cumulants with either two marked irrelevant vertices, one
irrelevant vertex and one marginal vertex, or a pure generated irrelevant local
operator after the dimension-at-most-four block has been projected out.  Lemma
10.28g3.7b1c gives the first two terms, while the positive-flow Symanzik
dimension gap gives the source term $g_n^2\tau_+^{\kappa_{dim}}$ and the lattice
source term $a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}$.

The coordinate $z_n$ is finite-dimensional after the Ward, typed, and vacuum
quotients are separated.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7c1a through 10.28g3.7c3 give a
uniformly invertible normalization matrix and a uniformly bounded scheme change,
so the reset coordinates obey the displayed finite-dimensional bound.  The block
triangular form of the counterterm matrix prevents these coordinates from
creating a new untyped marginal coordinate; their only effect on the coupling
row is through the already estimated remainder.

The corridor estimates are elementary.  The beta bound and the first
one-quarter inequality give:

$$
\boxed{
g_{n+1}
\le
g_n-\beta_0g_n^3\log b
+\frac14\beta_0g_n^3\log b
+\frac14\beta_0g_n^3\log b,
}
$$

which is the displayed half-beta decrease.  The irrelevant estimate follows by
combining the contraction bound with the second one-quarter inequality and then
choosing $r_*$ and $g_*$ so that the quadratic and mixed terms are absorbed by
the remaining part of $(1-q_{irr})r_*$.  Iterating the nonautonomous contraction
gives the cocycle bound.

The running-coupling window is then a consequence of the same beta inequality.
Summing the reciprocal-coupling estimate over shells gives logarithmic decrease
of $g$ toward the ultraviolet.  A short fixed-ratio window at sufficiently large
$\mu$ has bounded coupling ratio, while the absolute coupling can be made as
small as needed.  This is the window used in Definition 10.28g5.1a and Lemma
10.28g5.1c.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7c4: Packet-Uniform Upgrade Of The Finite-Packet RG Chart

The finite-packet estimates used in Theorem 10.34 and Theorem 10.43 admit a
packet-uniform version on the cofinal positive-flow frame tower of Lemma
10.28g3.7aU.  More precisely, for every fixed physical support radius, positive
flow time, Sobolev order, source radius, and response order, there are constants:

$$
\boxed{
C_{\beta},\ C_{mix},\ C_{op},\ C_{irr}<\infty,
\qquad
0<q_{irr}<1,
\qquad
\kappa_{RG}>0,
}
$$

independent of packet index, cutoff, and volume, such that the one-shell
positive-flow RG chart is the Banach map ${\mathscr R}_n$ of Definition
10.28g3.7c4b and has the following estimates in the RG kernel norm of Definition
10.28g3.7c.  Here $q_{irr}$ is chosen larger than the explicit envelope
$q_{irr}^{env}=\sup_{n\ge n_0}\|L_{irr,n}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1}$ from Lemma
10.28g3.7c4c and smaller than one.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4cS identifies the same
constant as a spectral-radius envelope for the fixed-space conjugates
$\widehat L_{irr,n}$.  The beta estimate below is supplied by Lemma
10.28g3.7c4beta, and the coupled invariant weak-coupling corridor is Theorem
10.28g3.7c4e.

Beta and relevant-coordinate estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\left|
g_{n+1}-g_n+\beta_0g_n^3\log b
\right|
\le
C_{\beta}\left(g_n^5+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\right).
}
$$

Uniform operator-basis and triangular mixing estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\|\Pi_{\le4}K_n\|_{RG}
\le
C_{op}\|K_n\|_{RG},
\qquad
\|\Pi_{phys}D{\mathscr R}_n Q_{>4}\|_{RG\to RG}
\le
C_{mix}a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}.
}
$$

Irrelevant contraction estimate:

$$
\boxed{
\|L_{irr,n}\|_{irr,n\to irr,n+1}
\le
q_{irr}
\qquad(n\ge n_0),
}
$$

and the nonlinear remainder obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\|Q_{>4}({\mathscr R}_n(K+H)-{\mathscr R}_n(K)-D{\mathscr R}_n(K)H)\|_{irr,n+1}
\le
C_{irr}\|H\|_{irr,n}^{2}
+
C_{irr}a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\|H\|_{irr,n}.
}
$$

Thus the packetwise constants in Theorem 10.34 and Theorem 10.43 are replaced,
inside subsection 10.28g3, by the explicit packet-uniform constants above.

Proof.  Theorem 10.34 and Theorem 10.43 supply only finite-packet algebraic
content: the finite local operator chart, the identification of the Yang-Mills
coupling coordinate, the absence of extra untyped marginal coordinates, and
triangular mixing.  They are not used here as a source of packet-dependent
contraction or beta-remainder constants.  The
one-shell Banach RG map is constructed locally in Definition 10.28g3.7c4b, and
its irrelevant derivative is the explicit operator $L_{irr,n}$ printed there.

First, all source and response norms are put into the single cofinal OS frame
tower of Lemma 10.28g3.7aU.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7aR, 10.28g3.7aD, 10.28g3.7aS, and
10.28g3.7a1 give cutoff-compatible packet normalization, no-bad-packet
refinement, an independent OS synthesis lower bound, and a physical response
lower-frame bound.  Therefore every finite packet chart is represented in the
same flowed source envelope with uniform upper and lower frame constants.  Any
packetwise Gram inverse from Theorem 10.34 or Theorem 10.43 is replaced by:

$$
\boxed{
C_U,\quad A_{phys}^{-1},\quad B_{phys},\quad c_{norm}^{-1},\quad c_{typed}^{-1}.
}
$$

Second, the shell integration derivatives are uniformly bounded in that same
envelope.  Definition 10.28g3.7b0 and Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a1 through
10.28g3.7b0a5 verify the finite-range covariance hypotheses.  Definition
10.28g3.7b1a and Lemmas 10.28g3.7b1b through 10.28g3.7b1c print the BK shell
norm, tree weights, vertex weights, and summable shell-cumulant constant.
Consequently all multilinear derivatives of the one-shell response map through
the fixed response order have packet-independent bounds in $\|\cdot\|_{RG}$.

Third, the relevant, marginal, anisotropic, Ward, and typed coordinates are no
longer inherited from an arbitrary finite-packet chart.  Definitions
10.28g3.7c0 and 10.28g3.7c1 print the coordinate rows.  Lemmas
10.28g3.7c1s and 10.28g3.7c1a print the finite-sector determinant and
leading-block determinant lower bounds.  Lemmas 10.28g3.7c2 and 10.28g3.7c3
give a uniformly bounded Ward-compatible counterterm projection and finite
scheme stability.  Hence the coordinate projection used by Theorem 10.34 has a
packet-independent inverse bound.

The beta estimate is Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta.  That lemma computes the one-shell
coupling row directly from the heat-kernel background-field determinant,
projects through the Ward-compatible physical block, and then evaluates the
fixed positive-flow curvature two-point normalization row.  It gives the
universal coefficient $\beta_0=11C_2(G)/(3(4\pi)^2)$ and bounds the packet,
lattice, and higher-loop remainders by $C_{\beta}(g_n^5+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}})$.

Triangular mixing is the finite local statement that Ward descendants, typed
coordinates, anisotropy rows, and irrelevant rows cannot create a new untyped
bulk relevant or marginal coordinate after the Ward-compatible projection.  In
the present norm this statement is enforced by the printed block form of
Definition 10.28g3.7c1 and the bounded projection of Lemma 10.28g3.7c2.  The
only residual physical mixing from $Q_{>4}$ into $\Pi_{phys}$ carries the
positive-flow Symanzik dimension gap and is therefore $O(a_n^{\kappa_{RG}})$.

Finally, Lemma 10.28g3.7c4c proves the strict irrelevant contraction directly:
the explicit irrelevant derivative is
$L_{irr,n}=Q_{>4}{\mathsf S}_b(I+{\mathsf A}_n)Q_{>4}$, canonical scaling gives
the factor $b^{-\Delta_0}$, and the shell-cumulant perturbation
${\mathsf A}_n$ has norm $O(a_n^{\kappa_A})$.  Hence
$q_{irr}^{env}=\sup_{n\ge n_0}\|L_{irr,n}\|<1$ after discarding finitely many
initial shells, and any fixed $q_{irr}$ between this envelope and one is an
admissible contraction constant.  Corollary 10.28g3.7c4c0 restates this as the
weighted derivative bound $\|D_hRG(g,0)\|_{irr}\le q_{irr}<1$ with the marginal
$F^2$ coordinate projected into the running coupling.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4cS
strengthens this to the weighted type-pressure spectral bound and the
nonautonomous cocycle bound.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4d proves the nonlinear Banach
analytic remainder bound for the same map.  Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e then couples
these estimates to the marginal beta coordinate and proves the invariant M1
corridor used by the positive-flow construction and the NT readout.

Thus the older finite-packet theorems are used only for their algebraic
finite-chart content.  The actual Banach RG map, its derivative, the weighted
irrelevant Banach norm, and the operator whose norm and spectral-radius
sequence defines the contraction envelope $q_{irr}^{env}$ are constructed in
this subsection.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.7d: Uniform Counterterm Projection And RG Remainder Bound

For the heat-kernel one-shell kernel $K_n$ restricted to the small-curvature
chart, the renormalized remainder after counterterm projection obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\|Q_{>4}K_n\|_{RG}
\le
C a_n^\kappa.
}
$$

Moreover the projected relevant, marginal, and typed coordinates are exactly
the coordinates used in the finite source-response RG chart:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}K_n
=
\hbox{renormalized coupling, normalization, anisotropy, and typed-sector
coordinates}.
}
$$

All constants are independent of the packet index.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g3.7b gives a packet-independent bound on the full connected
shell kernel in the RG norm and tail norm.  Definition 10.28g3.7c1 defines the
counterterm coordinates by finite Ward-compatible renormalization conditions.
Lemma 10.28g3.7c2 proves that the resulting projection is uniformly bounded
on the physical response quotient, and Lemma 10.28g3.7c3 proves scheme
stability under finite Ward-compatible changes of normalization packet.
Therefore applying
$\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}$ cannot introduce packet-dependent inverse Jacobians.

The positive-flow Symanzik dimension gap gives a factor $a_n^\kappa$ for the
irrelevant projected complement.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4 upgrades the finite-packet
operator chart, triangular mixing statement, and irrelevant contraction from
Theorem 10.34 and Theorem 10.43 to the uniform cofinal frame tower used here.
Therefore the relevant, marginal, anisotropic, and typed pieces are exactly the
printed coordinates of Definitions 10.28g3.7c0 and 10.28g3.7c1, and the
displayed bound is uniform over every finite projection packet.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g3.8: One-Step Shell Comparison

Let $B_n$ be the raw OS-frame heat-kernel blocking step of Definition
10.28g3.2a, descending to physical finite source jets by Lemma 10.28g3.2b, from
cutoff $a_n$ to $a_{n+1}$ along the asymptotically free heat-kernel trajectory.
For every fixed physical support radius, positive flow time, Sobolev order, and
source radius, there are
constants $C<\infty$ and $\kappa>0$, independent of the packet index, such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{(r_0)}-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_n\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C a_n^\kappa
+C a_n^{\kappa_{LF}}.
}
$$

Proof.  Let $J\in J^{r_0}{\mathcal A}_{m,n+1}$ be a finite blocked source jet
with norm at most one.  Write the one-step heat-kernel integral at cutoff $n$ as
the sum of the small-curvature cell and its complement:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}(J^{r_0}B_nJ)
=
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{sf}(J^{r_0}B_nJ)
+
{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{lf}(J^{r_0}B_nJ).
}
$$

On the small-curvature cell, integrate the shell variables, apply the
Ward-compatible counterterm projection, and rescale.  The resulting connected
kernel is:

$$
\boxed{
K_n^{sf}
=
\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}K_n
+
Q_{>4}K_n
+
K_n^{blk}
+
K_n^{disc}.
}
$$

Here $\Pi_{\le4}^{R,k,\tau}K_n$ is the renormalized relevant, marginal,
anisotropic, and typed coordinate block; $Q_{>4}K_n$ is the irrelevant
renormalized shell remainder; $K_n^{blk}$ is the finite source mismatch between
blocking the source before integration and evaluating the coarse positive-flow
source after integration; and $K_n^{disc}$ is the lattice/heat-kernel
discretization remainder in the flowed source coordinates.

Thus the response difference decomposes as:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{aligned}
{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{(r_0)}(J)
-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}(J^{r_0}B_nJ)
&=
{\mathcal E}_{\le4,n}(J)
\\
&\quad+
{\mathcal E}_{irr,n}(J)
\\
&\quad+
{\mathcal E}_{blk,n}(J)
\\
&\quad+
{\mathcal E}_{disc,n}(J)
\\
&\quad+
{\mathcal E}_{lf,n}(J).
\end{aligned}
}
$$

The five terms are defined by applying the finite response jet to the five
corresponding pieces:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{rcl}
{\mathcal E}_{\le4,n}
&=&
\hbox{coarse relevant/typed response minus the projected shell coordinates},
\\[1mm]
{\mathcal E}_{irr,n}
&=&
\hbox{response of }Q_{>4}K_n,
\\[1mm]
{\mathcal E}_{blk,n}
&=&
\hbox{response of }K_n^{blk},
\\[1mm]
{\mathcal E}_{disc,n}
&=&
\hbox{response of }K_n^{disc},
\\[1mm]
{\mathcal E}_{lf,n}
&=&
{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{lf}-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{lf}\circ J^{r_0}B_n .
\end{array}
}
$$

This is the comparison identity.  It is an identity of finite jets at finite
cutoff and finite volume, before any limit is taken.

On the small-curvature chart, Lemma 10.28g2.1a gives a local small-link gauge
after the sector labels are separated.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4 supplies the local
positive-flow source chart in packet-uniform form: the marginal beta estimate,
operator-basis control, triangular mixing, and irrelevant contraction all use
constants defined inside subsection 10.28g3.

The uniformity is supplied by Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 and Lemmas 10.28g3.7aU through
10.28g3.7d, not by compactness alone.  Lemma 10.28g3.7q2 constructs the
finite-cutoff OS frame and shared refinement schedule, Lemma 10.28g3.7aU
summarizes the resulting uniform raw OS tower, Lemma 10.28g3.7aD gives the
no-bad-packet refinement estimates, Lemma
10.28g3.7aS gives the independent OS synthesis lower bound, and Lemma
10.28g3.7a1 prevents degeneration of the physical response Gram after Ward,
vacuum, and typed null directions are removed.  Definition 10.28g3.7b0, Lemma
10.28g3.7b0a, Lemma 10.28g3.7b0b, and Lemma 10.28g3.7b1 give the finite
gauge-fixed shell measure, its elliptic finite-range covariance, the heat-kernel
interaction/Jacobian bounds, and the tree-cumulant estimate behind the connected
kernel bound of Lemma 10.28g3.7b.  Definition 10.28g3.7c, Definition
10.28g3.7c0, Definition 10.28g3.7c1, Lemma 10.28g3.7c1s, Lemma
10.28g3.7c1a, Lemma 10.28g3.7c2, Lemma 10.28g3.7c3, Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta,
Lemma 10.28g3.7c4, Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e, and Lemma 10.28g3.7d define the RG
kernel norm, print the finite-sector pivot determinant and leading-block
determinant bound, perform the Ward-compatible bounded counterterm projection,
prove scheme stability, compute the heat-kernel one-shell beta coordinate,
upgrade the finite-packet RG chart constants, couple the beta coordinate to the
irrelevant contraction corridor, and bound the irrelevant renormalized remainder.

These estimates land on the five terms as follows:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal E}_{\le4,n}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C\left(g_n^5+a_n^{\kappa_{RG}}\right),
}
$$

by Lemma 10.28g3.7c4beta and the Ward-compatible normalization matrix;

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal E}_{irr,n}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{RG}},
}
$$

by Lemma 10.28g3.7d and the irrelevant contraction estimates of Lemma
10.28g3.7c4 and Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e;

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal E}_{blk,n}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{blk}},
}
$$

by the raw OS-frame blocking construction of Definition 10.28g3.2a, the quotient
compatibility of Lemma 10.28g3.2b, the finite-jet bound of Lemma 10.28g3.2c, and
the source refinement estimate of Lemma 10.28g3.7q2;

and:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal E}_{disc,n}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{disc}},
}
$$

by the heat-kernel interaction/Jacobian bounds and the positive-flow Symanzik
dimension gap.  With:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa=\min(\kappa_{RG},\kappa_{blk},\kappa_{disc}),
}
$$

the small-field shell comparison has the packet-independent bound:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{(r_0)}-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_n\|_{m,r_0,small}
\le
C a_n^\kappa.
}
$$

The complement of the small-curvature chart is a union of large-field polymers.
The term ${\mathcal E}_{lf,n}$ is exactly the connected response generated by
those polymers after the same source blocking is inserted.  Theorem 10.28g2.6
and Corollary 10.28g2.6a bound its total contribution to all connected source
responses by:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal R}_{n+1,m}^{(r_0)}-{\mathcal R}_{n,m}^{(r_0)}\circ B_n\|_{m,r_0,large}
\le
C a_n^{\kappa_{LF}}.
}
$$

The non-anisotropic irrelevant contraction is the packet-uniform contraction
printed in Lemma 10.28g3.7c4 and coupled to the running coordinate in Theorem
10.28g3.7c4e.  It is applied inside the same flowed envelope, so it introduces
no packet-dependent inverse Jacobian.  Taking the supremum over
unit finite source jets in the comparison identity gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal E}_{\le4,n}
+{\mathcal E}_{irr,n}
+{\mathcal E}_{blk,n}
+{\mathcal E}_{disc,n}
+{\mathcal E}_{lf,n}\|_{m,r_0}
\le
C a_n^\kappa
+
C a_n^{\kappa_{LF}}.
}
$$

This is exactly the displayed one-step response comparison estimate.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g3.9: M1 One-Step RG Receipt

For the heat-kernel regulator at bounded positive flow, the uniform one-step RG
receipt of Definition 10.28g3.2 holds at every fixed response order along any
cofinal cutoff sequence for which:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n a_n^{\kappa_*}<\infty,
\qquad
\kappa_*=\min(\kappa,\kappa_{LF}).
}
$$

Proof.  Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e supplies the coupled M1 corridor: the running
coupling remains in the weak positive-flow window, the irrelevant block is a
strict Banach contraction in the weighted norm, and the relevant, typed, and Ward
coordinates are reset without creating a new untyped marginal direction.  Lemma
10.28g3.8 then supplies the one-step comparison estimate with:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_n=C'a_n^{\kappa_*}.
}
$$

The displayed summability assumption gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n\epsilon_n<\infty.
}
$$

Exact finite-packet functoriality is the zero-spectator functoriality stated in
