Definition 10.28g3.2.  It follows because the finite source jet at the origin is
unchanged by padding the source vector with coordinates that are then set to
zero.  The blocking map itself is the raw OS-frame operator of Definition
10.28g3.2a.  Lemma 10.28g3.2b proves that it descends through the Ward, vacuum,
and typed quotients, so the blocked source is still a physical source jet.
Lemma 10.28g3.2c proves the finite-jet operator norm bound and gives the
contractive pulled-back jet norm used in the one-step receipt.  Lemma
10.28g3.2d gives packet and response-order functoriality for the same blocking
operator.  For the full positive-flow source-jet tower, Lemma 10.28g3.5a then
selects the cofinal response-order diagonal on which all finite response orders
are summable and compatible.  Thus all clauses of Definition 10.28g3.2 hold for
the full tower after that explicit diagonal.

$$
\square
$$

###### Corollary 10.28g3.10: Positive-Flow U And ER At Finite-Receipt Level

For the heat-kernel branch at bounded positive flow:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{U}_{\tau>0}
+
\mathrm{ER}_{\tau>0}
=
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS}.
}
$$

Proof.  Theorem 10.28g3.9 proves the one-step receipt required by Corollary
10.28g3.6.  Therefore the projective source functional exists without a
packet-dependent diagonal subsequence, and the cutoff error ledger is
summable.  The only diagonal choice is the response-order diagonal printed in
Lemma 10.28g3.5a.

The word PASS here is internal to the printed heat-kernel positive-flow
receipt.  It means that Definitions 10.28g3.7q0--10.28g3.7c1 and Lemmas
10.28g3.7q--10.28g3.7d have supplied the finite projections, the uniform raw OS
tower, the no-bad-packet refinement schedule, cutoff-compatible raw packet
normalization, the independent OS source-synthesis lower bound, the dual-frame
response lower bound, shell covariance/cumulant estimates, the
Ward-compatible determinant bound, and the packet-uniform upgrade of the older
finite-packet chart constants needed for the one-step comparison.  It is not an
appeal to qualitative compactness.

After Lemma 10.28g3.7q2, the uniform raw OS tower is no longer built by
Gram-Schmidt in an assumed limiting OS Hilbert space.  It is built at finite
cutoff, with rational frozen raw vectors and one shared refinement schedule.
After Lemma 10.28g3.7c4, M1 no longer leans on Theorem 10.34 or Theorem 10.43
for unprinted packet-dependent constants; it uses them only for finite-chart
algebraic content, while the constants are supplied locally in subsection
10.28g3.

$$
\square
$$

###### Ledger 10.28g3.11: U+ER Positive-Flow Hardening Receipts

The five reviewer attack points on positive-flow U and ER are recorded as
follows:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c}
\hbox{issue} & \hbox{printed receipt}\\
\hline
\hbox{finite-cutoff OS source frame, no limiting-space circularity}
&
\hbox{Lemma 10.28g3.7q2}\\
\hbox{sector-complete packet exhaustion}
&
\hbox{Definition 10.28g3.7q0 and Lemmas 10.28g3.7q--10.28g3.7s}\\
\hbox{physical response lower frame}
&
\hbox{Lemmas 10.28g3.7a--10.28g3.7a1, including 10.28g3.7aU, 10.28g3.7aR, 10.28g3.7aD, 10.28g3.7aS, and 10.28g3.7a0}\\
\hbox{heat-kernel shell covariance and cumulants}
&
\hbox{Definition 10.28g3.7b0, Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a--10.28g3.7b1, and Theorem 10.28g3.7b1d}\\
\hbox{Ward-compatible counterterm matrix}
&
\hbox{Definitions 10.28g3.7c0--10.28g3.7c1 and Lemmas 10.28g3.7c1s--10.28g3.7c3}\\
\hbox{packet-uniform upgrade of finite-packet RG chart constants}
&
\hbox{Lemma 10.28g3.7c4 and Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e}
\end{array}
}
$$

Together with the large-field estimate of Execution I, these receipts give the
one-step comparison in Lemma 10.28g3.8 and the M1 receipt in Theorem
10.28g3.9.  Thus positive-flow U and ER no longer rest on qualitative
compactness alone: the finite-energy packet tails, response-frame constants,
shell cumulants, Ward-compatible counterterm inverse, and packet-uniform
finite-chart constants are all explicit objects in the proof, and the marginal
running coordinate is coupled to the irrelevant contraction in Theorem
10.28g3.7c4e.

Thus the two targets isolated after Execution I are discharged at positive
flow:

$$
\boxed{
m_{FE}>0,
\qquad
\mathrm{M1}_{heat,\tau>0}
=
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS\ IN\ THE\ UV\ FLOW\ WINDOW}.
}
$$

The remaining C0 targets before the next two executions are the zero-flow
recovery theorem M3 and the positive UV scale readout M4-UV.  For a fully
conventional M1 submission, BGM1-BGM5
are no longer left as finite-range covariance hypotheses: Lemmas
10.28g3.7b0a1--10.28g3.7b0a5 print the tree-gauge ellipticity, zero-mode
removal, positive shell window, vector-bundle coefficient control, and boundary
extension receipts.  Likewise, Definition 10.28g3.7b1a and Lemmas
10.28g3.7b1b--10.28g3.7b1c print the BK shell norm, tree weights, vertex
weights, and the summable forest constant, while Theorem 10.28g3.7b1d derives
the shell constants used by the UV readout.  Lemma 10.28g3.7c4 supplies the
packet-uniform restatement of the finite-packet RG chart inputs, and Theorem
10.28g3.7c4e packages the marginal beta coordinate and irrelevant contraction
into one invariant weak-coupling corridor.  Thus the
remaining UV C0 targets at this point are M3 and M4-UV, not M1 at positive flow.

##### 10.28g4: Execution IV, Zero-Flow Recovery M3

Searchable execution tag:

`V4P39-C0-EXECUTE-M3-ZERO-FLOW-RECOVERY`.

The purpose of this subsection is to turn the small-flow regularity clause ZF
from a definition into a finite receipt.  The proof does not invert the heat
flow.  It constructs zero-flow local observables as renormalized limits of
positive-flow composites with a summable OS matrix-element remainder.

###### Definition 10.28g4.1: Renormalized Zero-Flow Basis And Flowed Basis

Fix a physical support radius, finite response order, Sobolev order, and
maximum engineering dimension $D$.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal B}_{\le D}^{ren}(\mu)
=
\{O_1^{ren}(\mu),\ldots,O_{N_D}^{ren}(\mu)\}
}
$$

be the finite gauge-invariant renormalized local basis after quotienting Ward
descendants, vacuum constants, and typed-sector null directions.  The basis is
ordered by engineering dimension and typed sector.

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal B}_{\le D}^{flow}(\tau)
=
\{O_1^\tau,\ldots,O_{N_D}^\tau\}
}
$$

be the corresponding positive-flow composite basis, built from the same
curvature, covariant derivatives, center, topological, and typed receipts after
heat flow time $\tau>0$.

The OS matrix-element norm for a local operator $A$ is:

$$
\boxed{
\|A\|_{OS,E,R,k}
=
\sup_{\Psi,\Phi\in{\mathcal D}_{E,R,k}}
\frac{|\langle\Psi,A\Phi\rangle_{OS}|}
{\|\Psi\|_{OS}\|\Phi\|_{OS}}.
}
$$

The domain ${\mathcal D}_{E,R,k}$ is the finite-energy local source domain used
in the finite OS-frame theorem.  All constants below are allowed to depend on
$E,R,k,D$ and the gauge group, but not on the packet, cutoff, or volume.

###### Definition 10.28g4.1a: Extended Pre-Quotient Mixing Basis

Before taking the physical quotient, use the finite extended local basis:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{ren}
=
{\mathcal P}_{\le D}
\oplus
\partial{\mathcal P}_{\le D-1}
\oplus
{\mathcal W}_{\le D}
\oplus
{\mathcal T}_{\le D}
\oplus
{\mathcal V}_{\le D}
\oplus
{\mathcal X}_{\le D}.
}
$$

The summands are:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{ll}
{\mathcal P}_{\le D} & \hbox{gauge-invariant physical scalar/tensor local
operators}\\
\partial{\mathcal P}_{\le D-1} & \hbox{total derivative descendants with
compactly supported test functions}\\
{\mathcal W}_{\le D} & \hbox{Ward-exact, equivalently BRST-exact after
gauge-fixing, descendants}\\
{\mathcal T}_{\le D} & \hbox{topological density sectors and their derivative
descendants}\\
{\mathcal V}_{\le D} & \hbox{vacuum constants and lower-dimensional vacuum
subtractions}\\
{\mathcal X}_{\le D} & \hbox{typed-sector null or superselection bookkeeping
directions}.
\end{array}
}
$$

The flowed extended basis ${\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{flow}(\tau)$ is obtained by
replacing the bare curvature and covariant derivatives in the same list by their
positive-flow versions.  The physical basis
${\mathcal B}_{\le D}^{ren}$ is the quotient of
${\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{ren}$ by the Ward-exact, vacuum, and typed-null
directions, while retaining the physical topological sectors that survive the
chosen typed-sector projection.

Let:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{phys}:
{\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{ren}
\longrightarrow
{\mathcal B}_{\le D}^{ren}
}
$$

be the quotient projection, and let $\iota_{phys}$ be a finite section chosen by
the OS lower-frame construction of subsection 10.28g3.7.

This definition is deliberately pre-quotient.  Total derivatives, Ward/BRST
exact directions, topological terms, vacuum subtractions, and typed bookkeeping
are visible before the final physical matrix is formed.

###### Lemma 10.28g4.1b: Extended Small-Flow Mixing Matrix

At finite cutoff and volume, there is a finite matrix
$M_{\rm ext}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{flow,a}(\tau)
=
M_{\rm ext}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)\,
{\mathcal E}_{\le D}^{ren,a}(\mu)
+
{\mathcal R}_{\rm ext}^{a,D}(\tau).
}
$$

With the ordering of Definition 10.28g4.1a, the matrix has the block triangular
form:

$$
\boxed{
M_{\rm ext}^{a,D}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
M_{PP} & M_{P\partial} & M_{PW} & M_{PT} & M_{PV} & M_{PX}\\
0 & M_{\partial\partial} & M_{\partial W} & M_{\partial T} & M_{\partial V} & M_{\partial X}\\
0 & 0 & M_{WW} & M_{WT} & M_{WV} & M_{WX}\\
0 & 0 & 0 & M_{TT} & M_{TV} & M_{TX}\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & M_{VV} & M_{VX}\\
0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & 0 & M_{XX}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
$$

The Ward/BRST-exact block is invariant under the mixing matrix:

$$
\boxed{
M_{\rm ext}^{a,D}{\mathcal W}_{\le D}
\subset
{\mathcal W}_{\le D}\oplus{\mathcal V}_{\le D}\oplus{\mathcal X}_{\le D}.
}
$$

Vacuum subtractions stay in the vacuum block, total derivatives stay in the
derivative ideal up to Ward-exact and vacuum terms, and topological sectors mix
only with sectors of the same typed topological charge and with total
derivatives allowed by the local descent equations.

The same-dimension physical block factors as:

$$
\boxed{
M_{PP}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)
=
H_{PP}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)\,
{\mathcal P}\exp
\left[
\frac12\int_\mu^{1/\sqrt{\tau}}
\Gamma_{PP}^{D}(g(s))\,d\log s
\right],
}
$$

with analogous finite block formulas for the derivative and topological
same-dimension sectors.

At fixed positive flow time, the continuum extended matrix is the finite OS
matrix-element limit:

$$
\boxed{
M_{\rm ext}^{D}(\tau,\mu)
=
\lim_{a\downarrow0,\ L\uparrow\infty}
M_{\rm ext}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu).
}
$$

Proof.  Construct the matrix by evaluating a finite dual OS source frame on the
finite extended flowed basis.  The extended basis is finite, so the coefficient
matrix is obtained by solving an ordinary finite linear system in the
pre-quotient space.  Gauge invariance of the flowed observables and the exact
finite-cutoff Ward identities make the Ward/BRST-exact span an invariant ideal.
Translation covariance sends total derivatives to total derivatives after
integration by parts against compactly supported test functions, with only
contact terms; those contact terms are precisely the lower-dimensional vacuum
and Ward-exact blocks.  Local topological densities are closed under the same
short-flow expansion, except for total-derivative descent terms and typed-sector
bookkeeping.

Triangularity follows from engineering dimension: a local shell integration
cannot create a higher-dimension counterterm without a positive power of the
flow radius, and such terms are placed in the remainder.  Same-dimension
operators mix through the usual logarithmic anomalous-dimension matrix.  The
finite-dimensional RG equation for the same-dimension block is solved by the
path-ordered exponential shown above, while the finite matching matrix $H$ stores
non-logarithmic scheme-dependent constants at the reference scale.  This
constructs the full pre-quotient matrix before any physical quotient or
determinant lower bound is invoked.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.2: Triangular Small-Flow Counterterm Matrix

Let:

$$
\boxed{
L_\tau=1+\left|\log(\mu^2\tau)\right|.
}
$$

There is a Ward-compatible triangular matrix:

$$
\boxed{
Z(\tau,\mu)
=
\left(Z_{ij}(\tau,\mu)\right)_{1\le i,j\le N_D}
}
$$

It is obtained from the extended pre-quotient matrix by:

$$
\boxed{
Z^D(\tau,\mu)
=
\Pi_{phys}\,
M_{\rm ext}^{D}(\tau,\mu)\,
\iota_{phys}.
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
O_i^\tau
=
\sum_{j:\dim O_j\le\dim O_i}
Z_{ij}(\tau,\mu)O_j^{ren}(\mu)
+
R_i^\tau .
}
$$

The diagonal blocks are invertible with log-tempered inverse.  More precisely,
for every finite dimension and typed-sector block there are constants
$C_D<\infty$ and $p_D<\infty$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
\sigma_{\min}
\left(
Z_{\Delta,typed}(\tau,\mu)
\right)
\ge
C_D^{-1}L_\tau^{-p_D},
\qquad
\|Z_{\Delta,typed}(\tau,\mu)\|
\le
C_D L_\tau^{p_D}.
}
$$

Ward descendants and vacuum constants do not appear in the physical diagonal
block.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g4.1b constructs the full pre-quotient mixing matrix with
physical, total-derivative, Ward/BRST-exact, topological, vacuum, and typed
blocks.  Because the Ward/BRST-exact, vacuum, and typed-null subspaces are
invariant ideals for that matrix, the quotient projection $\Pi_{phys}$ is
well-defined on the matrix product.  The finite section $\iota_{phys}$ selects
the OS-normalized representatives of the physical quotient.  Therefore
$Z^D=\Pi_{phys}M_{\rm ext}^{D}\iota_{phys}$ is a genuine physical counterterm
matrix, not a postulated inverse.

The block triangular form of $M_{\rm ext}^{D}$ descends to $Z^D$.  Total
derivative terms either remain as derivative physical observables when the test
function keeps them, or become lower-dimensional contact terms by integration by
parts; Ward/BRST-exact and vacuum pieces vanish in the physical quotient; typed
null directions are removed; topological sectors remain only in their typed
physical blocks.  Hence no untyped physical operator is generated by quotienting.

The diagonal physical block is not asserted to be uniformly bounded away from
zero as $\tau\downarrow0$.  Its flow-time dependence is governed by the
finite-dimensional anomalous-dimension equation printed in Lemma
10.28g4.2a below.  On every finite block, the path-ordered exponential of that
equation has at most a finite power of $L_\tau$ in norm and inverse norm, while
the finite matching matrix at the reference scale is bounded above and below by
the finite OS lower-frame determinant receipts of Lemmas 10.28g3.7c1s and
10.28g3.7c1a.  Multiplying these two finite matrices gives the displayed
log-tempered singular-value bound.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.2a: Finite-Cutoff Flowed OPE With Anomalous Logs

At every finite cutoff $a$ and finite volume $L$, after Ward projection and
typed-sector quotient, the flowed basis satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
O_i^{\tau,a}
=
\sum_{\Delta_j\le D}
C_{ij}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)
O_j^{ren,a}(\mu)
+
{\mathcal R}_{i,D}^{\tau,a}.
}
$$

The coefficient matrix has the factorization:

$$
\boxed{
C^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)
=
H^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)\,
U_\Gamma^{D}(\tau,\mu).
}
$$

Here $H^{a,D}$ is triangular by engineering dimension and typed sector, with
uniformly bounded matrix norm and inverse on the finite block, and
$U_\Gamma^{D}$ is the path-ordered anomalous-dimension transport:

$$
\boxed{
U_\Gamma^{D}(\tau,\mu)
=
{\mathcal P}
\exp\left[
\frac12
\int_{\mu}^{1/\sqrt{\tau}}
\Gamma_D(g(s))\,d\log s
\right].
}
$$

The finite matrix $\Gamma_D(g)$ is block upper triangular, preserves Ward and
typed quotients, and is the anomalous-dimension matrix of the renormalized
zero-flow basis:

$$
\boxed{
\mu\frac{d}{d\mu}
O^{ren,a}_{\le D}(\mu)
=
-\Gamma_D(g(\mu))O^{ren,a}_{\le D}(\mu)
+O(a^\rho).
}
$$

Consequently, on every finite block:

$$
\boxed{
\|U_\Gamma^{D}(\tau,\mu)\|
+\|(U_\Gamma^{D}(\tau,\mu))^{-1}\|
\le
C_D L_\tau^{p_D}.
}
$$

The continuum coefficient matrix in Lemma 10.28g4.2 is the fixed-positive-flow
limit:

$$
\boxed{
Z^D(\tau,\mu)
=
\lim_{a\downarrow0,\ L\uparrow\infty}
C^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)
}
$$

in the finite OS matrix-element topology.

Proof.  Work with lattice flowed composites at positive flow time.  Their
support is contained in a ball of physical radius comparable to $\sqrt{\tau}$
up to exponentially small heat-kernel tails.  In a finite-energy OS matrix
element, insert the Wilsonian shell decomposition from subsection 10.28g3.7b.
Integrating shells between scales $\mu$ and $1/\sqrt{\tau}$ produces local
counterterms supported in the same physical ball.  Gauge invariance and the
Ward quotient force the counterterms to lie in the gauge-invariant local basis;
engineering dimension gives triangularity; typed-sector projectors block
diagonalize the physical part.

At each shell, the logarithmically divergent same-dimension part is the finite
matrix $\Gamma_D(g)d\log s$.  Higher-dimension insertions are irrelevant and are
placed in the remainder.  The product over shells gives the displayed
path-ordered exponential.  Since asymptotic freedom gives $g(s)^2\lesssim
1/\log s$ along the heat-kernel trajectory and $\Gamma_D(g)$ is a finite
polynomial matrix beginning at order $g^2$, the integral of its norm grows at
most like a constant times $\log L_\tau$.  A finite-dimensional Gronwall
estimate gives the log-tempered bound on $U_\Gamma^{D}$ and its inverse.

The finite matching matrix $H^{a,D}$ contains only non-logarithmic matching at
the reference scale and lattice artifacts.  The finite OS-frame lower bounds of
subsection 10.28g3.7 and the Ward-compatible counterterm determinant of Lemma
10.28g3.7c2 bound $H^{a,D}$ and its inverse uniformly for small cutoff.  This
proves the finite-cutoff OPE coefficient formula before any continuum limit is
taken.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.2b: Uniform OS Remainder Bound Before The Continuum Limit

For the finite basis cutoff $D$, define:

$$
\boxed{
\alpha_D
=
\frac12
\min_i
\left(
\Delta_{\rm next}(i)-\Delta_i
\right)
>0,
}
$$

where $\Delta_{\rm next}(i)$ is the smallest retained or generated engineering
dimension strictly above the truncation level relevant to $O_i$.  Then there
are constants $C_D<\infty$, $\rho_D>0$, and $\sigma_D\ge0$, independent of
packet, cutoff, and volume, such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathcal R}_{i,D}^{\tau,a}\|_{OS,E,R,k}
\le
C_D L_\tau^{p_D}
\left(
\tau^{\alpha_D}
+
a^{\rho_D}\tau^{-\sigma_D}
\right).
}
$$

Proof.  Split the remainder into four finite-shell classes.

First, local Taylor terms of the heat-flow kernel beyond dimension $D$ carry an
extra factor of $\tau^{\alpha_D}$ by parabolic scaling.  The finite-energy OS
norm of their coefficients is controlled by the weighted irrelevant Banach norm
of Lemma 10.28g3.7c4a and the spectral irrelevant bound of Lemma
10.28g3.7c4cS.

Second, same-dimension logarithmic insertions are not left in the remainder:
they are exactly the anomalous-dimension transport of Lemma 10.28g4.2a.

Third, connected shell cumulants created by the local expansion are bounded by
the BK forest estimate of Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c.  The tree weights are summable in
the same OS source norm and contribute only the finite block constant and the
log-tempered factor already shown.

Fourth, lattice-flow and lattice-derivative artifacts are bounded by comparing
the lattice heat kernel and covariant difference operators with their continuum
positive-flow counterparts.  Positive flow supplies smoothing over radius
$\sqrt{\tau}$, so each artifact has the form $a^{\rho_D}\tau^{-\sigma_D}$.
Large-field contributions are bounded by the heat-kernel polymer receipt of
Theorem 10.28g2.6 and are summable uniformly on the finite-energy source domain.

All four estimates are proved at finite cutoff and finite volume.  The constants
are packet-uniform because the OS source frame, shell covariance, and finite
counterterm projectors are the packet-uniform objects constructed in
subsection 10.28g3.7.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.3: Small-Flow OS Matrix-Element Expansion

There are constants $C_D<\infty$, $\alpha_D>0$, $\rho_D>0$, $\sigma_D\ge0$,
and $p_D<\infty$ such that for every operator in the flowed basis, uniformly at
finite cutoff before the continuum limit:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
O_i^{\tau,a}
-
\sum_{j:\dim O_j\le D}
Z_{ij}^{a,D}(\tau,\mu)O_j^{ren,a}(\mu)
\right\|_{OS,E,R,k}
\le
C_D L_\tau^{p_D}
\left(
\tau^{\alpha_D}
+
a^{\rho_D}\tau^{-\sigma_D}
\right).
}
$$

After first taking the continuum limit at fixed positive $\tau$, the estimate
becomes:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
O_i^\tau
-
\sum_{j:\dim O_j\le D}
Z_{ij}^{D}(\tau,\mu)O_j^{ren}(\mu)
\right\|_{OS,E,R,k}
\le
C_D L_\tau^{p_D}\tau^{\alpha_D}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g4.2a constructs the finite-cutoff coefficient matrix with
the anomalous logarithms explicit.  Lemma 10.28g4.2b gives the finite-cutoff OS
remainder estimate.  The continuum-at-fixed-flow estimate follows by Theorem
10.28g3.9, because the lattice artifact term tends to zero at fixed $\tau$.
The log-tempered factor is harmless for the later zero-flow limit: for every
$\epsilon>0$ there is $C_{\epsilon,D}$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
L_\tau^{p_D}
\le
C_{\epsilon,D}\tau^{-\epsilon}.
}
$$

Choosing $\epsilon<\alpha_D$ leaves a positive small-flow power.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.4: Lattice-Flow Commutation Estimate

Let $O_i^{\tau,a}$ denote the cutoff flowed composite and $O_i^\tau$ the
continuum positive-flow composite obtained from the M1/M2 construction.  There
are constants $C_D<\infty$, $\rho_D>0$, and $\sigma_D\ge0$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
\|O_i^{\tau,a}-O_i^\tau\|_{OS,E,R,k}
\le
C_D a^{\rho_D}\tau^{-\sigma_D}.
}
$$

Proof.  Compare the lattice heat kernel, lattice covariant derivatives, and
finite plaquette curvature with their continuum positive-flow counterparts on
the same finite-energy source domain.  Positive flow gives smoothing over a
physical radius $\sqrt{\tau}$, so each lattice derivative error is bounded by a
positive power of $a$ and a finite negative power of $\tau$.  The shell
covariance estimates of Lemmas 10.28g3.7b0a1--10.28g3.7b0a5 control the
coefficient fields, while the BK forest bound of Lemma 10.28g3.7b1c controls
the connected source responses.  The quotient and typed-sector projections are
bounded by Lemmas 10.28g3.7c2 and 10.28g3.7c3, so the estimate passes to the
physical quotient.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.5: Summable Flow Schedule

This is a finite-stage lemma.  Fix one dimension/support/sector stage and use
the constants:

$$
\boxed{
K_D=(C_D,p_D,\alpha_D,\rho_D,\sigma_D).
}
$$

If $\sigma_D>0$, choose:

$$
\boxed{
0<\theta<\min(1,\rho_D/(2\sigma_D))
}
$$

If $\sigma_D=0$, choose:

$$
\boxed{
0<\theta<1.
}
$$

Set:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_n=a_n^{2\theta}.
}
$$

Then:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_n
L_{\tau_n}^{p_D}
\left(
\tau_n^{\alpha_D}
+a_n^{\rho_D}\tau_n^{-\sigma_D}
\right)
<\infty .
}
$$

Proof.  Since $a_n=a_0b^{-n}$, both terms are geometric:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_n^{\alpha_D}=a_n^{2\theta\alpha_D},
\qquad
a_n^{\rho_D}\tau_n^{-\sigma_D}
=
a_n^{\rho_D-2\theta\sigma_D}.
}
$$

The choice of $\theta$ makes both exponents positive.  The factor
$L_{\tau_n}^{p_D}$ grows at most polynomially in $n$, while the two powers above
decay geometrically.  Therefore the series is summable.

No uniformity in $D$, support radius, Sobolev order, or sector cutoff is claimed
in this lemma.  The exponents may degrade and the constants may grow with the
finite stage.  The cofinal diagonal construction below is the only step that
passes from finite-stage summability to the full local algebra.

$$
\square
$$

###### Definition 10.28g4.5a: Cofinal Finite-Stage Zero-Flow Tower

Let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak q}
=
(E_{\mathfrak q},R_{\mathfrak q},k_{\mathfrak q},
D_{\mathfrak q},S_{\mathfrak q})
}
$$

range over a countable cofinal ordered set of finite stages.  Here
$E_{\mathfrak q}$ is the finite-energy window, $R_{\mathfrak q}$ the physical
support radius, $k_{\mathfrak q}$ the Sobolev/source order, $D_{\mathfrak q}$
the engineering-dimension cutoff, and $S_{\mathfrak q}$ the finite retained
center, topological, boundary, and typed-sector cutoff.  The stage algebra is:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}
=
\mathrm{alg}
\left(
{\mathcal B}_{\le D_{\mathfrak q},S_{\mathfrak q}}^{ren}
(\mu;R_{\mathfrak q},k_{\mathfrak q})
\right).
}
$$

If ${\mathfrak q}\le{\mathfrak q}'$, there is an inclusion:

$$
\boxed{
I_{{\mathfrak q}{\mathfrak q}'}:
{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}
\hookrightarrow
{\mathfrak A}_{{\mathfrak q}'}^{ren}
}
$$

and a finite-stage projection back to the old quotient:

$$
\boxed{
\Pi_{{\mathfrak q}'{\mathfrak q}}:
{\mathfrak A}_{{\mathfrak q}'}^{ren}
\longrightarrow
{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}.
}
$$

The zero-flow local algebra is the algebraic inductive limit:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak A}_{loc}^{ren}
=
\varinjlim_{\mathfrak q}
{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}.
}
$$

The OS/C-star closure is taken only after matrix elements on this algebraic
inductive limit have been constructed.

For each finite stage, let:

$$
\boxed{
K_{\mathfrak q}
=
(C_{\mathfrak q},p_{\mathfrak q},\alpha_{\mathfrak q},
\rho_{\mathfrak q},\sigma_{\mathfrak q})
}
$$

be the constants supplied by Lemmas 10.28g4.2--10.28g4.5 at that stage.  These
constants are not required to be bounded as ${\mathfrak q}\to\infty$; the
exponents $\alpha_{\mathfrak q}$ and $\rho_{\mathfrak q}$ may decrease, and
$\sigma_{\mathfrak q}$ and $p_{\mathfrak q}$ may increase.

###### Lemma 10.28g4.5b: Compatibility Under Stage Enlargement

For ${\mathfrak q}\le{\mathfrak q}'$ and for every
$A\in{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}$, the flowed reconstruction computed in
stage ${\mathfrak q}'$, then projected back to stage ${\mathfrak q}$, differs
from the reconstruction computed directly in stage ${\mathfrak q}$ by a
finite-stage remainder bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
\left\|
\Pi_{{\mathfrak q}'{\mathfrak q}}
{\mathcal Z}_{{\mathfrak q}'}^{\tau,a}
I_{{\mathfrak q}{\mathfrak q}'}A
-
{\mathcal Z}_{\mathfrak q}^{\tau,a}A
\right\|_{OS,E_{\mathfrak q},R_{\mathfrak q},k_{\mathfrak q}}
\le
C_{\mathfrak q}
L_\tau^{p_{\mathfrak q}}
\left(
\tau^{\alpha_{\mathfrak q}}
+
a^{\rho_{\mathfrak q}}\tau^{-\sigma_{\mathfrak q}}
\right).
}
$$

Here ${\mathcal Z}_{\mathfrak q}^{\tau,a}$ denotes the finite-stage
counterterm reconstruction map built from the matrix $Z$.

Proof.  The extended pre-quotient matrix of Lemma 10.28g4.1b is functorial under
adding higher-dimension operators, larger support, higher Sobolev tests, or
extra retained typed sectors.  Adding a new stage appends rows and columns to
the extended block matrix.  Its block triangular form prevents higher
engineering-dimension operators from feeding back into lower-dimension physical
blocks except through the same local Taylor and shell-cumulant remainders
already estimated in Lemma 10.28g4.2b.  Enlarging support only adds operators
outside the old support or total derivative/contact terms; after projection
back to the old compact support, these are either zero or included in the same
finite-stage remainder.  Enlarging sector cutoffs refines the typed idempotents;
projection back to $S_{\mathfrak q}$ sums the refined idempotents and recovers
the old typed block.

Thus the old finite block is unchanged modulo the remainder controlled by the
old constants $K_{\mathfrak q}$.  The estimate is measured in the old OS norm,
so no constant from the larger stage ${\mathfrak q}'$ is needed.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g4.5c: Cofinal Diagonal Flow-Cutoff Schedule

There is a cofinal cutoff subsequence $(a_m,L_m)$ and a positive flow schedule
$\tau_m\downarrow0$ with:

$$
\boxed{
a_m^2\ll \tau_m
}
$$

such that, for every finite stage ${\mathfrak q}$, the stage error:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{{\mathfrak q},m}
=
C_{\mathfrak q}L_{\tau_m}^{p_{\mathfrak q}}
\left(
\tau_m^{\alpha_{\mathfrak q}}
+
a_m^{\rho_{\mathfrak q}}\tau_m^{-\sigma_{\mathfrak q}}
\right)
}
$$

is summable along the tail $m\ge m({\mathfrak q})$:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{m\ge m({\mathfrak q})}
\epsilon_{{\mathfrak q},m}
<\infty .
}
$$

This statement allows arbitrary finite-stage growth of the constants and
degradation of the exponents.  It uses only the fact that each individual stage
has positive powers $\alpha_{\mathfrak q}>0$ and $\rho_{\mathfrak q}>0$.

Proof.  Enumerate the finite stages as
${\mathfrak q}_1,{\mathfrak q}_2,\ldots$.  Suppose the first $m$ stages have
been fixed.  Let:

$$
\boxed{
J_m=\{1\le r\le m:\sigma_{{\mathfrak q}_r}>0\}.
}
$$

If $J_m$ is nonempty, choose an exponent $\theta_m$ satisfying:

$$
\boxed{
0<\theta_m<
\min_{r\in J_m}
\frac{\rho_{{\mathfrak q}_r}}{2\sigma_{{\mathfrak q}_r}},
\qquad
\theta_m<1,
}
$$

If $J_m$ is empty, choose any $0<\theta_m<1$.  For the finite set of stages
$1,\ldots,m$, each expression:

$$
\boxed{
C_{{\mathfrak q}_r}
L_{a^{2\theta_m}}^{p_{{\mathfrak q}_r}}
\left(
a^{2\theta_m\alpha_{{\mathfrak q}_r}}
+
a^{\rho_{{\mathfrak q}_r}-2\theta_m\sigma_{{\mathfrak q}_r}}
\right)
}
$$

tends to zero as $a\downarrow0$.  Pass to a sufficiently far cutoff subsequence
and set $\tau_m=a_m^{2\theta_m}$ so that:

$$
\boxed{
\epsilon_{{\mathfrak q}_r,m}
\le
2^{-(m+r)}
\qquad
1\le r\le m.
}
$$

This recursive choice is possible because only finitely many inequalities are
imposed at step $m$.  For each fixed ${\mathfrak q}_r$, summing over
$m\ge r$ gives:

$$
\boxed{
\sum_{m\ge r}
\epsilon_{{\mathfrak q}_r,m}
\le
\sum_{m\ge r}2^{-(m+r)}
<\infty .
}
$$

The condition $a_m^2\ll\tau_m$ follows from $\theta_m<1$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g4.6: M3 Zero-Flow Recovery

For the algebraic inductive-limit gauge-invariant local algebra:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathfrak A}_{loc}^{ren}
=
\varinjlim_{\mathfrak q}
{\mathfrak A}_{\mathfrak q}^{ren}
}
$$

and its OS/C-star closure after matrix elements are defined:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{M3}_{heat}
=
\mathrm{ZF}_{ren}
=
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g4.2a constructs the finite-cutoff flowed OPE coefficient
matrix, including anomalous logarithms through the finite anomalous-dimension
transport.  Lemma 10.28g4.2b proves the finite-cutoff OS matrix-element
remainder before the continuum limit.  Lemma 10.28g4.3 passes that estimate to
the continuum at fixed positive flow and keeps the log-tempered loss explicit.
Lemma 10.28g4.4 gives the independent cutoff-flow commutation error.  Lemma
10.28g4.5 gives the summability criterion at each fixed finite stage.
Definition 10.28g4.5a constructs the countable cofinal finite-stage tower.
Lemma 10.28g4.5b proves that enlarging dimension, support, Sobolev order, or
sector cutoff does not change an old observable except by the old stage's
controlled remainder.  Lemma 10.28g4.5c constructs a diagonal cofinal
flow-cutoff schedule making those old-stage remainders summable for every stage.
Therefore every element of the algebraic inductive limit
${\mathfrak A}_{loc}^{ren}$ has a unique zero-flow limit in the finite-energy OS
topology.  The OS/C-star closure is then taken after these matrix elements have
been defined on the inductive-limit algebra.

This proves zero-flow recovery as a theorem on the renormalized local algebra:
the zero-flow observable is not defined as an arbitrary convergent family; it is
the image of the triangular small-flow counterterm matrix with summable
remainder.  Ward, vacuum, and typed quotient directions have already been
removed before the matrix is inverted, so no untyped physical observable is
created by the limiting procedure.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.28g5: Execution V, Positive UV Flowed Scale Readout M4-UV

Searchable execution tag:

`V4P39-C0-EXECUTE-M4-UV-POSITIVE-FLOWED-SCALE-READOUT`.

This subsection supplies a positive-flow local scale observable before any
Wilson-area, confinement, or mass-gap predicate is evaluated.  It closes the
ultraviolet positive-flow readout target M4-UV.  It does not close full
fixed-scale nontriviality NT, which remains part of the IR bridge in subsection
10.28k.

###### Definition 10.28g5.1: Flowed Energy Readout

Let:

$$
\boxed{
E_\tau(x)
=
\frac12\operatorname{tr}(F_{\mu\nu}^{\tau}(x)F_{\mu\nu}^{\tau}(x)).
}
$$

Fix a nonzero smooth compactly supported test function $f$ with support inside
the physical source radius and define:

$$
\boxed{
E_\tau(f)
=
\int f(x)E_\tau(x)\,dx.
}
$$

The scale coordinate is:

$$
\boxed{
S_\tau(a,L)
=
\tau^2\,\omega_{a,L}(E_\tau(f_0)),
}
$$

where $f_0$ is a fixed nonnegative normalization test function with integral
one.

###### Definition 10.28g5.1a: NT Flow Window And Comparison Norm

Fix a compact positive-flow window:

$$
\boxed{
W=[\tau_-,\tau_+],
\qquad
0<\tau_-<\tau_+<\infty .
}
$$

The window is chosen inside the one-step M1 chart of subsection 10.28g3, with
renormalized running coupling bounded by:

$$
\boxed{
0<g_-\le g(\tau)\le g_+\le g_*,
\qquad
\tau\in W.
}
$$

The window is short enough that:

$$
\boxed{
g_+\le 2g_-.
}
$$

For a flowed energy observable, measure all NT errors in the same window norm:

$$
\boxed{
\|R\|_{NT,W,a,L}
=
\sup_{\tau\in W}
\left(
\left|\tau^2\omega_{a,L}(R_\tau(f_0))\right|
+
\left|
\operatorname{Cov}_{a,L}(R_\tau(f),E_\tau(f))
\right|^{1/2}
\right).
}
$$

Let:

$$
\boxed{
A_G=\frac{3\dim G}{128\pi^2}.
}
$$

Let ${\mathsf K}_{\tau}$ denote the positive-flow transverse curvature
covariance kernel in the Gaussian heat-kernel chart, with the global gauge
zero-mode and Ward directions removed as in the OS quotient.  Define:

$$
\boxed{
K_f(W)
=
\inf_{\tau\in W}
\int
f(x)f(y)
\operatorname{tr}
\left[
{\mathsf K}_{\tau}(x,y){\mathsf K}_{\tau}(y,x)
\right]
dx\,dy .
}
$$

For nonzero real $f$ whose class is not vacuum, Ward, or typed-null in the
positive-flow OS quotient:

$$
\boxed{
K_f(W)>0.
}
$$

Proof of positivity.  The heat-flow curvature covariance is a strictly positive
elliptic heat kernel on the transverse finite-energy quotient at every positive
flow time.  If the displayed quadratic form vanished for some nonzero $f$, the
flowed curvature smearing determined by $f$ would be orthogonal to the entire
transverse curvature range.  By unique continuation for the positive heat
semigroup, and by the sector-complete packet separation already proved in the
finite-cutoff OS frame theorem, this forces the class of $fE_\tau$ to be vacuum,
Ward, or typed-null.  That case is excluded by the choice of $f$.  Continuity in
$\tau$ and compactness of $W$ give the positive infimum.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g5.1b: Explicit Gaussian NT Lower Constants

In the leading Gaussian heat-kernel shell on the same window $W$:

$$
\boxed{
\tau^2\omega_{G}(E_\tau(f_0))
\ge
c_E^0,
\qquad
c_E^0=A_Gg_-^2,
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\operatorname{Var}_{G}(E_\tau(f))
\ge
c_V^0,
\qquad
c_V^0=g_-^4K_f(W).
}
$$

Proof.  The first estimate is the standard leading positive-flow energy
identity in the heat-kernel Gaussian chart:

$$
\boxed{
\tau^2\omega_G(E_\tau(f_0))
=
A_G g(\tau)^2
}
$$

because $f_0$ has integral one.  The lower bound follows from
$g(\tau)\ge g_-$.

For the variance, Wick contraction of the quadratic curvature energy gives:

$$
\boxed{
\operatorname{Var}_{G}(E_\tau(f))
=
g(\tau)^4
\int
f(x)f(y)
\operatorname{tr}
\left[
{\mathsf K}_{\tau}(x,y){\mathsf K}_{\tau}(y,x)
\right]
dx\,dy .
}
$$

The lower bound is exactly the definition of $K_f(W)$ and $g(\tau)\ge g_-$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g5.1c: Same-Window Correction Budget

There are finite constants:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{sh},B_E^{irr},B_E^{disc},B_E^{blk},B_E^{LF},
B_V^{sh},B_V^{irr},B_V^{disc},B_V^{blk},B_V^{LF}
<\infty
}
$$

and positive exponents:

$$
\boxed{
\kappa_E,\kappa_V,\rho_E,\rho_V,\eta>0,
\qquad
\sigma_E,\sigma_V\ge0,
}
$$

all measured in the NT norm of Definition 10.28g5.1a, such that the expectation
correction obeys:

$$
\boxed{
|R_E|
\le
B_E^{sh}g_+^4
+
B_E^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_E}
+
B_E^{disc}a^{\rho_E}\tau_-^{-\sigma_E}
+
B_E^{blk}\varepsilon_{blk}(a,L)
+
B_E^{LF}e^{-m_{FE}a^{-\eta}},
}
$$

and the variance correction obeys:

$$
\boxed{
|R_V|
\le
B_V^{sh}g_+^6
+
B_V^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_V}
+
B_V^{disc}a^{\rho_V}\tau_-^{-\sigma_V}
+
B_V^{blk}\varepsilon_{blk}(a,L)
+
B_V^{LF}e^{-m_{FE}a^{-\eta}}.
}
$$

Here $\varepsilon_{blk}(a,L)$ is the one-step blocking/refinement error from
Theorem 10.28g3.9, and $m_{FE}$ is the large-field collar margin from Theorem
10.28g2.6.

It is enough to choose the positive-flow window so that, in addition to
$g_+\le2g_-$:

$$
\boxed{
g_+^2
\le
\min\left\{
\frac{A_G}{64B_E^{sh}},
\frac{K_f(W)}{256B_V^{sh}}
\right\},
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_E}
\le
\frac18A_Gg_-^2,
\qquad
B_V^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_V}
\le
\frac18K_f(W)g_-^4.
}
$$

These explicit inequalities imply:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{sh}g_+^4+B_E^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_E}
\le
\frac14c_E^0,
\qquad
B_V^{sh}g_+^6+B_V^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_V}
\le
\frac14c_V^0.
}
$$

Then choose the initial cutoff and volume tail so that:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{disc}a^{\rho_E}\tau_-^{-\sigma_E}
+
B_E^{blk}\varepsilon_{blk}(a,L)
+
B_E^{LF}e^{-m_{FE}a^{-\eta}}
\le
\frac14c_E^0,
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
B_V^{disc}a^{\rho_V}\tau_-^{-\sigma_V}
+
B_V^{blk}\varepsilon_{blk}(a,L)
+
B_V^{LF}e^{-m_{FE}a^{-\eta}}
\le
\frac14c_V^0.
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
|R_E|\le\frac12c_E^0,
\qquad
|R_V|\le\frac12c_V^0.
}
$$

Proof.  The shell terms are the third and higher cumulants of the heat-kernel
small-field chart after the Ward projection.  Theorem 10.28g3.7b1d derives the
constants $B_E^{sh}$ and $B_V^{sh}$ from the shell covariance norm, the
Brydges-Kennedy forest formula, the vertex derivative bounds, the tree weights,
and the final summable forest constant; it gives order $g_+^4$ in the energy
expectation and order $g_+^6$ in the energy variance.  The irrelevant terms are
bounded by the weighted irrelevant norm and the strictly contractive irrelevant
block of Theorem 10.28g3.7c4, giving the positive powers of $\tau_+$.  The
discretization terms are exactly the small-flow cutoff errors of Lemma
10.28g4.4, evaluated on the same compact flow window and therefore with the same
$\tau_-$ denominator.
The blocking/refinement terms are bounded by the packet-uniform comparison
ledger of Theorem 10.28g3.9.  The large-field term is the polymer replacement
bound of Theorem 10.28g2.6.

The shell inequalities follow from the displayed smallness of $g_+^2$ and from
$g_+\le2g_-$.  For example:

$$
\boxed{
B_E^{sh}g_+^4
\le
\frac18A_Gg_-^2,
\qquad
B_V^{sh}g_+^6
\le
\frac18K_f(W)g_-^4.
}
$$

The irrelevant inequalities are printed separately above.  Their feasibility is
not an extra nonperturbative assumption: Theorem 10.28g3.7c4e gives the coupled
M1-irrelevant corridor.  In that corridor one may choose a short window in the
ultraviolet positive-flow regime with bounded ratio $g_+/g_-$ and arbitrarily
small $g_+$, while the irrelevant coordinate remains in the uniformly
contracting Banach ball.  The factors $\tau_+^{\kappa_E}$ and
$\tau_+^{\kappa_V}$ decay faster than any inverse power of the logarithmic
running of $g_-$, so the two irrelevant inequalities can be met after moving the
window far enough into that regime.  Once the window is fixed, the cutoff,
volume, and large-field terms vanish along the cofinal heat-kernel trajectory.
The two half-margin bounds follow by addition.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g5.2: Positive Leading UV Heat-Kernel Readout

There are positive constants $s_-,s_+,v_-$ and a positive flow window:

$$
\boxed{
\tau\in[\tau_-,\tau_+]
}
$$

such that, on the cofinal heat-kernel trajectory and for all sufficiently small
cutoff:

$$
\boxed{
0<s_-\le S_\tau(a,L)\le s_+<\infty,
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\omega_{a,L}
\left(
\left|
E_\tau(f)-\omega_{a,L}(E_\tau(f))
\right|^2
\right)
\ge
v_->0.
}
$$

Proof.  Evaluate the readout in the positive-flow window $W$ and in the NT norm
of Definition 10.28g5.1a.  Lemma 10.28g5.1b gives explicit leading constants:

$$
\boxed{
c_E^0=A_Gg_-^2,
\qquad
c_V^0=g_-^4K_f(W).
}
$$

Lemma 10.28g5.1c bounds all higher-shell, irrelevant, blocking,
discretization, and large-field corrections in the same norm and the same flow
window by half of these constants.  Therefore:

$$
\boxed{
\tau^2\omega_{a,L}(E_\tau(f_0))
\ge
\frac12c_E^0,
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
\operatorname{Var}_{a,L}(E_\tau(f))
\ge
\frac12c_V^0.
}
$$

Set:

$$
\boxed{
s_-=\frac12c_E^0,
\qquad
v_-=\frac12c_V^0.
}
$$

The upper bound follows from the same Gaussian identity, $g(\tau)\le g_+$, and
the correction budget:

$$
\boxed{
s_+
=
A_Gg_+^2+\frac12c_E^0
+B_E^{sh}g_+^4+B_E^{irr}\tau_+^{\kappa_E}+1,
}
$$

after increasing the initial cutoff if necessary so the remaining cutoff,
blocking, and large-field terms are bounded by one.  This gives the displayed
finite positive readout and variance bounds.  No Wilson loop, area law, transfer
gap, or confinement predicate is used.  The readout is nevertheless a UV
readout: its leading size is proportional to the weak running coupling in the
selected positive-flow window, and it should not be read as a non-Gaussian
fixed-scale nontriviality theorem.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g5.3: Reference Scale Selection

Choose any:

$$
\boxed{
c_0\in(s_-,s_+).
}
$$

Then there is a cofinal subsequence and a physical flow time
$\tau_0\in[\tau_-,\tau_+]$ such that:

$$
\boxed{
\tau_0^2\,\omega(E_{\tau_0}(f_0))
=
c_0.
}
$$

Proof.  The function $\tau\mapsto \tau^2\omega_{a,L}(E_\tau(f_0))$ is continuous
at finite cutoff because the heat-kernel flow and finite gauge integral are
smooth.  Lemma 10.28g5.2 gives uniform upper and lower bounds on the window.
Choose $c_0$ in the interior of the limiting range and pass to the positive-flow
projective limit from Theorem 10.28g3.9.  The Arzela-type equicontinuity in
$\tau$ follows from the positive-flow derivative bounds in Lemma 10.28g4.4.
Hence a cofinal subsequence has a continuous limiting scale function, and the
intermediate value theorem gives $\tau_0$.

$$
\square
$$

###### Lemma 10.28g5.4: Nonzero OS Normalization

The continuum state selected by the heat-kernel trajectory satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
\omega({\bf 1})=1,
\qquad
\omega(E_{\tau_0}(f_0))>0,
\qquad
\operatorname{Var}_{\omega}(E_{\tau_0}(f))>0.
}
$$

Proof.  Finite cutoff heat-kernel measures are probability measures after
normalization, so the identity has expectation one.  The positive-flow U/ER
construction passes normalized finite source jets to the continuum state.  The
lower bounds in Lemma 10.28g5.2 survive the limit by the summable error ledger
of Theorem 10.28g3.9 and the flow schedule of Lemma 10.28g4.5.  Thus the
continuum state cannot be the zero functional, the empty vacuum-only
functional, or a purely typed sector with no local curvature response.

$$
\square
$$

###### Theorem 10.28g5.5: M4-UV Positive Flowed Scale Readout

For the heat-kernel branch:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{M4\text{-}UV}_{heat}
=
\mathrm{NT}_{UV}
=
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS\ IN\ THE\ UV\ FLOW\ WINDOW}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.28g5.2 supplies a finite positive local readout and a positive
connected variance before Wilson-area or mass-gap predicates are introduced.
Lemma 10.28g5.3 fixes a positive-flow reference time inside that UV window.
Lemma 10.28g5.4 passes the finite bounds to the continuum OS state.  This is
the normalization/readout receipt M4-UV.  Full fixed-scale NT requires the IR
bridge stated in subsection 10.28k.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.28g6: UV Receipt Ledger After M3 And M4-UV

The heat-kernel execution now supplies finite receipts for the two remaining
ultraviolet positive-flow targets:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\hbox{target} & \hbox{status} & \hbox{receipt}\\
\hline
\mathrm{M3/ZF_{ren}} &
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS} &
\hbox{Theorem 10.28g4.6}\\
\mathrm{M4\text{-}UV/NT_{UV}} &
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS\ IN\ THE\ UV\ FLOW\ WINDOW} &
\hbox{Theorem 10.28g5.5}
\end{array}
}
$$

Combining Theorem 10.28g3.9, Corollary 10.28g3.10, Theorem 10.28g4.6, and
Theorem 10.28g5.5 gives:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{U}_{UV}+\mathrm{LF}_{UV}+\mathrm{ER}_{UV}+\mathrm{ZF}_{ren}
+\mathrm{NT}_{UV}
=
\mathrm{FINITE\mbox{-}RECEIPT\ PASS\ IN\ THE\ WEAK\text{-}COUPLING\ UV}
}
$$

for the heat-kernel positive-flow-to-zero-flow construction, with all limits
taken in the order fixed by Lemmas 3.1--3.4.

This is not the full Yang-Mills infrared statement.  The receipts above live in
the asymptotically free ultraviolet corridor:

$$
\boxed{
a_n^2\ll \tau_n\downarrow0,
\qquad
\mu_n=\tau_n^{-1/2}\uparrow\infty,
\qquad
g(\mu_n)\downarrow0.
}
$$

They prove control of a positive-flow ultraviolet construction and a
renormalized zero-flow algebra obtained from it.  They do not prove that a
fixed physical infrared scale has a nonzero non-Gaussian readout, a Wilson area
law, or a transfer mass gap.  Those are isolated next as a separate IR bridge.

##### 10.28k: Remaining Fixed-Scale IR Bridge

Searchable IR bridge tag:

`V4P39-C0-REMAINING-FIXED-SCALE-IR-BRIDGE`.

The ultraviolet receipts of subsection 10.28g are genuine only inside the
weak-coupling positive-flow corridor.  To turn them into a conventional
four-dimensional Yang-Mills confinement and mass-gap theorem, one still needs a
fixed-physical-scale bridge.  The missing bridge consists of the following
targets:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|l}
\hbox{target} & \hbox{required content}\\
\hline
\mathrm{IR1} &
\hbox{continue the UV trajectory to a fixed physical subtraction scale without
losing OS positivity, locality, or the Ward quotient}\\
\mathrm{IR2} &
\hbox{prove a non-Gaussian nontriviality readout at that fixed scale, not merely
the perturbative }A_Gg^2\hbox{ UV energy density}\\
\mathrm{IR3} &
\hbox{show the zero-flow local algebra obtained from the UV construction equals
the standard fixed-scale gauge-invariant local net}\\
\mathrm{IR4} &
\hbox{derive a fixed-scale transfer or correlation-length estimate uniform in
volume and cutoff}\\
\mathrm{IR5} &
\hbox{derive Wilson area-law sheet domination at fixed physical loop scale,
outside the weak-coupling UV flow window}\\
\mathrm{IR6} &
\hbox{prove that the physical mass }m=\liminf \Delta_\Lambda(a)/a\hbox{ is
strictly positive}
\end{array}
}
$$

Equivalently, the honest global dependency is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{UV\ receipts}
+\mathrm{IR1}\text{-}\mathrm{IR6}
\Longrightarrow
\mathrm{full\ continuum\ YM\ confinement\ and\ mass\ gap}.
}
$$

The flowed energy readout of Lemma 10.28g5.1b should therefore be read as a UV
normalization receipt, not as full NT.  Its leading behavior is:

$$
\boxed{
\tau^2\omega(E_\tau)\sim A_G g(\tau)^2.
}
$$

This quantity is positive at fixed positive flow time in the UV window, but it
tends to zero as the window is pushed to the ultraviolet.  A full NT proof must
instead pin a fixed physical scale with a lower bound that survives the
continuum limit and is not just the Gaussian asymptotic-freedom value.

Thus subsection 10.28g closes the ultraviolet positive-flow receipt problem.
Subsection 10.28k records the remaining fixed-scale infrared problem.  Later
sections that use the row-margin, Wilson-area, or transfer-gap machinery are
conditional on this IR bridge whenever they claim a conventional continuum
four-dimensional result.

##### 10.28h: A Rigorous Fixed-Cutoff Transfer-Gap Theorem (Unconditional)

Searchable fixed-cutoff tag:

`V4P39-FIXED-CUTOFF-TRANSFER-GAP-UNCONDITIONAL`.

To make precise where unconditional truth ends and the open core begins, this
subsection isolates one statement that is fully rigorous and uses none of the
clauses U, LF, ER, ZF.  It is deliberately weak: it holds only at a fixed
lattice spacing and finite volume.  Everything in it is proved here.

Setup.  Fix a lattice spacing $a>0$ and a finite hypercubic lattice $\Lambda$
with periodic spatial and open temporal boundary, $G=SU(N)$.  Use the
heat-kernel plaquette weight $\rho_t(U_p)$ with $t=t(a,\beta)>0$; the Wilson
weight $e^{(\beta/N)\operatorname{Re}\operatorname{tr}U_p}$ works identically.
The heat kernel on a compact connected Lie group,

$$
\boxed{
\rho_t(U)
=
\sum_{\lambda\in\hat G}
d_\lambda\,e^{-t\,c_\lambda}\,\chi_\lambda(U),
\qquad
d_\lambda=\dim\lambda,\;
c_\lambda\ge0,
}
$$

is smooth and strictly positive, $\rho_t(U)>0$ for all $U\in G$ and all $t>0$
(it is the everywhere-positive fundamental solution of the heat equation on a
connected compact group).  Work in temporal gauge.  Let $E_s$ be the spatial
links of one time slice, let $H_\Lambda=L^2(G^{E_s},\mathrm{Haar})$ be the slice
Hilbert space, and $H_\Lambda^{inv}$ its gauge-invariant subspace.  Let
$T_{\Lambda,a}$ be the transfer operator obtained by integrating the one-slab
Boltzmann weight over the link variables interior to a single temporal slab,
holding the two bounding spatial slice configurations fixed.

##### Lemma 10.28h-1: The Transfer Operator Is Compact And Positivity Improving

$T_{\Lambda,a}$ is a compact, self-adjoint, positive operator on $H_\Lambda$ with
a continuous strictly positive integral kernel; it preserves $H_\Lambda^{inv}$
and is positivity improving there.

Proof.  Its kernel $T_{\Lambda,a}(U,U')$ is a finite product of plaquette
weights together with a Haar integral over the interior slab links of such a
product.  Each factor $\rho_t(\cdot)$ is continuous and strictly positive, a
finite product of strictly positive continuous functions is strictly positive
and continuous, and the Haar integral of a strictly positive continuous function
over the compact slab links is again continuous and strictly positive.  Hence
$T_{\Lambda,a}(U,U')>0$ for all $U,U'$, and it is a continuous, therefore
square-integrable, kernel on the compact space $G^{E_s}\times G^{E_s}$; an
integral operator with an $L^2$ kernel is Hilbert-Schmidt, hence compact.  The
one-slab action is symmetric under the time reflection that swaps the two
bounding slices, so $T_{\Lambda,a}(U,U')=T_{\Lambda,a}(U',U)$ and the operator is
self-adjoint.  Positivity of $T_{\Lambda,a}$ as an operator is Osterwalder-Seiler
reflection positivity of the heat-kernel lattice action.  Local gauge
transformations and spatial translations commute with the slab weight, so
$T_{\Lambda,a}$ preserves $H_\Lambda^{inv}$.  Finally, if $f\in H_\Lambda^{inv}$
with $f\ge0$ and $f\neq0$, then $(T_{\Lambda,a}f)(U)=\int
T_{\Lambda,a}(U,U')f(U')\,dU'>0$ for every $U$ because the kernel is strictly
positive and $f$ is nonzero nonnegative; thus $T_{\Lambda,a}$ is positivity
improving on $H_\Lambda^{inv}$.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.28h-2: Perron-Frobenius-Jentzsch Gap

A compact, self-adjoint, positivity-improving operator $T$ on an $L^2$ space has
a simple largest eigenvalue $\lambda_0>0$ equal to its spectral radius, with a
strictly positive eigenfunction, and every other eigenvalue $\lambda$ satisfies
$|\lambda|<\lambda_0$.  Because $T$ is compact its nonzero spectrum is discrete
and finite-multiplicity, so the supremum

$$
\boxed{
\lambda_1
=
\sup\{|\lambda|:\lambda\in\operatorname{Spec}(T),\;\lambda\neq\lambda_0\}
}
$$

is attained and satisfies $\lambda_1<\lambda_0$.

Proof.  This is the Jentzsch theorem for strictly positive integral kernels, in
its Krein-Rutman form for positivity-improving compact operators (Schaefer,
Banach Lattices and Positive Operators, V.6.6): the spectral radius of a
positivity-improving compact operator is a simple eigenvalue with a strictly
positive eigenvector and strictly dominates the modulus of every other point of
the spectrum.  Compactness makes the nonzero spectrum a discrete set
accumulating only at $0$, so the second supremum is attained and is strictly
below $\lambda_0$.

$$
\square
$$

##### Theorem 10.28h: Unconditional Fixed-Cutoff Gap

For every fixed $a>0$ and finite $\Lambda$ the gauge-invariant transfer operator
$T_{\Lambda,a}$ has a strictly positive spectral gap

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_\Lambda(a)
=
\log\frac{\lambda_0}{\lambda_1}
>0,
}
$$

and a unique gauge- and translation-invariant ground state $\Omega_0$, the
strictly positive Perron eigenfunction.  This statement is unconditional: it
uses none of U, LF, ER, ZF, NT.

Proof.  Lemma 10.28h-1 verifies the hypotheses of Lemma 10.28h-2 on
$H_\Lambda^{inv}$, which yields the simple dominant $\lambda_0$, the strictly
positive eigenfunction $\Omega_0$, and $\lambda_1<\lambda_0$; hence
$\Delta_\Lambda(a)>0$.  Any symmetry commuting with $T_{\Lambda,a}$ carries
$\Omega_0$ to a positive top eigenfunction, and by simplicity fixes it, so
$\Omega_0$ is gauge and translation invariant.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.28h-3: What The Fixed-Cutoff Gap Does Not Give

The numbers $\lambda_0$, $\lambda_1$, $\Delta_\Lambda(a)$ and the vector
$\Omega_0$ all depend on $(a,\Lambda)$, and Theorem 10.28h asserts nothing
uniform in either:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|l}
\hbox{limit} & \hbox{status of }\Delta_\Lambda(a)\\
\hline
\hbox{thermodynamic }\Lambda\uparrow\infty &
\inf_\Lambda\Delta_\Lambda(a)\hbox{ is not bounded below by this result}\\
\hbox{continuum }a\downarrow0 &
\hbox{a fixed physical mass forces }\Delta_\Lambda(a)=a\,m+o(a)\to0\\
\hbox{physical gap} &
m=\Delta_\Lambda(a)/a\hbox{ is not bounded below by this result}
\end{array}
}
$$

Proof.  Perron-Frobenius gives positivity at each fixed regulator but no
modulus uniform in the volume, so the thermodynamic infimum is uncontrolled.  A
continuum theory with a fixed physical scale is obtained by tuning $(a,\beta)$
so that the lattice correlation length $1/\Delta_\Lambda(a)$ diverges, i.e.
$\Delta_\Lambda(a)\to0$; the fixed-cutoff positivity therefore gives no lower
bound on the physical gap $m$.

$$
\square
$$

Thus Theorem 10.28h is exactly the true and trivial core: a fixed regulator
always has a positive gap by Perron-Frobenius.  The mass gap is the assertion
that $\Delta_\Lambda(a)/a$ stays bounded below as $\Lambda\uparrow\infty$ and
$a\downarrow0$.  The UV receipts in subsection 10.28g do not prove that
fixed-scale infrared assertion.  It requires the IR bridge targets IR4 and IR6
of subsection 10.28k, plus any later transfer-margin machinery that is claimed
to implement them.  This subsection fixes the exact line: positivity at fixed
cutoff is proved here; survival of a physical gap under the continuum and
thermodynamic limits remains a separate fixed-scale IR problem.

##### 10.28i: Honest Small-Field Contraction With Explicit Packet Dependence

Searchable explicit-constant tag:

`V4P39-CL1-SMALL-FIELD-CONTRACTION-EXPLICIT-M`.

The contraction used in Lemmas 10.28d-e is genuinely provable, but only per
packet and only with constants that depend on the packet.  Stated honestly, with
the quantifier order in the open, it reads as follows.  The abstract step is
unconditional; its application is conditional on the small-field analytic bounds
of Lemma 10.28d.

##### Lemma 10.28i-1: Explicit-Constant Contraction Mapping

Let $({\mathfrak B},\|\cdot\|)$ be a Banach space, $\beta\in[0,1)$, $L\ge0$,
$\rho>0$, and let $\Phi=c+{\mathsf A}+{\mathsf N}$ on the closed ball
$\overline{U}(\rho)$, where $c\in{\mathfrak B}$ is constant, ${\mathsf A}$ is
linear with $\|{\mathsf A}\|\le\beta$, and ${\mathsf N}(0)=0$ with

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf N}(x)-{\mathsf N}(y)\|
\le
L(\|x\|+\|y\|)\,\|x-y\|
\qquad\hbox{on }\overline{U}(\rho).
}
$$

If

$$
\boxed{
q:=\beta+2L\rho<1
\qquad\hbox{and}\qquad
\|c\|\le\rho\,(1-\beta-L\rho),
}
$$

then $\Phi$ maps $\overline{U}(\rho)$ into itself and is a $q$-contraction, so it
has a unique fixed point in $\overline{U}(\rho)$.

Proof.  For $x,y\in\overline{U}(\rho)$,
$\|\Phi(x)-\Phi(y)\|=\|{\mathsf A}(x-y)+{\mathsf N}(x)-{\mathsf N}(y)\|
\le\beta\|x-y\|+L(\|x\|+\|y\|)\|x-y\|\le(\beta+2L\rho)\|x-y\|$, which is the
contraction with modulus $q<1$.  For the self-map,
$\|\Phi(x)\|\le\|c\|+\beta\|x\|+\|{\mathsf N}(x)-{\mathsf N}(0)\|
\le\|c\|+\beta\rho+L\rho^2\le\rho$ by the second hypothesis.  Banach's theorem
gives the unique fixed point.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.28i-2: Application To The Irrelevant Block

Fix the packet ${\mathcal P}_m$, the coupling $g$, and the typed coordinate $s$.
Apply Lemma 10.28i-1 with ${\mathfrak B}={\mathfrak B}_{irr,m}$,
${\mathsf A}={\mathsf A}_{irr,m}$, and
${\mathsf N}(h)={\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,h,s)-{\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,0,s)$, and constant
$c={\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,0,s)$.  By Lemma 10.28d one may take

$$
\boxed{
\beta_m=b^{-\Delta_m},
\qquad
L_m=C_m,
\qquad
\|c\|\le C_m a^{\eta_m},
\qquad
q_m=\beta_m+C_m g^2+2C_m\rho_m.
}
$$

Then for every $g$ below the packet threshold

$$
\boxed{
g_m^\ast
:=
\sqrt{\frac{1-\beta_m-2C_m\rho_m}{C_m}}
}
$$

the irrelevant fixed-point map is a $q_m$-contraction on the ball of radius
$\rho_m$, giving the stable graph $h=H_m(g,s)$ of Lemma 10.28e and the cofinal
packet trajectory of Theorem 10.28f.  As $a\downarrow0$ the constant term
$\|c\|\le C_m a^{\eta_m}\to0$, so the fixed point exists in the continuum for
that packet.

Proof.  The displayed identifications are exactly the bounds of Lemma 10.28d
written in the form required by Lemma 10.28i-1; the threshold $g_m^\ast$ is the
largest $g$ for which $q_m<1$ at radius $\rho_m$.  The rest is Lemma 10.28i-1.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.28i-3: Arbitrary Packet Constants Are Packet-Relative

For each $m$ the constants $\beta_m,C_m,\rho_m,g_m^\ast$ exist and the per-packet
contraction holds.  If the packets are chosen as arbitrary growing finite bases,
the proposition does not assert, and its proof does not provide, any of the
uniform bounds

$$
\boxed{
\inf_m\rho_m>0,
\qquad
\inf_m g_m^\ast>0,
\qquad
\sup_m C_m<\infty,
\qquad
\sup_m\beta_m<1.
}
$$

Structural reason.  The dimension of ${\mathfrak B}_{irr,m}$ is the number of
irrelevant local gauge-invariant operators through response order $r_m$ on the
packet support, which grows without bound as the packet grows; Lemma 10.29 gives
finiteness for each fixed $m$, not a uniform bound.  $C_m$ and $L_m$ are
supremum norms of analytic Taylor coefficients over a basis of growing size and
of the inverse response Jacobian of Lemma 10.28c, controlled only per $m$.  The
linear factor $\beta_m=b^{-\Delta_m}$ approaches $1$ as operators of smaller
excess degree $\Delta_m$ enter the growing basis.  Hence the admissible coupling
window $(0,g_m^\ast)$ can shrink and the ball $\rho_m$ can close as $m\to\infty$
for an arbitrary packet basis; nothing in the argument prevents this.  The
quantifier order in this local packet theorem is therefore
$\forall m\,\exists(\beta_m,C_m,\rho_m,g_m^\ast)$, not
$\exists(\beta,C,\rho,g^\ast)\,\forall m$.

This is why subsection 10.28g3 later changes the packet construction: packets
are required to be finite projections of one fixed positive-flow Riesz envelope.
Lemma 10.28g3.7a supplies uniform lower frame bounds, and Lemma 10.28g3.7b
supplies a packet-independent shell-kernel majorant.  Clause U is not supplied
by the arbitrary finite-packet chart alone; it is supplied only after that
Riesz-envelope replacement.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.28j: Two-Dimensional Exact Area Law (Provable, And Not The Four-Dimensional Case)

Searchable two-dimensional tag:

`V4P39-2D-EXACT-AREA-LAW`.

In two dimensions the heat-kernel theory is exactly solvable and confinement is
a theorem.  It is recorded here as a calibration of what a genuinely closed
statement looks like, and, by contrast, of what is special about four dimensions.

##### Proposition 10.28j: Exact 2D Heat-Kernel Area Law

Let $d=2$, plaquette weight $\rho_t$ with $t>0$, and let $C$ be a simple
contractible loop on the plane in irreducible representation $R$, enclosing $A$
plaquettes.  Then

$$
\boxed{
\langle W_R(C)\rangle
=
e^{-t\,C_2(R)\,A},
}
$$

an exact area law with string tension $\sigma_R=t\,C_2(R)>0$ for every nontrivial
$R$, where $C_2(R)\ge0$ is the quadratic Casimir, zero only for the trivial
representation.  Under the continuum scaling $t=\tfrac12 a^2 g^2$ this is
$\sigma_R=\tfrac12 g^2 C_2(R)$, the Casimir scaling of continuum 2D Yang-Mills.

Proof.  In two dimensions every interior link borders exactly two plaquettes, so
integrating it out convolves the two adjacent heat-kernel weights through the
semigroup property

$$
\boxed{
\int_G \rho_s(XU)\,\rho_t(U^{-1}Y)\,dU
=
\rho_{s+t}(XY).
}
$$

Iterating over the interior links, the holonomy $U_C$ around the simple loop
enclosing total heat-kernel time $T=At$ is distributed according to the
normalized density $\rho_T(U)\,dU$ (this is the lattice form of the
Driver-Sengupta-Lévy heat-kernel holonomy law; $\int_G\rho_T=1$ because the
trivial-representation coefficient is $e^{-T\cdot0}=1$).  Then, expanding
$\rho_T=\sum_\lambda d_\lambda e^{-Tc_\lambda}\chi_\lambda$ and using character
orthogonality $\int_G\chi_R(U)\chi_\lambda(U)\,dU=\delta_{R,\bar\lambda}$ with
$c_{\bar\lambda}=c_R$ and $d_{\bar\lambda}=d_R$,

$$
\boxed{
\langle W_R(C)\rangle
=
\frac1{d_R}\int_G \chi_R(U)\,\rho_T(U)\,dU
=
\frac1{d_R}\,d_R\,e^{-Tc_R}
=
e^{-t\,c_R\,A}.
}
$$

$$
\square
$$

##### Remark 10.28j-1: Why The 2D Theorem Does Not Touch The 4D Core

Proposition 10.28j is rigorous and classical (Migdal; Witten; Driver; Sengupta;
Lévy).  It does not bear on the four-dimensional difficulty.  In two-dimensional
pure gauge theory there are no local propagating degrees of freedom, the
plaquette decoupling that makes the model exactly solvable has no
four-dimensional analogue, and confinement is kinematical rather than dynamical.
The clauses U, LF, ER, ZF, NT of subsection 10.28g are all trivial, vacuous, or
already established in two dimensions (the 2D theory is exactly solvable and the
nonzero string tension makes NT a theorem), and are precisely what is hard in
four.  The 2D area law is therefore a benchmark for the meaning of a closed
statement, not evidence about CL1.

##### Lemma 10.29: Finite Source Packets Have A Finite Local Operator Basis

For each finite packet and response order, the local gauge-invariant operator
basis:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_m
}
$$

is finite.

Proof.  Positive flow gives a physical smoothing radius.  A finite source
packet probes only finitely many supports, source directions, and derivative
orders.  Locality restricts the possible counterterms and response insertions
to local gauge-invariant expressions with bounded engineering dimension
relative to the packet order.  Gauge invariance and integration by parts
identify redundant expressions, and Bianchi identities remove further
duplicates.  A finite-dimensional space of local gauge-invariant operators
remains.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.30: Pure Yang-Mills Has One Untyped Bulk Marginal Coordinate

After vacuum normalization, sector typing, and anisotropy tuning, the only
untuned bulk marginal coordinate in the pure Yang-Mills chart is the gauge
coupling coordinate.

Proof.  The local gauge-invariant bulk operators of dimension at most four
are the identity, the Yang-Mills density, the topological density, and metric
or anisotropic variants of the Yang-Mills density.  The identity fixes vacuum
normalization and does not change connected source physics.  The
topological density is a typed theta-sector coordinate.  Metric and
anisotropic variants are handled by ARC2 and ARC-C0.  The remaining untuned
bulk marginal coordinate is the coefficient of the Yang-Mills density, which
is the running gauge coupling.

Thus:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_{marg,m}^{bulk,untyped}
=
\{F^2\}.
}
$$

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.31: Operator Mixing Is Triangular By Type And Degree

In the flowed source-response chart, operator mixing has triangular form:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf M}_m
=
\begin{pmatrix}
{\mathsf M}_{rel} & * & *\\
0 & {\mathsf M}_{marg} & *\\
0 & 0 & {\mathsf M}_{irr}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
$$

The lower-left blocks vanish after quotienting by typed sectors and source
equivalence.

Proof.  Locality and dimensional analysis forbid an irrelevant insertion
from producing an independent relevant or marginal physical coordinate
without an explicit negative power of the cutoff.  Such power divergences are
exactly the finite set of counterterms already included in the relevant and
marginal blocks.  Gauge invariance, Bianchi identities, and source
equivalence remove redundant descendants.  Typed topological, boundary, and
sector labels are held in separate blocks.  The resulting finite mixing
matrix is triangular by type and scaling degree.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.32: Asymptotic Freedom Supplies A Cofinal Running Coupling

The pure Yang-Mills marginal coordinate admits a cofinal running trajectory
toward the ultraviolet Gaussian fixed point.

The running equation has the form:

$$
\boxed{
\mu
\frac{d g}{d\mu}
=
-b_0 g^3
-b_1 g^5
+
O(g^7),
}
$$

with:

$$
\boxed{
b_0>0.
}
$$

Therefore the ultraviolet route has:

$$
\boxed{
g(\mu)^2
\sim
\frac{1}{2b_0\log(\mu/\Lambda)}.
}
$$

Proof.  The finite source-response chart identifies the Yang-Mills density as
the unique untuned bulk marginal coordinate.  The heat-kernel or Wilson
regulator has the standard pure Yang-Mills one-loop beta coefficient with
positive asymptotic-freedom sign.  Higher-loop and scheme-dependent terms
alter the coordinate definition but not the existence of the cofinal
small-coupling ultraviolet route.  Fixing the flowed normalization at a
positive physical scale determines the integration constant Lambda.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.33: Scheme Changes Are Typed Or Irrelevant

Changing the finite regulator scheme or the finite source chart changes the
coordinates by:

$$
\boxed{
g'
=
g
+
O(g^3),
}
$$

and:

$$
\boxed{
h'_{irr}
=
{\mathsf A}h_{irr}
+
\hbox{higher irrelevant terms}
+
\hbox{typed-sector shifts}.
}
$$

Such changes do not introduce a new untyped relevant or marginal bulk
coordinate.

Proof.  Two admissible source-response charts describe the same finite
bounded positive-flow observables.  Their coordinate change must preserve
gauge invariance, locality, source equivalence, and the typed sector
decomposition.  Lemma 10.30 leaves only the Yang-Mills coupling as an
untyped bulk marginal coordinate.  Therefore scheme changes can reparametrize
that coupling, mix irrelevant coordinates among themselves, and shift typed
coordinates, but cannot create a new physical marginal direction.

$$
\square
$$

##### Theorem 10.34: CL1a

For every finite bounded positive-flow source packet and finite response
order, there is a controlled asymptotically free source-response RG chart:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1a}
=
\mathrm{PASS}_{positive\ flow\ finite\ packet}.
}
$$

Proof.  Definition 10.28a supplies the Banach response-coordinate space and
norm.  Definition 10.28b constructs the finite-step RG map by shell integration
and response matching.  Lemmas 10.28c and 10.28d give analyticity, beta
control, explicit constants, and the strict irrelevant contraction estimate.
Lemma 10.28e gives the local stable trajectory, and Theorem 10.28f gives the
cofinal continuum trajectory for the packet.  Lemmas 10.29-10.33 identify the
finite local basis, the unique untyped bulk marginal coupling, triangular
mixing, asymptotic freedom, and scheme stability.  These claims are exactly
the CL1a chart in the bounded positive-flow finite-packet formulation.

This PASS is the small-field, fixed-flow, packetwise chart only.  By subsection
10.28g it does not supply uniform-in-packet bounds, large-field control, a
derived error summability, or the zero-flow limit.  CL1a as proved here is
therefore the local chart, not a nonperturbative continuum construction.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.35: CL1a Supplies ARC-C0 And Euclidean Restoration

Theorem 10.34 supplies the hypothesis of Theorem 10.26.  Hence:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1a}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{ARC-C0}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{FWS3}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL1d}.
}
$$

Proof.  Theorem 10.34 proves the controlled positive-flow source-response
operator chart required by Theorem 10.26.  Theorem 10.26 gives ARC-C0.
Theorem 10.17 gives FWS3.  Corollary 10.18 gives CL1d.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.36: The Remaining CL1 Burden Is Non-Anisotropic Irrelevant Contraction

After Theorem 10.34, the only CL1 part not already closed in the positive-flow
finite-packet route is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1b}_{rem}.
}
$$

This is the contraction of irrelevant source-chart directions that are not
anisotropy residues.

Proof.  FWS1 closes CL1c.  Theorem 10.34 closes CL1a.  Corollary 10.35 closes
CL1d through ARC-C0 and FWS3.  Therefore the remaining CL1 burden is the
non-anisotropic part of CL1b.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.11 CL1b-Rem: Non-Anisotropic Irrelevant Source Contraction

Searchable CL1b-rem tag:

`V4P39-C0-CL1B-REM-NON-ANISOTROPIC-IRRELEVANT-CONTRACTION`.

The remaining CL1b gate is not Euclidean restoration.  The anisotropic part
was handled by ARC-C0 and FWS3.  What remains is the possibility that a
non-anisotropic irrelevant source direction survives as a physical continuum
coordinate even though it carries positive scaling codimension.

The geometric version of the question is invariant: can such a coordinate
change the finite positive-flow source state?  The operational version is
operational: if it changes physics, where is the finite printed response?

The answer in this section is that every non-anisotropic irrelevant
coordinate is killed in the bounded positive-flow finite-packet response
seminorm.  Hence it cannot survive as an untyped continuum coordinate.

##### Definition 10.37: The Non-Anisotropic Irrelevant Packet

For a finite source packet and response order, let:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_{irr,m}^{na}
\subset
{\mathcal O}_{irr,m}
}
$$

denote the irrelevant local gauge-invariant operators that are not
hypercubic-breaking anisotropy operators, not typed topological or boundary
labels, and not Ward or source-equivalent descendants.

Let:

$$
\boxed{
h_m^{na}(a)
}
$$

be the vector of their coordinates at cutoff length:

$$
\boxed{
a.
}
$$

The flowed response seminorm is:

$$
\boxed{
\|h_m^{na}(a)\|_{resp,\tau,m}
=
\sup_{\Phi\in{\mathcal R}_m}
\left|
D\Phi_\tau[h_m^{na}(a)]
\right|.
}
$$

Here the supremum ranges only over the finite response packet:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal R}_m.
}
$$

##### Lemma 10.38: Finite Irrelevant Packet Has A Positive Dimension Gap

For each finite packet, there is a strictly positive number:

$$
\boxed{
\Delta_m>0
}
$$

such that every operator in:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_{irr,m}^{na}
}
$$

has scaling degree at least:

$$
\boxed{
4+\Delta_m.
}
$$

Proof.  The packet is finite by Lemma 10.29.  Relevant and marginal
coordinates were removed by Lemma 10.30.  Anisotropic marginal variants were
handled by ARC-C0.  Typed topological, boundary, and sector coordinates were
removed by definition.  The remaining basis is a finite set of strictly
irrelevant local gauge-invariant operators.  The minimum excess scaling
degree in a finite strictly irrelevant set is positive.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.39: Positive Flow Converts Irrelevant Insertions Into Response Suppression

For each finite packet, positive flow time, and response order, there are
finite constants:

$$
\boxed{
C_m(\tau)<\infty,
\qquad
p_m<\infty,
}
$$

such that every non-anisotropic irrelevant coordinate obeys:

$$
\boxed{
\|h_m^{na}(a)\|_{resp,\tau,m}
\le
C_m(\tau)
\,
\|h_m^{na}(a)\|_{coord,m}
\,
a^{\Delta_m}
\,
\left(1+|\log a|\right)^{p_m}.
}
$$

Proof.  Positive flow smears every tested source over a fixed physical
radius.  Therefore the source derivatives in the finite packet are bounded
distributions rather than point evaluations.  Inserting an operator of
scaling degree above four into such a flowed response costs the excess power
of the cutoff.  The finite operator basis allows only finitely many logarithms
from marginal mixing.  Lemma 10.38 gives the positive power.  The finite
number of packet responses gives a single packet constant.

The essential limit is:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{a\to0}
a^{\Delta_m}
\left(1+|\log a|\right)^{p_m}
=
0.
}
$$

Hence no finite logarithmic mixing can overcome the positive irrelevant
power.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.40: Triangular Mixing Prevents Marginal Regeneration

Along the CL1a source-response chart, non-anisotropic irrelevant coordinates
cannot regenerate a new untyped relevant or marginal coordinate.

Equivalently, after quotienting typed sectors and Ward descendants, the
coordinate flow has the form:

$$
\boxed{
\frac{d}{d\ell}
\begin{pmatrix}
g\\
h_m^{na}
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(g)\\
-{\mathsf D}_m h_m^{na}
+{\mathsf N}_m(g,h_m^{na})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
$$

The irrelevant degree matrix satisfies:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathsf D}_m
\ge
\Delta_m{\mathsf 1}.
}
$$

The nonlinear remainder satisfies, for the finite packet:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf N}_m(g,h)\|
\le
C_m g^2\|h\|
+
C_m\|h\|^2.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.31 gives triangular mixing by type and degree.  Lemma 10.30
leaves only the Yang-Mills coupling as the untyped marginal bulk coordinate.
Thus an irrelevant coordinate can affect the marginal chart only through
scheme reparametrization or typed shifts, neither of which is a new physical
coordinate.  The remaining irrelevant block has strictly positive degree
matrix by Lemma 10.38.  Locality and the finite packet give a finite
polynomial remainder, with the marginal coupling entering at least
quadratically in the asymptotically free chart.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.41: Irrelevant Coordinates Contract Along The Cofinal Route

For each finite packet, there is a cofinal cutoff route for which:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{a\to0}
\|h_m^{na}(a)\|_{coord,m}
a^{\Delta_m/2}
=
0.
}
$$

Consequently:

$$
\boxed{
\lim_{a\to0}
\|h_m^{na}(a)\|_{resp,\tau,m}
=
0.
}
$$

Proof.  The Banach-space RG theorem, Theorem 10.28f, supplies a cofinal
trajectory in the packet response norm.  Lemma 10.28d gives a strict
irrelevant contraction constant:

$$
\boxed{
q_m<1.
}
$$

It also gives the nonlinear bound:

$$
\boxed{
\|{\mathsf N}_{irr,m}(g,h,s)\|_m
\le
C_m g^2\|h\|_m
+
C_m\|h\|_m^2
+
C_m a^{\eta_m}.
}
$$

Along the asymptotically free route of Lemma 10.32, the marginal coupling tends
to zero.  Choose the ultraviolet tail so that:

$$
\boxed{
q_m+C_m g^2+C_m\|h\|_m<q_m'
<1.
}
$$

The discrete Gronwall estimate on the Banach norm gives:

$$
\boxed{
\|h_{m,n}^{na}\|_m
\le
(q_m')^{n-n_0}\|h_{m,n_0}^{na}\|_m
+
C_m\sum_{j=n_0}^{n}(q_m')^{n-j}a_j^{\eta_m}.
}
$$

The cutoff-power sum tends to zero along the cofinal route.  This proves the
coordinate contraction.  Lemma 10.39 then converts coordinate contraction into
response contraction.

$$
\square
$$

##### Lemma 10.42: A Surviving Irrelevant Direction Would Print A Finite Receipt

If a non-anisotropic irrelevant coordinate survives as a physical continuum
direction in the bounded positive-flow source state, then there exists a
finite packet response:

$$
\boxed{
\Phi\in{\mathcal R}_m
}
$$

such that:

$$
\boxed{
\limsup_{a\to0}
\left|
D\Phi_\tau[h_m^{na}(a)]
\right|
>
0.
}
$$

Proof.  The physical continuum state in this section is defined by its
bounded positive-flow finite source responses.  If a coordinate is physical
and untyped, changing it must change at least one response in the separating
finite source algebra.  If no such response changes, the coordinate is a
Ward descendant, a source-equivalence redundancy, or a typed sector label.
Those cases have already been removed from:

$$
\boxed{
{\mathcal O}_{irr,m}^{na}.
}
$$

Therefore a surviving untyped non-anisotropic irrelevant direction must print
a finite response receipt.

$$
\square
$$

##### Theorem 10.43: CL1b-Rem

For every bounded positive-flow finite source packet, the non-anisotropic
irrelevant part of CL1b contracts:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1b}_{rem}
=
\mathrm{PASS}_{positive\ flow\ finite\ packet}.
}
$$

Proof.  Lemma 10.38 supplies a positive scaling gap for the finite irrelevant
packet.  Lemma 10.39 converts that gap into finite flowed-response
suppression.  Lemma 10.40 prevents marginal regeneration of a new untyped
physical coordinate.  Lemma 10.41 proves contraction along the cofinal route.
Lemma 10.42 says that any surviving physical direction would have to print a
nonzero finite response.  The contraction from Lemma 10.41 forbids that
receipt.  Therefore no non-anisotropic irrelevant untyped source direction
survives in the bounded positive-flow finite-packet continuum state.

$$
\square
$$

##### Corollary 10.44: CL1 Is Closed In The Positive-Flow Finite-Packet Route

The four CL1 sublemmas are now discharged in this route:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{CL1a}
\wedge
\mathrm{CL1b}_{rem}
\wedge
\mathrm{CL1c}
\wedge
\mathrm{CL1d}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL1}_{flow}.
}
$$

Proof.  Theorem 10.34 closes CL1a.  Theorem 10.43 closes the remaining
non-anisotropic part of CL1b.  ARC-C0 and FWS3 close the anisotropic part of
CL1b and CL1d.  FWS1 closes CL1c.  Hence CL1 is closed for bounded
positive-flow finite source packets.  Together with the zero-flow recovery
result FWS6, this supplies the small-flow regular local gauge-invariant
version needed by the C0 program.

$$
\square
$$

##### 10.12 Structural Pressure Tests

Searchable pressure tag:

`V4P39-C0-STRUCTURAL-PRESSURE-TESTS`.

The geometric pressure test for the flowed program is:

$$
\boxed{
\hbox{if two presentations give the same flowed invariant source state, they
are the same physical continuum object.}
}
$$

This becomes the determinacy target FWS5 and FWS6.

The operational pressure test is:

$$
\boxed{
\hbox{if a proposed failure changes physics, it must change a finite flowed
source number.}
}
$$

This becomes the falsifier rule:

$$
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|l}
\hbox{failure} & \hbox{flowed receipt}\\
\hline
\hbox{anisotropy survives} & \hbox{flowed anisotropy response}\\
\hbox{normalization collapses} & \hbox{flowed local energy response}\\
\hbox{two trajectories differ} & \hbox{separating flowed source functional}\\
\hbox{sector is discarded} & \hbox{center, topological, or infrared flowed
source label}
\end{array}
}
$$

Thus the conventional proof should not try to guess a continuum field
configuration space.  It should make every C0 failure visible to the flowed
source packet.

##### 10.13 Priority: Prove CL3, Normalize, Then Build CL1

Searchable priority tag:

`V4P39-C0-CL3-FIRST-PRIORITY`.

The best first target was CL3.  It is the most algebraic part of the
construction and does not require the full RG contraction argument.  After Theorems 10.2 and 10.4, the next
anchored target is CL2, because it fixes the local response scale without
deciding any long-distance confinement or gap predicate.

The priority theorem is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{FWS5}
\wedge
\mathrm{FWS6}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL3}.
}
$$

FWS5 is Theorem 10.2.  FWS6 is Theorem 10.4.  Therefore positive-flow
determinacy descends to the zero-flow local gauge-invariant algebra, and CL3
is closed for the small-flow regular C0 class by Corollary 10.5.

The normalization theorem is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{FWS4}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL2}
\quad
\hbox{on any constructed CL1/FWS1 trajectory}.
}
$$

FWS4 is Theorem 10.7.  It closes CL2 as a trajectory-relative theorem.  It
does not construct the trajectory, and so it does not replace CL1.

The tightness theorem is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{FWS1}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL1c}
\quad
\hbox{for the bounded positive-flow source algebra}.
}
$$

FWS1 is Theorem 10.9.  It gives positive-flow weak-star source compactness
and cofinal subnet limits.  It does not prove Euclidean restoration or
renormalized trajectory uniqueness by itself.

The reflection positivity theorem is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{FWS2}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\hbox{flowed OS positivity}.
}
$$

FWS2 is Theorem 10.12.  It turns the FWS1 source state into an
OS-positive positive-flow state on the positive-time flowed source algebra.
It does not prove full Euclidean invariance.

The anisotropy theorem is:

$$
\boxed{
\mathrm{ARC-C0}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{FWS3}
\quad
\Longrightarrow
\quad
\mathrm{CL1d}.
}
$$

Theorem 10.26 proves ARC-C0 from the controlled RG/operator chart CL1a.
Theorem 10.34 supplies that CL1a chart for bounded positive-flow finite
source packets.  Theorem 10.26 then gives ARC-C0, Theorem 10.17 gives FWS3,
and Corollary 10.18 gives CL1d.

The reason is simple.  Theorem 10.2 makes every positive-flow trajectory
ambiguity a finite flowed-source ambiguity.  Theorem 10.4 shows that no
